Answering the Objection: Human Power and Divine Origination
Nasafi answers the objection that rejecting human creation nullifies human power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi defends the reality of human power (qudra) and human acts without requiring humans to originate (ikhtira') their own acts, thereby reconciling divine creation with human acquisition (kasb).

Core Idea
Human power attaches to acts without originating them, making them truly our acts through acquisition.

This passage directly answers a critical objection in the debate on human free will: if humans do not create their own acts, doesn't that make their power (qudra) pointless? Nasafi responds by recalling earlier proofs and then clarifying that divine origination does not nullify human agency. Instead, human power attaches to acts through the mode of acquisition (kasb), not creation (ikhtira'). This lesson unpacks that response and the threefold distinction Nasafi makes.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Nasafi's initial response
Start by reading the first part of the passage where the objectors claim human power becomes null. Notice that Nasafi appeals to already-established proofs and insists on 'submitting to the proof.'
The phrase 'established by the sum of the two proofs' refers to proofs for divine creation and human acquisition.
2
Understand the three categories of divine origination
Nasafi distinguishes three cases: what Allah originates in beings without choice, what He originates in beings with choice but without power attaching, and what He originates with the slave's choice and power. Trace each case carefully.
This shows that the human act is a special case: the slave's choice and power affect the attribution of the act.
3
Grasp how the slave's act is affirmed
Focus on the third case: when Allah originates an act by the slave's choice and the slave has power over it, the power's effect is that the act becomes the slave's act. This is the doctrine of kasb (acquisition).
Nasafi says that without the slave's choice and intention of acquisition, Allah would not create it as an act for him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لو استحال ذلك لبطل تعلق قدرة العبد بشيء وتعطلت قدرته. قلنا : وقد أقمنا الدليل على أن العبد له فعل هو مقدوره فيجب الانقياد للدليل وإثبات الفعل للعبد وإن لم يخترعه، وثبت بمجموع الدليلين جواز تعلق القدرة لا بجهة الاختراع. ثم نقول : ما يخترعه الله تعالى فيما لا اختيار له لا يكون فعلاً له فيكون مخلوق الله تعالى ومفعوله لا فعله ولا فعل غيره عندنا، وعند الأشعرية والنجارية يكون فعل الله تعالى لأنه مفعوله والفعل والمفعول واحد، وما يخترعه فيمن له الاختيار، إن كان ذلك الشيء مما لا يتعلق به قدرة المحل فهو أيضا ليس بفعل للعبد بل العبد محله لا غير، وما يخترعه فيه باختيار العبد ذلك وله عليه قدرة فأثر تعلق قدرته به كونه فعلاً، فيكون الله تعالى مخترعا فعل العبد باختياره لولا اختيار العبد وقصده اكتسابه لما خلقه الله تعالى فعلا له فأثر قدرته كون ذلك المخترع فعلاً له، هذا عن جهة التبرع مع أنا لا حاجة بنا إلى بيان ذلك على ما بينا من أن وجوب اتباع الدليلين يقتضي ما قلنا، والله الموفق.
If they say: If that is impossible, then the attachment of the slave's power to anything would be nullified and his power would become inoperative. We say: We have already established the proof that the slave has an act which is his power, so it is necessary to submit to the proof and affirm the act for the slave even if he does not originate it. And it is established by the sum of the two proofs that it is permissible for power to attach without the mode of origination. Then we say: What Allah originates in that which has no choice is not an act for it; rather it is the creature of Allah and His effect, not His act nor the act of another according to us. According to the Ash'aris and the Najjariyya, it is the act of Allah because it is His effect, and the act and the effect are one. And what He originates in one who has choice, if that thing is such that the power of the locus does not attach to it, then it is also not an act of the slave; rather the slave is merely its locus, nothing more. And what He originates in it by the slave's choice and he has power over it, then the effect of the attachment of his power to it is its being an act. Thus Allah originates the slave's act by his choice; were it not for the slave's choice and his intention of acquisition, Allah would not have created it as an act for him. So the effect of his power is that that originated thing is an act for him. This is from the perspective of dispensing with need, although we have no need to explain that, given that what we have said is that the obligation to follow the two proofs necessitates what we have said. And Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 902

Commentary
This passage is an answer to an objection. The objectors argue that if it is impossible for the slave to originate (ikhtira') his acts, then the slave's power (qudra) would be nullified and his capability would become inoperative. Nasafi replies by recalling that earlier proofs have already established that the slave has an act that is his power (maqdur), so one must submit to the proof and affirm an act for the slave even though he does not originate it. The combination of two proofs (one for divine creation of acts and one for human acquisition) shows that power can attach without the mode of origination. He then distinguishes: what Allah originates in what has no choice (like inanimate objects) is not an act for that object; it is simply Allah's creation and effect. For Ash'aris and Najjariyya, it is Allah's act because effect and act are identical. What Allah originates in a being that has choice, if that being's power does not attach to it, then it is not an act of that being; the being is merely the locus. But if it is originated with the slave's choice and the slave has power over it, then the effect of the power's attachment is that it becomes an act of the slave. Thus Allah originates the slave's act by the slave's choice; without the slave's choice and intention of acquisition, Allah would not have created it as an act for him. Nasafi concludes that this explanation is not strictly necessary because the obligation to follow the proofs already yields the conclusion.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if the slave does not create his own act, then his power (qudra) is nullified and he cannot be held responsible.
Correction: Nasafi shows that power attaches to the act through acquisition (kasb), not creation (ikhtira'). The slave's choice and intention are necessary for the act to be attributed to him, so power remains meaningful.

D) The power is nullified.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi preserves human responsibility by showing that power attaches to acts through acquisition, not origination, so divine creation of acts does not negate human agency.

?

?

Refutation of the Knowledge Analogy for Divine Power
Nasafi rejects the analogy between divine knowledge and power regarding information.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the analogy between divine knowledge and power fails, and how the Maturidi doctrine of kasb distinguishes two modes of power attachment.

Core Idea
Power has two modes; knowledge has one—that's why the analogy fails.

In this passage, Nasafi engages with an objection that attempts to draw an analogy between God's knowledge and His power. The objectors argue that just as God's information must match His knowledge, so His empowerment must match His power's mode (origination). Nasafi dismantles this by revealing a fundamental asymmetry: knowledge attaches to its object in only one way, but power attaches in two. This distinction is central to the Maturidi understanding of human agency and the concept of kasb.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get the full argument.
The passage begins with an objection, then the reply, then a further refutation.
2
Identify the objection from the analogy
Find where the objectors argue that divine empowerment must match divine power's mode, just as divine information must match divine knowledge.
They claim that if God empowers us differently, it is not true empowerment.
3
Understand Nasafi's two-mode distinction for power
Nasafi replies that power attaches to the power (maqdur) in two modes: origination (ikhtira') and acquisition (iktisab). Allah is distinguished by origination, humans by acquisition.
This is unlike knowledge, which attaches in only one mode.
4
Contrast with the single mode of knowledge
Notice that Nasafi asserts knowledge attaches only as the object actually is; any other attachment would be ignorance. This is why the analogy breaks down.
The proof for knowledge shows no duality.
5
Reflect on the implications for kasb
Consider how this distinction supports the Maturidi doctrine that human acts are acquired (kasb) while God is the true originator.
The thing remains originated by God's power even when our power attaches by acquisition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة والرد عليها] وهكذا الجواب عن قولهم إن الله تعالى إذا علم شيئا ثم أعلمنا إنما يكون ما يثبت علمه بذلك الشيء، أي لو أعلمنا على الوجه الذي علم هو به، فأما إذا أعلمنا لا على ذلك الوجه لا يكون ذلك إعلاماً بل يكون ذلك تجهيلاً، فإنه تعالى إذا علم شيئًا أسود أو أبيض أو طويلاً أو عريضا فإن أعلمنا على ذلك الوجه بأن أعلمنا أنه أسود أو أبيض وعلى ما كان كان ما ثبت لنا علمًا وإن علم هو شيئًا أسود وأعلمنا أبيض فما ثبت لنا لا يكون علمًا بل يكون جهلاً، فكذا هذا في قدرته وإقداره إيانا، فإذا قدر على شيء وأقدرنا عليه ينبغي أن يقدرنا على ذلك الوجه ولو أقدرنا لا على ذلك الوجه لا يكون ذلك إقدار ثم إنه تعالى يقدر اختراع الأشياء فإذا أقدرنا يقدرنا على جهة الاختراع، ولو لم يقدرنا على تلك الجهة لا يكون ذلك إقدارا. لما مر فإنا نجيب عن هذا الكلام فنقول : بل يكون ذلك إقدارًا وإن لم يقدرنا على الاختراع أن للعبد فعلاً يتعلق به قدرته، وأن ثبوت الاختراع من جهته مستحيل، وثبت بمجموع الدليلين أن المقدور نوعان: مخترع ومكتسب، والقدرة تتعلق بالمقدور بجهتين جهة اختراع وجهة اكتساب اختص الله تعالى بأحدهما واختص المحدث بالآخر، بخلاف العلم فإن هناك لم يثبت دليل يوجب أن يعلق العلم بالمعلوم بجهتين بل قام الدليل أن تعلقه بالمعلوم بجهة واحدة وهو أن يتعلق به على ما هو به، إذ لو تعلق به لا على هذه الجهة لكان جهلاً لا علمًا. ثم نشتغل بإبطال ذلك فنقول : قياس العلم يقتضي ما قلنا لو عقلتم، فإن علمنا يتعلق بما هو معلوم الله تعالى وليس من ضرورة تعلق علمنا به زوال علم الباري جل وعلا بل بقي علمه متعلقا به، وبقي المعلوم معلومًا له وإن صار معلومًا لنا، فكذا قدرتنا ينبغي أن تتعلق بما هو مقدور الله تعالى وعند تعلق قدرتنا به يبقى مقدورًا له، وكانت قدرته للاختراع فيبقى كذلك وكون الشيء مخترعًا بقدرتين
An objection and its reply: Likewise the answer to their saying: If Allah knows a thing then informs us, what He informs us of must be what He knows of that thing, i.e., if He informed us in the manner in which He knows it. But if He informs us not in that manner, that is not information but rather misguidance. For if He knows a thing to be black or white or long or wide, and He informs us in that manner such that He informs us that it is black or white and as it is, then what we establish is knowledge. But if He knows a thing to be black and informs us it is white, then what we establish is not knowledge but ignorance. So likewise in His power and His enabling us: if He has power over a thing and enables us over it, He ought to enable us in that manner; and if He enables us not in that manner, that is not enabling. Then He has power over originating things, so if He enables us, He should enable us in the mode of origination; and if He did not enable us in that mode, that would not be enabling. As for what has passed, we answer this statement and say: Rather it is enabling even if He does not enable us to originate, because the slave has an act to which his power attaches, and that origination from his side is impossible. And it is established by the sum of the two proofs that the power (maqdur) is of two types: originated (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). And power attaches to the power (maqdur) in two modes: the mode of origination and the mode of acquisition. Allah is distinguished by one of them, and the contingent being is distinguished by the other. Unlike knowledge, for there no proof has been established necessitating that knowledge attaches to the known in two modes; rather the proof has established that its attachment to the known is in one mode, namely that it attaches to it as it is, for if it attached to it not in this mode, it would be ignorance, not knowledge. Then we engage in refuting that by saying: The analogy of knowledge necessitates what we say, if you understood. For our knowledge attaches to what is known by Allah, and it is not necessary that our knowledge's attachment to it removes the knowledge of the Exalted and Majestic; rather His knowledge remains attached to it, and the known remains known to Him even if it becomes known to us. Likewise, our power should attach to what is the power of Allah, and upon the attachment of our power to it, it remains His power. And His power is for origination, so it remains so, and the thing is originated by two powers.
Source pages p. 902

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection based on an analogy with divine knowledge. The objectors argue: when God knows something and informs us, the information must match His knowledge; otherwise it is ignorance, not knowledge. They apply this to power: if God has power over something and empowers us, He should empower us in the same mode (i.e., origination). If He does not, it is not true empowerment. Nasafi replies by reiterating the two-fold division of the power (maqdur): originated (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). Power attaches in two modes: origination and acquisition. Allah is distinguished by origination, the contingent being by acquisition. This is unlike knowledge, which attaches in only one mode — as the object actually is. The proof for knowledge shows no duality of attachment. Then Nasafi goes further to refute the analogy by pointing out that our knowledge attaches to what Allah knows without removing Allah's knowledge; similarly our power should attach to what Allah has power over without removing His power. Since His power is for origination, the thing remains originated by His power, and our power attaches by acquisition, so the thing is originated by two powers (Allah's and the slave's by acquisition). This is the Maturidi doctrine of kasb.

Key Terms
علم
إعلام
قدرة
إقدار
اختراع
اكتساب
مقدور
معلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The mode of divine empowerment must be identical to the mode of divine power.
Correction: Nasafi shows that power attaches in two modes (origination and acquisition), so God can empower humans in the mode of acquisition without sharing His mode of origination.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does the analogy between divine knowledge and divine power fail in the objection?
A) Because knowledge attaches in one mode, but power attaches in two modes.
B) Because knowledge is eternal, while power is temporal.
C) Because knowledge is active, while power is passive.
D) Because the objectors misunderstood the nature of divine knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Power attaches to the power in two modes (origination and acquisition), whereas knowledge attaches in only one mode—this is why the analogy fails and the Maturidi doctrine of kasb stands.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own actions, do you truly believe that they are simultaneously your acquisition (kasb) and Allah's origination? How does this affect the way you approach your daily choices, especially when you are tempted to take credit for your successes or blame failures on external factors?
?
This lesson shows that God's power operates differently than His knowledge. Are there areas in your life where you mistakenly assume that God must act in a certain way based on a false analogy? Can you identify a specific expectation you hold of God that might be based on a misunderstanding of His attributes?
?
Nasafi's refutation preserves both divine omnipotence and human responsibility. Examine your own heart: Do you tend to lean more towards fatalism (denying your own responsibility) or towards self-reliance (forgetting that all power originates from Allah)? What concrete step can you take today to balance both?

Human Power as Acquisition, Not Origination
Nasafi presents and replies to the objection that human power must be origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi distinction between divine origination (ikhtira') and human acquisition (kasb), and why human power cannot be creative like God's.

Core Idea
Human power is acquisition, not creation; divine power alone originates.

Imam Nasafi begins by presenting an objection based on analogy with divine knowledge. If God's knowledge and power are absolute, then His giving us power should mirror His own power. The objection claims that if God has power to originate, He must give us power to originate. Nasafi responds by distinguishing two types of maqdur (objects of power) and two respects of power attachment, showing that human power is acquisition, not origination. This lesson lays out the initial argument and its core response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objection uses an analogy between knowledge and power. Notice how it sets up the problem: if God informs us truthfully, that's knowledge; if He gives power in the same respect, that's iqdar.
The objection claims that human power must be in the respect of origination.
2
Identify the two types of maqdur
The reply introduces mukhtara' (originated) and muktasab (acquired). Understand that God's power is creative, human power is not.
These are the two categories of things over which power is exercised.
3
Contrast with knowledge
Unlike power, knowledge attaches in only one respect. Why? Because attaching to something not as it is would be ignorance. This highlights the unique nature of power.
Knowledge's attachment is uniform; power has two respects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعلمنا أنه أسود أو أبيض وعلى ما كان كان ما ثبت لنا علمًا وإن علم هو شيئًا أسود وأعلمنا أبيض فما ثبت لنا لا يكون علمًا بل يكون جهلاً، فكذا هذا في قدرته وإقداره إيانا، فإذا قدر على شيء وأقدرنا عليه ينبغي أن يقدرنا على ذلك الوجه ولو أقدرنا لا على ذلك الوجه لا يكون ذلك إقدار ثم إنه تعالى يقدر اختراع الأشياء فإذا أقدرنا يقدرنا على جهة الاختراع، ولو لم يقدرنا على تلك الجهة لا يكون ذلك إقدارا.
فإنا نجيب عن هذا الكلام فنقول : بل يكون ذلك إقدارًا وإن لم يقدرنا على الاختراع أن للعبد فعلاً يتعلق به قدرته، وأن ثبوت الاختراع من جهته مستحيل، وثبت بمجموع الدليلين أن المقدور نوعان: مخترع ومكتسب، والقدرة تتعلق بالمقدور بجهتين جهة اختراع وجهة اكتساب اختص الله تعالى بأحدهما واختص المحدث بالآخر، بخلاف العلم فإن هناك لم يثبت دليل يوجب أن يعلق العلم بالمعلوم بجهتين بل قام الدليل أن تعلقه بالمعلوم بجهة واحدة وهو أن يتعلق به على ما هو به، إذ لو تعلق به لا على هذه الجهة لكان جهلاً لا علمًا.
ثم نشتغل بإبطال ذلك فنقول : قياس العلم يقتضي ما قلنا لو عقلتم، فإن علمنا يتعلق بما هو معلوم الله تعالى وليس من ضرورة تعلق علمنا به زوال علم الباري جل وعلا بل بقي علمه متعلقا به، وبقي المعلوم معلومًا له وإن صار معلومًا لنا، فكذا قدرتنا ينبغي أن تتعلق بما هو مقدور الله تعالى وعند تعلق قدرتنا به يبقى مقدورًا له، وكانت قدرته للاختراع فيبقى كذلك وكون الشيء مخترعًا بقدرتين محال بالإجماع، فتكون قدرة العبد متعلقة لا بجهة الاختراع ضرورة، فأما كون المعلوم معلومًا بعلمين فليس بمحال فيتعلق به علمه تعالى وعلمنا، والذي يؤيد ما قلنا: أن اعتبار العلم يوجب ما ذهبنا إليه أن إعلام الغير ممن لا علم له به محال، وإنما يصح إعلام الغير ممن له العلم، فكذا إقدار الغير على شيء لا قدرة للمقدور عليه يكون محالاً، وكذا زوال العلم عما هو معلوم غيره لا يكون إلا عن جهل، فكذا زوال القدرة عما هو مقدور الغير لن يكون إلا عن عجز، فكان فيما قلتم تعجيز الله تعالى وذلك محال.
ثم نقول لهم : لما كان يستحيل أن يعلمنا الله تعالى خلاف معلومه يستحيل أن يقدرنا الله تعالى على خلاف مقدوره، ومقدوره مخترع يضاف إليه لا مطلق المخترع، فبقدرنا أيضا على مخترع مضاف إليه لا على مطلق المخترع، ولو جاز أن يقدرنا على مخترع غير مضاف إليه لجاز أن يعلمنا معلومًا غير مضاف إليه وذا باطل، فكذا هذا.
وعلى هذا الوجه يبطل أيضًا قولهم إن ما قلتم يؤدي إلى جعل العباد مضطرين أو إلى تعجيز الله تعالى فإن الله تعالى إذا أراد أن يخلق كسب العبد إن كان للعبد قوة الامتناع فقد عجز الله تعالى عن تخليقه وإن لم يكن له قدرة الامتناع فهو إذًا مضطر
فإنا نقول: ثبتنا بالدليل أن لا اختراع من قبل العبد وأن له فعلاً كان
He informed us that it is black or white and whatever it was, what was established for us is knowledge. But if He knows something is black and informs us it is white, then what is established for us is not knowledge but ignorance. So likewise this is in His power (qudra) and His giving us power (iqdar). So when He has power over something and gives us power over it, He should give us power in that respect. And if He gives us power not in that respect, that would not be iqdar. Then He, exalted, has power to originate (ikhtira') things. So when He gives us power, He gives us power in the respect of origination. And if He did not give us power in that respect, that would not be iqdar. So we reply to this statement and say: Rather, that is iqdar even if He did not give us power over origination, because the servant has an act that his power is attached to, and that the affirmation of origination from his side is impossible. And it is established by the two proofs together that the thing over which power is exercised (maqdur) is of two types: originated (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). And power attaches to the maqdur in two respects: the respect of origination and the respect of acquisition. Allah, exalted, is specialized with one of them, and the originated being (muhdath) is specialized with the other. Unlike knowledge, for there no proof is established that requires that knowledge attaches to the known in two respects; rather, the proof is established that its attachment to the known is in one respect, which is that it attaches to it as it is. For if it attached to it not in this respect, it would be ignorance, not knowledge. Then we turn to invalidating that and say: The analogy of knowledge necessitates what we said, if you understood. For our knowledge attaches to what is known by Allah, exalted, and it is not necessary from the attachment of our knowledge to it that the knowledge of the Exalted Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, ceases. Rather, His knowledge remains attached to it, and the known remains known to Him even if it becomes known to us. So likewise our power should attach to what is an object of power (maqdur) of Allah, exalted, and when our power attaches to it, it remains an object of power to Him. And His power was for origination, so it remains so. And a thing being originated by two powers is impossible by consensus. So the servant's power attaches not in the respect of origination necessarily. As for a thing being known by two knowledges, it is not impossible, so His knowledge, exalted, and our knowledge attach to it. And what supports what we said is that considering knowledge necessitates what we have gone to: that informing others who have no knowledge of it is impossible, and informing others is only valid from one who has knowledge. So likewise, giving power to others over something when the one over whom power is exercised has no power is impossible. And similarly, the removal of knowledge from what is known to another is only from ignorance. So likewise, the removal of power from what is an object of power of another would only be from incapacity. So in what you said there is incapacitation (ta'jiz) of Allah, exalted, and that is impossible. Then we say to them: Since it is impossible that Allah, exalted, make us know contrary to what He knows, it is impossible that Allah, exalted, give us power over contrary to what He has power over. And what He has power over is an originated thing attributed to Him, not originated absolutely. So we too have power over an originated thing attributed to Him, not over originated absolutely. And if it were permissible that He give us power over an originated thing not attributed to Him, it would be permissible that He make us know a known thing not attributed to Him, and that is false. So likewise this. And in this way their statement is also refuted: that what you say leads to making servants compelled (mudtarrin) or to incapacitating Allah, exalted. For if Allah, exalted, wills to create the acquisition (kasb) of the servant, if the servant has the power to resist, then Allah, exalted, is incapacitated from creating it, and if he has no power to resist, then he is compelled. So we say: We have established by proof that there is no origination from the servant and that he has an act that was...
Source pages p. 903

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the objection that human power must be of the same kind as divine power, namely origination (ikhtira'). The argument proceeds by analogy with divine knowledge ('ilm). The author begins by establishing a principle: if Allah informs us of something as it truly is, that information is true knowledge; if He informs us contrary to His own knowledge, it is ignorance. The same applies to power (qudra): if Allah has power over something and gives us power, He must give it in the same respect—otherwise it would not be true iqdar. But He, exalted, has power to originate things, so if He gives us power, it must be in the respect of origination. The objector might say that human power cannot be origination. The author replies by distinguishing two types of maqdur: originated (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). Power attaches in two respects: origination and acquisition. Allah is exclusive to origination, and the created being is exclusive to acquisition. Unlike knowledge, which attaches in only one respect (as the thing is), so if it attached otherwise it would be ignorance. Then the author reinforces this with an analogy: our knowledge attaches to what is already known by Allah without removing His knowledge; similarly, our power should attach to what is already an object of divine power without removing His power. Since a thing cannot be originated by two powers, the servant's power necessarily attaches not in the respect of origination. He further argues that just as informing others requires prior knowledge, giving power to others requires prior power; otherwise it would be incapacitation (ta'jiz) of Allah, which is impossible. The final section refutes the charge that this view leads to compulsion (jabr) or divine incapacitation. The author asserts that it is established that there is no origination from the servant and that the servant has an act (which is acquisition). Thus the text maintains the Maturidi doctrine of kasb: human action is acquired, not created ex nihilo by the human, while divine power is creative.

اختراع (ikhtira')
مخترع (mukhtara')
مكتسب (muktasab)
قدرة (qudra)
مقدور (maqdur)
علم (ilm)
معلوم (ma'lum)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human power must be of the same nature as divine power for human action to be real.
Correction: Human power is acquisition, not origination; it attaches in a different respect, yet constitutes genuine action.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many types of maqdur are there?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Infinite

Key Takeaway
Human power is a real acquisition (kasb) distinct from divine origination (ikhtira').

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own actions, do you secretly feel that you are the originator of them, or do you truly see them as acquisitions from Allah? What would change in your humility if you internalized the distinction?
?
Nasafi distinguishes between knowledge and power. In your life, do you treat your knowledge of Allah's commands as something that informs your actions, or do you sometimes act as if your power is independent? How can you align your self-perception with the reality that your power is only acquisition?
?
If Allah restricted your power to only acquisition and not origination, does that make your actions less real or less accountable to you? How does the concept of kasb affect your sense of responsibility before your Creator?

Power Does Not Remove Divine Power
Nasafi argues from analogy and impossibility to show human power is not creative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why human power cannot be origination: because a thing cannot be originated by two powers, and because giving power to another requires prior power.

Core Idea
A thing cannot be created by both God and human; human power is thus a different kind.

In this passage, Nasafi deepens the argument by analyzing the relationship between divine and human power through analogy with knowledge. Just as our knowledge of something does not remove God's knowledge, our power over something should not remove God's power. Since God's power is creative, if our power were also creative, the same thing would be originated by two powers, which is impossible. He then argues that giving power to another requires prior power, otherwise it would be an incapacitation (ta'jiz) of God. This lesson covers these crucial proofs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the analogy with knowledge
Our knowledge attaches to what God knows without removing His knowledge. Similarly, our power should attach to what God has power over without removing His power.
The analogy is central: knowledge and power are both divine attributes that remain when humans acquire them.
2
Impossibility of two origination powers
If God's power is for origination, and our power also were for origination, the same act would be created by both, which is impossible by consensus.
The text says 'كون الشيء مخترعًا بقدرتين محال بالإجماع'.
3
The ta'jiz argument
Giving power to someone who has no power is impossible; it would imply God's incapacity. Thus human power must be of a different nature.
This uses the parallel of informing: you can only inform from knowledge, not ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعلمنا أنه أسود أو أبيض وعلى ما كان كان ما ثبت لنا علمًا وإن علم هو شيئًا أسود وأعلمنا أبيض فما ثبت لنا لا يكون علمًا بل يكون جهلاً، فكذا هذا في قدرته وإقداره إيانا، فإذا قدر على شيء وأقدرنا عليه ينبغي أن يقدرنا على ذلك الوجه ولو أقدرنا لا على ذلك الوجه لا يكون ذلك إقدار ثم إنه تعالى يقدر اختراع الأشياء فإذا أقدرنا يقدرنا على جهة الاختراع، ولو لم يقدرنا على تلك الجهة لا يكون ذلك إقدارا.
فإنا نجيب عن هذا الكلام فنقول : بل يكون ذلك إقدارًا وإن لم يقدرنا على الاختراع أن للعبد فعلاً يتعلق به قدرته، وأن ثبوت الاختراع من جهته مستحيل، وثبت بمجموع الدليلين أن المقدور نوعان: مخترع ومكتسب، والقدرة تتعلق بالمقدور بجهتين جهة اختراع وجهة اكتساب اختص الله تعالى بأحدهما واختص المحدث بالآخر، بخلاف العلم فإن هناك لم يثبت دليل يوجب أن يعلق العلم بالمعلوم بجهتين بل قام الدليل أن تعلقه بالمعلوم بجهة واحدة وهو أن يتعلق به على ما هو به، إذ لو تعلق به لا على هذه الجهة لكان جهلاً لا علمًا.
ثم نشتغل بإبطال ذلك فنقول : قياس العلم يقتضي ما قلنا لو عقلتم، فإن علمنا يتعلق بما هو معلوم الله تعالى وليس من ضرورة تعلق علمنا به زوال علم الباري جل وعلا بل بقي علمه متعلقا به، وبقي المعلوم معلومًا له وإن صار معلومًا لنا، فكذا قدرتنا ينبغي أن تتعلق بما هو مقدور الله تعالى وعند تعلق قدرتنا به يبقى مقدورًا له، وكانت قدرته للاختراع فيبقى كذلك وكون الشيء مخترعًا بقدرتين محال بالإجماع، فتكون قدرة العبد متعلقة لا بجهة الاختراع ضرورة، فأما كون المعلوم معلومًا بعلمين فليس بمحال فيتعلق به علمه تعالى وعلمنا، والذي يؤيد ما قلنا: أن اعتبار العلم يوجب ما ذهبنا إليه أن إعلام الغير ممن لا علم له به محال، وإنما يصح إعلام الغير ممن له العلم، فكذا إقدار الغير على شيء لا قدرة للمقدور عليه يكون محالاً، وكذا زوال العلم عما هو معلوم غيره لا يكون إلا عن جهل، فكذا زوال القدرة عما هو مقدور الغير لن يكون إلا عن عجز، فكان فيما قلتم تعجيز الله تعالى وذلك محال.
ثم نقول لهم : لما كان يستحيل أن يعلمنا الله تعالى خلاف معلومه يستحيل أن يقدرنا الله تعالى على خلاف مقدوره، ومقدوره مخترع يضاف إليه لا مطلق المخترع، فبقدرنا أيضا على مخترع مضاف إليه لا على مطلق المخترع، ولو جاز أن يقدرنا على مخترع غير مضاف إليه لجاز أن يعلمنا معلومًا غير مضاف إليه وذا باطل، فكذا هذا.
وعلى هذا الوجه يبطل أيضًا قولهم إن ما قلتم يؤدي إلى جعل العباد مضطرين أو إلى تعجيز الله تعالى فإن الله تعالى إذا أراد أن يخلق كسب العبد إن كان للعبد قوة الامتناع فقد عجز الله تعالى عن تخليقه وإن لم يكن له قدرة الامتناع فهو إذًا مضطر
فإنا نقول: ثبتنا بالدليل أن لا اختراع من قبل العبد وأن له فعلاً كان
He informed us that it is black or white and whatever it was, what was established for us is knowledge. But if He knows something is black and informs us it is white, then what is established for us is not knowledge but ignorance. So likewise this is in His power (qudra) and His giving us power (iqdar). So when He has power over something and gives us power over it, He should give us power in that respect. And if He gives us power not in that respect, that would not be iqdar. Then He, exalted, has power to originate (ikhtira') things. So when He gives us power, He gives us power in the respect of origination. And if He did not give us power in that respect, that would not be iqdar. So we reply to this statement and say: Rather, that is iqdar even if He did not give us power over origination, because the servant has an act that his power is attached to, and that the affirmation of origination from his side is impossible. And it is established by the two proofs together that the thing over which power is exercised (maqdur) is of two types: originated (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). And power attaches to the maqdur in two respects: the respect of origination and the respect of acquisition. Allah, exalted, is specialized with one of them, and the originated being (muhdath) is specialized with the other. Unlike knowledge, for there no proof is established that requires that knowledge attaches to the known in two respects; rather, the proof is established that its attachment to the known is in one respect, which is that it attaches to it as it is. For if it attached to it not in this respect, it would be ignorance, not knowledge. Then we turn to invalidating that and say: The analogy of knowledge necessitates what we said, if you understood. For our knowledge attaches to what is known by Allah, exalted, and it is not necessary from the attachment of our knowledge to it that the knowledge of the Exalted Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, ceases. Rather, His knowledge remains attached to it, and the known remains known to Him even if it becomes known to us. So likewise our power should attach to what is an object of power (maqdur) of Allah, exalted, and when our power attaches to it, it remains an object of power to Him. And His power was for origination, so it remains so. And a thing being originated by two powers is impossible by consensus. So the servant's power attaches not in the respect of origination necessarily. As for a thing being known by two knowledges, it is not impossible, so His knowledge, exalted, and our knowledge attach to it. And what supports what we said is that considering knowledge necessitates what we have gone to: that informing others who have no knowledge of it is impossible, and informing others is only valid from one who has knowledge. So likewise, giving power to others over something when the one over whom power is exercised has no power is impossible. And similarly, the removal of knowledge from what is known to another is only from ignorance. So likewise, the removal of power from what is an object of power of another would only be from incapacity. So in what you said there is incapacitation (ta'jiz) of Allah, exalted, and that is impossible. Then we say to them: Since it is impossible that Allah, exalted, make us know contrary to what He knows, it is impossible that Allah, exalted, give us power over contrary to what He has power over. And what He has power over is an originated thing attributed to Him, not originated absolutely. So we too have power over an originated thing attributed to Him, not over originated absolutely. And if it were permissible that He give us power over an originated thing not attributed to Him, it would be permissible that He make us know a known thing not attributed to Him, and that is false. So likewise this. And in this way their statement is also refuted: that what you say leads to making servants compelled (mudtarrin) or to incapacitating Allah, exalted. For if Allah, exalted, wills to create the acquisition (kasb) of the servant, if the servant has the power to resist, then Allah, exalted, is incapacitated from creating it, and if he has no power to resist, then he is compelled. So we say: We have established by proof that there is no origination from the servant and that he has an act that was...
Source pages p. 903

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the objection that human power must be of the same kind as divine power, namely origination (ikhtira'). The argument proceeds by analogy with divine knowledge ('ilm). The author begins by establishing a principle: if Allah informs us of something as it truly is, that information is true knowledge; if He informs us contrary to His own knowledge, it is ignorance. The same applies to power (qudra): if Allah has power over something and gives us power, He must give it in the same respect—otherwise it would not be true iqdar. But He, exalted, has power to originate things, so if He gives us power, it must be in the respect of origination. The objector might say that human power cannot be origination. The author replies by distinguishing two types of maqdur: originated (mukhtara') and acquired (muktasab). Power attaches in two respects: origination and acquisition. Allah is exclusive to origination, and the created being is exclusive to acquisition. Unlike knowledge, which attaches in only one respect (as the thing is), so if it attached otherwise it would be ignorance. Then the author reinforces this with an analogy: our knowledge attaches to what is already known by Allah without removing His knowledge; similarly, our power should attach to what is already an object of divine power without removing His power. Since a thing cannot be originated by two powers, the servant's power necessarily attaches not in the respect of origination. He further argues that just as informing others requires prior knowledge, giving power to others requires prior power; otherwise it would be incapacitation (ta'jiz) of Allah, which is impossible. The final section refutes the charge that this view leads to compulsion (jabr) or divine incapacitation. The author asserts that it is established that there is no origination from the servant and that the servant has an act (which is acquisition). Thus the text maintains the Maturidi doctrine of kasb: human action is acquired, not created ex nihilo by the human, while divine power is creative.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas)
علم (ilm)
قدرة (qudra)
إقدار (iqdar)
اختراع (ikhtira')
مخترع (mukhtara')
تعجيز (ta'jiz)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God has power to create, then humans can also create.
Correction: A thing cannot be created by two powers, and giving creative power would imply divine incapacity.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if human power were origination?
A) Human would be independent
B) God's power would be removed
C) The thing would be created by two powers (impossible)
D) None

Key Takeaway
Human power is non-creative and attaches without removing divine power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you genuinely succeed at something—whether it's a career achievement, a personal goal, or an act of worship—do you ever feel, even for a moment, that your own power was the real creator of that success? This lesson says that would be attributing origination to yourself. What would it cost you to completely, radically attribute every good outcome to Allah alone as the sole originator, and how would that change the way you speak about your achievements?
?
Think of an area in your life where you struggle with reliance on Allah—perhaps a habit you're trying to change, or a fear of the future. Deep down, do you ever act as if your own power must do the creating, and that Allah's power is somehow secondary or limited? This lesson warns that such a belief is an incapacitation (ta'jiz) of Allah. What is one specific step you will take today to consciously affirm that only Allah originates, and your role is simply to attach your effort without claiming creativity?
?
If you truly believe that your power is not creative—that it attaches but does not originate—then your daily actions are not the cause of outcomes, but only the acquisition of something Allah creates. How does that change the weight of your responsibility and the peace in your heart? Are you willing to fully embrace the vulnerability that comes with knowing your power is not the last word, and why or why not?

Divine Decree
intermediate
5 min
Refuting the Charge of Compulsion and Incapacitation
Nasafi refutes the charge of jabr and ta'jiz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi refutes the objection that his view leads to compulsion or divine incapacitation, affirming the reality of human kasb.

Core Idea
Human acquisition is real action; it does not compel nor incapacitate God.

The final part of Nasafi's argument addresses a counter-objection: if humans do not originate their own acts, they are either compelled (mujbar) or God is incapacitated by their resistance. Nasafi refutes this by reiterating the distinction: there is no origination from the servant, but the servant has a genuine act (kasb). This lesson examines the logical force of this refutation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection states: if God creates the servant's act, either the servant can resist (making God unable) or cannot (making him compelled). So either ta'jiz or jabr.
2
Nasafi's reply
He simply states that it is established that there is no human origination, and the servant has an act (kasb). This presupposes the earlier proofs.
The argument relies on the prior distinction between mukhtara' and muktasab.
3
The force of the argument
The earlier distinction already precludes the false dilemma; human action is real through acquisition, not compulsion or incapacity.
Kasb is a genuine act even though not creative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أعلمنا أنه أسود أو أبيض وعلى ما كان كان ما ثبت لنا علمًا وإن علم هو شيئًا أسود وأعلمنا أبيض فما ثبت لنا لا يكون علمًا بل يكون جهلاً، فكذا هذا في قدرته وإقداره إيانا، فإذا قدر على شيء وأقدرنا عليه ينبغي أن يقدرنا على ذلك الوجه ولو أقدرنا لا على ذلك الوجه لا يكون ذلك إقدار ثم إنه تعالى يقدر اختراع الأشياء فإذا أقدرنا يقدرنا على جهة الاختراع، ولو لم يقدرنا على تلك الجهة لا يكون ذلك إقدارا.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the objection that human power must be of the same kind as divine power, namely origination (ikhtira'). The argument proceeds by analogy with divine knowledge ('ilm). According to the passage, what does the servant have if not origination?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever secretly blame God for your sins, thinking He forced you? This lesson declares your kasb is real. Will you now own your wrongs and turn to Him without excuse?
?
If you truly believe that your actions are your own acquisition while God is not incapacitated, how will you approach your next moment of weakness? Commit now to one concrete action that reflects your responsibility.
?
When you face a situation you feel powerless to change, do you doubt God's ability to act? This lesson affirms His power and your agency. What will you do today to act righteously despite your circumstances?

Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
Why the Servant Cannot Abstain from Any Act
Author refutes objections by showing impossibility of abstention in all actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to the author, the servant cannot abstain from actions whether they are necessary or voluntary, and how this relates to God's will and the concept of acquisition.

Core Idea
God's will leaves no room for the servant to abstain from any action.

This passage presents a key argument in the Maturidi refutation of objections to divine predetermination. The author examines two scenarios—necessary and voluntary actions—to demonstrate that in both cases, abstention is impossible. Understanding this argument clarifies the Maturidi view on human capacity and divine action.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
The passage contains a footnote marker (۲) which is unimportant for the argument.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify the two cases: (1) God wills necessary motion, (2) God wills voluntary motion. Notice how each leads to the same conclusion about abstention.
The key difference is the role of the servant's will and acquisition in the second case.
3
Analyze the rationale for impossibility of abstention
For necessary motion, the servant is compelled. For voluntary motion, God's consistent practice (ʿāda) ensures creation when the servant intends, and abstention from an existing act is logically impossible.
Focus on the final argument: 'Abstention from the existent is impossible.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : إن كان الله تعالى أراد (۲) الحركة الضرورية من العبد فيخلقه ولا يكون للعبد قدرة الامتناع والله تعالى قادر والعبد مضطر ، وإن أراد تخليق الحركة الاختيارية فالعبد لا يتصور منه الامتناع لأنه تعالى إنما يخلق تلك الحركة إذا أرادها العبد واختار وقصد اكتسابها فيخلق الله تعالى لا محالة لإجرائه العادة في تخليقه عند وجود قصد العهد لا لكونه ملجأ إلى ذلك، على أن الله تعالى إذا كان يخلقه مقارنا لقدرة العبد كيف يتصور منه الامتناع عن الفعل وهو موجود والامتناع عن الموجود محال، والله الموفق.
Then we say: If God, exalted, willed the necessary motion from the servant, He creates it and the servant has no power of abstention – and God is powerful and the servant is compelled. And if He wills the creation of the voluntary motion, then abstention from it is inconceivable from the servant, because He, exalted, only creates that motion when the servant wills it, chooses it, and intends to acquire it. Then God, exalted, inevitably creates it, due to His continuous practice in creating when the intention of the servant occurs, not because He is compelled to that. Moreover, if God, exalted, creates it concomitant with the servant's power, how can abstention from the act be conceived from him while the act exists? And abstention from the existent is impossible. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 905

Commentary
This passage examines the implications of God's will for human action. The author considers two cases: (1) If God wills a necessary motion from the servant, then He creates it and the servant has no power to refrain – the servant is compelled (muḍṭarr). (2) If God wills to create a voluntary (ikhtiyārī) motion, then the servant cannot conceive of abstention. Why? Because God only creates that motion when the servant wills it, chooses it, and intends to acquire (kasb) it. God then inevitably creates it, due to His continuous practice (ʿāda) of creating when the servant's intent is present, not because God is compelled. The author then argues: since God creates the act concomitant with the servant's power (qādir), how can the servant abstain from an existent act? Abstention from what exists is impossible. Thus, in both necessary and voluntary actions, the servant cannot truly abstain, which refutes any objection that posits real ability to abstain.

حركة ضرورية
حركة اختيارية
قدرة الامتناع
اكتساب
عادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The servant has an independent ability to abstain from actions that God creates.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that in both necessary and voluntary actions, abstention is impossible: necessary actions compel, and voluntary actions are created by God concurrent with the servant's power, making abstention from an existing act logically impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does God create the voluntary motion?
A) Only when He compels the servant.
B) When the servant wills, chooses, and intends to acquire it.
C) Randomly without cause.
D) Only when the servant abstains.

Key Takeaway
God's will and His established practice ensure that the servant cannot abstain from any action that He creates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel that God's will was involved in that action? How does this lesson confront your sense of personal responsibility? What would it mean to fully accept that every act you commit is created by God, yet you are accountable?
?
If abstention from an existing act is impossible, then how do you view your moments of weakness? Are you ready to stop blaming your circumstances and instead see your actions as inseparable from God's decree, and still strive to choose what pleases Him?
?
This passage denies any real 'power of abstention' once the act exists. How does that challenge your assumptions about free will? Will you change how you ask for forgiveness, knowing that your repentance itself is an act that God creates when you will it?

Two Powers on One Act: The Ahl al-Sunna Position
Al-Nasafi states the Ahl al-Sunna position and uses the Mu'tazila's tawallud to argue against them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position that two powers can attach to one act from the same aspect, and how they use this to refute the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Two powers on one act is possible; the Mu'tazila's rejection leads to contradiction.

Al-Nasafi introduces a key theological dispute: can two divine powers attach to a single created act? The Mu'tazila deny it, but Ahl al-Sunna affirm its possibility. This lesson presents the initial question, the Ahl al-Sunna stance, and their argument that the Mu'tazila's own principles lead to absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the core issue: is it permissible for another power to attach to an act by creation?
Note that 'by creation' means from the aspect of bringing into existence.
2
Identify the Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila positions
Locate where Al-Nasafi states 'with us it is permissible' and 'with them it is impossible'. See how he claims consensus against attachment from creation.
3
Understand the argument from tawallud
The Ahl al-Sunna use the Mu'tazila's own theory of generation to force them into admitting two agents for one act. Follow the example of two men moving a stone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بمقدور بجهة الاختراع هل يجوز أن تتعلق به قدرة أخرى يكون أثرها جعل ذلك المخترع فعلا له أم لا؟ الجواز. عندنا ذلك جائز وعندهم ذلك ممتنع، وقد أقمنا الدلالة على فضلاً وجوبه عن ثم إنهم مع أبائهم تعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد بجهتين وانعقاد الإجماع من كل العقلاء على استحالة تعلقهما (۱) به من جهة الاختراع أفضت الأصول الفاسدة بهم إلى تجويز تعلقهما به من جهة واحدة وهي الاختراع فعظم عليهم الخطب بذلك وتفرقت رؤساؤهم في الاحتيال للتخلص عنه فلم يمكنهم ولم يحصل لهم بذلك إلا التجاهل والخروج عن شهادات المعارف، وذلك أن أهل السنة ألزموهم على قولهم أن بالتولد أن رجلين مستويي القدرة لو حركا حجر فتحرك الحجر فكان ما فيه من الحركة فعلاً للمحركين مقدوراً لهما، فكان الشيء الواحد فعلاً لفاعلين مقدورًا لقادرين فبطل ما يوجهون على أهل السنة من إنكار مقدور لقادرين وعلى متكلمي أهل الحديث والنجارية من استحالة كون شيء واحد فعلا لفاعلين، فتفرقت المعتزلة في دفع هذا الإلزام، فزعم بشر بن المعتمر أن أجزاء الحجر لو كانت زوجا يتحرك نصفها بأحدهما والنصف الآخر بالثاني. فقيل له: لو كانت الأجزاء وتر بأن كانت مثلاً أحد عشر جزءًا ؟ فقال: حركات ستة منها لأحدهما وحركات الخمسة الباقية للثاني. قيل له: لو كانوا استويا في البنية والقوة والنشاط والإرادة كيف يتصور أن يضاف إلى أحدهما أكثر وإلى الآخر الأقل؟ فقال: محال أن يستويا في ذلك، فقيل له: لم قلت ذلك ؟ فقال : لأنهما لو (۲) استويا في ذلك لأوجب أحد أمرين: إما وجود فعل من فاعلين، وإما انقسام حركة جزء لا يتجزأ وكلاهما محال، وما أدى إلى المحال كان محالاً في نفسه، ثم مثل هذا بجزء متوسط بين رجلين أحدهما عن يمينه والآخر عن يساره لا يجوز أن يستوي الرجلان في القوة والإرادة للتحرك إلى ذلك الجزء، لأنهما لو استويا ولا يكون أحدهما أولى ببلوغ مراده (۱) أدى إلى أحد أمرين كل واحد منهما محال فإنهما إما أن لا يبرحا من مكانهما من غير منع، وإما أن يوافيا ذلك الجزء جميعًا، وكل واحد من الأمرين فاسد، فكذا (۲) هذا.
والجواب عن هذا أن يقال : لا وجه لإنكار قدرة الله تعالى أن يخلق شخصين مستويي القدرة والبنية، ومن ضرورة ذلك أن يكون في قدرة كل واحد منهما مثل ما في قدرة (۳) الآخر ليقع الفرق بين القوتين المستويتين والقوتين المختلفة، ثم لا شك أن اتفاقهما على فعل ليس بممتنع، وليس هذا الممكن يجعله محالاً أو من جعل ذلك المحال ممكناً لمكان هذا، وهكذا هذا على كل من دفع موهومًا خوفاً من وجوب المحال عليه؛ لأن دفع الممكن هرباً من المحال كتصحيح المحال هرباً من إحالة الصحيح. ثم نقول لهم (٤): لا نزاع لأحد من العقلاء في كون (ثبوت الرجلين المستويين) (۵) في القوة واتفاقهما على الإرادة ممكنًا، ولا دليل في الفعل يدل على إحالته بل فيه دليل إمكانه، وكون فعل واحد لفاعلين وتعلق قدرتين بمقدور واحد مما للعقلاء فيه كلام، فهلا علمت بإفضاء ذلك الممكن إليه أنه ممكن حتى خالفت العقل والعقلاء، وجعلت الممكن ممتنعاً، وهذا جهل فاحش
By the aspect of creation, is it permissible that another power (qudra) attaches to it, the effect of which is to make that created thing an act for him or not? The answer: permissibility. With us, that is permissible; with them, that is impossible. We have demonstrated the proof for it, rather its obligatoriness, concerning [missing]. Then, despite their rejection of the attachment of two powers to one object from two aspects, and the consensus of all rational beings on the impossibility of their attachment to it from the aspect of creation, their corrupt principles led them to permit their attachment to it from one aspect, which is creation. So the matter became grave for them, and their leaders scattered in devising ways to escape it, but they could not, and they only gained ignorance and departure from the testimonies of intellects. That is because Ahl al-Sunna compelled them, on their doctrine of generation (tawallud), that if two men of equal power moved a stone, and the stone moved, then the movement in it would be an act of the movers and within their power. So a single thing would be an act of two agents and within the power of two capable beings. Thus their objection to Ahl al-Sunna about denying a single object of power for two capable beings, and to the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith and al-Najjariyya about the impossibility of a single thing being an act of two agents, is invalidated. So the Mu'tazila scattered in repelling this required consequence. Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir claimed that if the parts of the stone were even, half would move by one and the other half by the second. It was said to him: If the parts were odd, e.g., eleven parts? He said: Six movements would be from one and the remaining five from the second. It was said to him: If they were equal in constitution, strength, energy, and will, how can it be conceived that more is attributed to one and less to the other? He said: It is impossible for them to be equal in that. It was said to him: Why did you say that? He said: Because if they were equal in that, it would necessitate one of two things: either the existence of an act from two agents, or the division of the movement of an indivisible part, both of which are impossible. Whatever leads to the impossible is itself impossible. Then he compared this to a part between two men, one on his right and the other on his left: it is not permissible for the two men to be equal in strength and will to move toward that part, because if they were equal and one is not more deserving of reaching his goal, it would lead to one of two things, each impossible: either they would not leave their places without hindrance, or they would both reach that part together. Each of the two cases is invalid. So likewise this. The answer to this is to say: There is no basis for denying the power of Allah Most High to create two persons equal in power and constitution. Necessary to that is that in the power of each one there is the like of what is in the power of the other, so that a distinction occurs between equal powers and unequal powers. Then there is no doubt that their agreement on an act is not impossible. And this possible thing is not rendered impossible nor is that impossible made possible due to this. And so this applies to everyone who repels a supposed [objection] out of fear of the necessity of the impossible upon him; because repelling the possible to escape the impossible is like affirming the impossible to escape the absurdity of the sound. Then we say to them: There is no dispute among any rational persons concerning the possibility of two men being equal in strength and agreeing in will. And there is no evidence in the act indicating its impossibility; rather, the evidence indicates its possibility. And the fact of a single act from two agents and the attachment of two powers to one object of power is something about which rational persons have discussion. So why do you not realize that this possible leads to it being possible, such that you have opposed reason and the rational persons, and rendered the possible impossible? This is gross ignorance.
Source pages p. 907

Commentary
This passage is a kalam argument about whether two powers (qudratān) can attach to a single act (maqdūr wāḥid) from the same aspect (jihat al-ikhtirāʿ). It presents the Ahl al-Sunna position, the Mu'tazilite objection using the example of two men moving a stone, Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir's attempt to avoid the implication, and the Ahl al-Sunna refutation.

The passage opens with a question: Can another power attach to an act from the aspect of creation? The answer is 'permissible' (al-jawāz). Ahl al-Sunna hold it permissible; the Mu'tazila hold it impossible. Al-Nasafi states that Ahl al-Sunna have already demonstrated its proof. Then he notes that despite the Mu'tazila's rejection of two powers attaching from two aspects and the consensus of all rational beings against attachment from the aspect of creation, their corrupt principles led them to permit attachment from one aspect (creation), causing them great difficulty. Their leaders tried to devise escape but failed, only gaining ignorance and departing from intellect.

The core objection: Ahl al-Sunna compelled the Mu'tazila, on their own theory of generation (tawallud), with the example of two equally powerful men moving a stone. If they both move it, the movement would be an act of both and within both their powers, meaning one thing is an act of two agents. This refutes the Mu'tazila's denial of a single object of power for two agents, and also refutes Ahl al-Hadith and al-Najjariyya who deem one act from two agents impossible. Faced with this, the Mu'tazila split. Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir proposed a solution: if the stone's parts were even (e.g., 10 parts), half would move by one man, half by the other. When pressed about odd numbers (e.g., 11), he said six movements for one, five for the other. Asked how that could happen if both are equal in strength and will, he claimed equality is impossible. He argued that equality would necessitate either a single act from two agents or the division of an indivisible part, both impossible. He analogized to a piece between two men: if equal, they would either not move or both reach it—both invalid.

The answer (al-jawāb) begins: There is no basis to deny that God can create two persons exactly equal in power and constitution. Necessarily, each would have the same power as the other, distinguishing equal powers from unequal ones. Their agreement on an act is not impossible. Rejecting this possible scenario to avoid an impossible consequence is itself flawed—it is like affirming an impossibility to avoid something absurd. Ahl al-Sunna then assert that rational persons agree on the possibility of two equal men agreeing in will. The act itself gives no evidence of impossibility; rather, it suggests possibility. The notion of one act from two agents and two powers on one object is debated among rational persons, so why does the Mu'tazila insist it is impossible, contradicting reason and rational persons? This is gross ignorance.

تعلق قدرتين
اختراع

فاعل
محال
ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Two agents cannot perform one act.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna show it is possible by the example of two men moving a stone.

Checkpoint
What is the Ahl al-Sunna position on the attachment of two powers to one act by creation?
A) Impossible
B) Permissible
C) Obligatory
D) Only from two aspects

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna affirm that two powers can attach to one act from the same aspect, and this is proven by the rational example of two agents affecting one object.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though your actions are entirely your own, forgetting that God's power creates them? How does this lesson's truth that two powers affect one act change how you will seek help from Allah tonight?
?
When you sin, do you blame yourself entirely or forget that your act is also under Allah's will? Will you now repent with the awareness that your power is a gift, and hold yourself accountable without arrogance?
?
If the Mu'tazila's error was inconsistency, where in your own beliefs about causality and God's control do you find contradictions? Are you ready to submit to the Ahl al-Sunna position, even if it challenges your rational assumptions?

Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir's Attempt and the Ahl al-Sunna Refutation
Al-Nasafi presents Bishr's attempted escape and the Ahl al-Sunna refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir's attempt to avoid the implication of two agents for one act and the Ahl al-Sunna refutation that shows the possibility of equal powers agreeing on an act.

Core Idea
Bishr's arbitrary division fails; God can create equal powers, and their agreement is not impossible.

The Mu'tazila, faced with the stone-moving example, proposed various escape attempts. Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir tried to divide the stone's movement between the two agents. This lesson presents his argument and the Ahl al-Sunna response, which defends the possibility of two equal powers acting together.

Guided Path
1
Read Bishr's proposal
Read how Bishr tries to avoid a single act from two agents by dividing the stone's movement based on even or odd parts.
His proposal is problematic: why would one contribute more if equal?
2
Follow the counter-arguments
Notice the objections: how can equal men produce unequal movements? Bishr denies equality can occur.
3
Examine Bishr's reasoning
He argues equality would lead to either one act from two agents or division of indivisible parts, both impossible.
4
Study the Ahl al-Sunna answer
The answer denies that equality is impossible; it is within God's power to create equal persons. Their agreement on an act is possible, and rejecting it is gross ignorance.

By the aspect of creation, is it permissible that another power (qudra) attaches to it, the effect of which is to make that created thing an act for him or not? The answer: permissibility. With us, that is permissible; with them, that is impossible. We have demonstrated the proof for it, rather its obligatoriness, concerning [missing]. Then, despite their rejection of the attachment of two powers to one object from two aspects, and the consensus of all rational beings on the impossibility of their attachment to it from the aspect of creation, their corrupt principles led them to permit their attachment to it from one aspect, which is creation. So the matter became grave for them, and their leaders scattered in devising ways to escape it, but they could not, and they only gained ignorance and departure from the testimonies of intellects. That is because Ahl al-Sunna compelled them, on their doctrine of generation (tawallud), that if two men of equal power moved a stone, and the stone moved, then the movement in it would be an act of the movers and within their power. So a single thing would be an act of two agents and within the power of two capable beings. Thus their objection to Ahl al-Sunna about denying a single object of power for two capable beings, and to the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith and al-Najjariyya about the impossibility of a single thing being an act of two agents, is invalidated. So the Mu'tazila scattered in repelling this required consequence. Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir claimed that if the parts of the stone were even, half would move by one and the other half by the second. It was said to him: If the parts were odd, e.g., eleven parts? He said: Six movements would be from one and the remaining five from the second. It was said to him: If they were equal in constitution, strength, energy, and will, how can it be conceived that more is attributed to one and less to the other? He said: It is impossible for them to be equal in that. It was said to him: Why did you say that? He said: Because if they were equal in that, it would necessitate one of two things: either the existence of an act from two agents, or the division of the movement of an indivisible part, both of which are impossible. Whatever leads to the impossible is itself impossible. Then he compared this to a part between two men, one on his right and the other on his left: it is not permissible for the two men to be equal in strength and will to move toward that part, because if they were equal and one is not more deserving of reaching his goal, it would lead to one of two things, each impossible: either they would not leave their places without hindrance, or they would both reach that part together. Each of the two cases is invalid. So likewise this. The answer to this is to say: There is no basis for denying the power of Allah Most High to create two persons equal in power and constitution. Necessary to that is that in the power of each one there is the like of what is in the power of the other, so that a distinction occurs between equal powers and unequal powers. Then there is no doubt that their agreement on an act is not impossible. And this possible thing is not rendered impossible nor is that impossible made possible due to this. And so this applies to everyone who repels a supposed [objection] out of fear of the necessity of the impossible upon him; because repelling the possible to escape the impossible is like affirming the impossible to escape the absurdity of the sound. Then we say to them: There is no dispute among any rational persons concerning the possibility of two men being equal in strength and agreeing in will. And there is no evidence in the act indicating its impossibility; rather, the evidence indicates its possibility. And the fact of a single act from two agents and the attachment of two powers to one object of power is something about which rational persons have discussion. So why do you not realize that this possible leads to it being possible, such that you have opposed reason and the rational persons, and rendered the possible impossible? This is gross ignorance.
Source pages p. 907

Commentary
This passage is a kalam argument about whether two powers (qudratān) can attach to a single act (maqdūr wāḥid) from the same aspect (jihat al-ikhtirāʿ). It presents the Ahl al-Sunna position, the Mu'tazilite objection using the example of two men moving a stone, Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir's attempt to avoid the implication, and the Ahl al-Sunna refutation.

The passage opens with a question: Can another power attach to an act from the aspect of creation? The answer is 'permissible' (al-jawāz). Ahl al-Sunna hold it permissible; the Mu'tazila hold it impossible. Al-Nasafi states that Ahl al-Sunna have already demonstrated its proof. Then he notes that despite the Mu'tazila's rejection of two powers attaching from two aspects and the consensus of all rational beings against attachment from the aspect of creation, their corrupt principles led them to permit attachment from one aspect (creation), causing them great difficulty. Their leaders tried to devise escape but failed, only gaining ignorance and departing from intellect.

The core objection: Ahl al-Sunna compelled the Mu'tazila, on their own theory of generation (tawallud), with the example of two equally powerful men moving a stone. If they both move it, the movement would be an act of both and within both their powers, meaning one thing is an act of two agents. This refutes the Mu'tazila's denial of a single object of power for two agents, and also refutes Ahl al-Hadith and al-Najjariyya who deem one act from two agents impossible. Faced with this, the Mu'tazila split. Bishr ibn al-Mu'tamir proposed a solution: if the stone's parts were even (e.g., 10 parts), half would move by one man, half by the other. When pressed about odd numbers (e.g., 11), he said six movements for one, five for the other. Asked how that could happen if both are equal in strength and will, he claimed equality is impossible. He argued that equality would necessitate either a single act from two agents or the division of an indivisible part, both impossible. He analogized to a piece between two men: if equal, they would either not move or both reach it—both invalid.

The answer (al-jawāb) begins: There is no basis to deny that God can create two persons exactly equal in power and constitution. Necessarily, each would have the same power as the other, distinguishing equal powers from unequal ones. Their agreement on an act is not impossible. Rejecting this possible scenario to avoid an impossible consequence is itself flawed—it is like affirming an impossibility to avoid something absurd. Ahl al-Sunna then assert that rational persons agree on the possibility of two equal men agreeing in will. The act itself gives no evidence of impossibility; rather, it suggests possibility. The notion of one act from two agents and two powers on one object is debated among rational persons, so why does the Mu'tazila insist it is impossible, contradicting reason and rational persons? This is gross ignorance.

Key Terms
إلزام
تولد
قدرة
محال
ممكن
جهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Two equal agents cannot act on one object; Bishr's argument is valid.
Correction: Bishr's argument is invalid because God can create equals and their agreement is possible.

Checkpoint
According to the Ahl al-Sunna response, why is Bishr's argument invalid?
A) Because God cannot create equals
B) Because equality leads to impossibility
C) Because God can create equal persons and their agreement is possible
D) Because the stone example is irrelevant

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Sunna maintain that two equal powers can agree on one act, and attempts to deny this are based on false assumptions and ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a theological possibility because your own reasoning could not conceive it, rather than submitting to the boundless power of Allah? What specific assumption do you need to surrender today?
?
When you face a contradiction between your logic and divine attributes, do you force the attribute to fit your logic, or do you humble your logic before Allah's omnipotence? What would it cost you to truly accept that Allah can do what seems impossible to you?
?
In your daily life, do you trust Allah's power to bring about outcomes that seem impossible from your perspective? What is one situation right now where you are acting as if God's power is limited by your reasoning, and what would it look like to trust Him fully?

The Mu'tazila Claim of Irrationality Refuted
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila accusation by showing their own position is irrational.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi defends the rationality of kasb by exposing the absurd consequences of the Mu'tazila doctrine of the non-existent.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila accuse kasb of irrationality, but their own belief in the non-existent leads to absurdity.

In this passage, Nasafi responds to the Mu'tazila objection that the doctrine of kasb is irrational. He turns their accusation around, arguing that their own doctrine—that the non-existent is a thing—leads to devastating consequences for theology, including nullifying the Creator and making the world eternal. This lesson explores that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage where Nasafi states the Mu'tazila claim and his response. Notice how he first affirms the rationality of kasb, then turns the accusation back on the Mu'tazila.
The passage uses strong rhetorical language.
2
Identify the consequences
List the four consequences Nasafi draws from the Mu'tazila belief that the non-existent is a thing. Each follows from the idea that power cannot relate to existence.
These consequences are: nullification of the Creator, eternity of the world, annulment of human action, nullification of religious commands.
3
Reflect on the argument
Consider how these consequences show the irrationality of the Mu'tazila position. Why does Nasafi believe this refutes their objection to kasb?
The Mu'tazila claim kasb is irrational, but their own doctrine leads to theological absurdities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن المعتزلة يزعمون أن ما تدعون أنتم من الكسب غير معقول وقد بينا أنه معقول لقيام الدلائل العقلية عليه إلا أنه ليس بموهوم، ولو رفضت المعتزلة التعصب ونظرت بالعقل وانقادت للدليل وجانبت الهوى وأنصفت من نفسها لعرفت أنهم القائلون بما لا يعقل المستمسكون بما هو المحال الممتنع، وذلك أن من مذهب جمهورهم أن المعدوم شيء، وأكثرهم يزعمون أنه عين وعرض وجوهر قبل الحدوث وكذا سواد وحركة وذات على ما قررنا قبل هذا من بيان أقاويلهم. ثم قدرة الفاعل لا تتعلق إلا بالوجود ولا تعلق لها بالشيئية، ولا تكون حركة ولا سوادا ولا جوهرا ولا ذاتاً ولا عينا لأن هذه الأوصاف كانت ثابتة في الأزل، ثم الوجود ليس بمعنى وراء الذات ولا تعلق للقدرة بالذات فلا يتصور تعلقها بالوجود إذ هو ليس معنى وراء الذات فإذا لا تعلق القدرة ما، لا للقدرة القديمة ولا للقدرة المحدثة بمقدور البتة، وفيه تعطيل الصانع والقول بقدم العالم، وإبطال ثبوت الفعل للعباد، وتعطيل الأمر والنهي والوعد والوعيد، ونحن نقول: إن الله تعالى خلق العالم وجعل ما ليس بسواد ولا بياض ولا جوهر ولا عرض ولا موجود سوادا وبياضا وجوهرًا وعرضاً وموجودًا ، ثم ما كان من ذلك أفعال العباد فوجوده وشيئيته متعلقة بقدرة الله تعالى وكونه حركة وسكونا وطاعة ومعصية متعلقة بقدرة العبد، وعندهم لا تتعلق شيئية بقدرة أحد ووجوده ليس بمعنى
Then indeed the Mu'tazila claim that what you (the Ash'aris/Maturidis) call kasb is irrational. And we have shown that it is rational because of the rational proofs established for it, except that it is not sensible (mawhum). And if the Mu'tazila abandoned partisanship, and looked with intellect, and submitted to the proof, and shunned desire, and were fair to themselves, they would recognize that they are the ones saying what is irrational, holding fast to what is impossible and absurd. That is because from the doctrine of most of them (the Mu'tazila) is that the non-existent (al-ma'dum) is a thing (shay'), and most of them claim that it is an entity ('ayn), an accident ('arad), and a substance (jawhar) before coming into existence, and likewise blackness, motion, and essence (dhat) - as we established before this in the exposition of their sayings. Then the power of the agent does not relate except to existence, and it has no relation to thingness (al-shay'iyya). It is not a motion, nor blackness, nor substance, nor essence, nor entity, because these descriptions were established in pre-eternity. Then existence is not a meaning beyond the essence, and power has no relation to the essence, so it is not conceivable that power relates to existence, since it is not a meaning beyond the essence. Thus, power relates to nothing whatsoever - neither the eternal power nor the originated power relates to any object of power (maqdur) at all. This entails the nullification of the Creator (al-Sani'), the assertion of the eternity of the world, the annulment of the establishment of action for the servants, and the nullification of command and prohibition, promise and threat. And we say: Indeed, God Almighty created the world and made that which is not black, nor white, nor substance, nor accident, nor existent - black, white, substance, accident, and existent. Then what of that which is the actions of the servants - its existence and thingness are related to the power of God Almighty, while its being motion and rest, obedience and disobedience, is related to the power of the servant. According to them (the Mu'tazila), thingness is not related to anyone's power, and existence is not a meaning...
Source pages p. 918

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila objection that the doctrine of kasb is irrational. Nasafi begins by stating that they have already shown kasb to be rational, supported by rational proofs, even if it is not something that can be imagined sensorily. He then turns the accusation back on the Mu'tazila: if they abandoned prejudice, they would see that they themselves hold irrational positions. The core of the refutation focuses on the Mu'tazila doctrine that the non-existent (al-ma'dum) is a thing (shay'), existing as an entity, accident, substance, etc., before creation. Nasafi argues that if this were true, then divine power could not relate to existence because existence is not a separate meaning from the essence, and the essence already exists in pre-eternity. Thus, power would relate to nothing, which leads to absurdities: nullifying the Creator, claiming the eternity of the world, denying human action, and invalidating religious commands and promises. Then Nasafi presents the correct position: God Almighty creates the world and brings non-existing things into existence. For the actions of servants, their existence and thingness depend on God's power, while their specific qualities (motion, rest, obedience, disobedience) are related to the servant's power. This contrasts with the Mu'tazila, who deny that any power can relate to thingness and claim existence is not a separate meaning. The passage concludes by noting that in the Mu'tazila view, thingness is not related to anyone's power.
