Refuting Compulsion: The Believer Paradox
Al-Nasafi refutes Abū al-Hudhayl's definition of compulsion using the Mu'tazila's own principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila interpretation of divine compulsion by appealing to their own principle that the believer is the agent of faith.

Core Idea
If God creates faith, He is the believer—contradicting Mu'tazila doctrine.

Al-Nasafi begins his refutation by asking a simple question: what exactly do you mean by 'will of compulsion'? He then reports that Abū al-Hudhayl defined it as God creating faith in a person without their choice. The refutation then turns the Mu'tazila's own principle against them, showing that if God is the creator of acts, He would be the doer, and thus the believer, not the servant.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the Mu'tazila definition of compulsion.
Notice Abū al-Hudhayl's interpretation: God creates faith in people without their choice, so faith exists and disbelief is repelled.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila principle about agency.
The Mu'tazila hold that the believer is the doer (fāʿil) of faith and the disbeliever the doer of disbelief. They deny that God creates acts because that would make Him the doer.
3
Apply the principle to the definition of compulsion.
If God creates faith in a person, then God is the doer of that faith, so He would be the believer, not the person. Thus the person's faith is not conceivable.
4
Reflect on the consequence for Quranic verses.
Verses like 'If He willed, He would have guided you all' would be invalid because God can only make Himself a believer, not others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عنه أن نقول : أيش تعنون بمشيئة القصر والجبر؟ فتفرقوا عند ذلك في تفسيرها، فزعم أبو الهذيل ومن تابعه أن تفسير ذلك بأن يخلق فيهم الإيمان جبرا بدون اختيارهم فيوجد فيهم الإيمان ويندفع الكفر. قيل لهم: إن من مذهبكم أن المؤمن هو فاعل الإيمان والكافر هو فاعل الكفر، ولهذا أبيتم أن يكون الله تعالى خالقًا لأفعال الخلق لأنه لو كان خالقا لكان هو المؤمن الكافر المطيع العاصي المصلي الصائم، فعلى هذا لو خلق فيهم الإيمان لكان هو المؤمن لا العباد فلا يتصور إيمانهم ولم تنفذ مشيئة فبطل قوله: ﴿فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَيْنَكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ﴾ وقوله: ﴿ وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا ﴾ إذ له قدرة جعل نفسه مؤمنًا لا قدرة جعل الكافر مؤمنًا وكذا ما اندفع عنه العجز عن جعل الكافر مؤمناً بل له القدرة على جعل نفسه مؤمنًا فلو شاء لآمن بنفسه وأتى نفسه هداها لا غير، ومن العجب العجيب أنه لو خلق في العبد إيمانا كسبا له باختياره وتعلقت قدرته به لم يكن العبد مؤمناً بل كان الله تعالى به مؤمنًا، لأنه هو الذي أوجد الإيمان ولو خلق فيه إيمانا وهدى بلا اختيار من جهة العبد ولا اكتساب ولا تعلق قدرته به لكان العبد مؤمناً، ولو كان الله تعالى أشرك المعتزلة في ربوبيته وفوض إليهم نصب أدلة دينه وعلق ذلك باختيارهم فأوجب على جميع الأمم الانقياد إليهم والرضا لصنيعهم والقبول لتحكمهم لكان الأولى بهم أن يستحيوا عن مثل هذا الكلام ونصب مثل هذا الدليل، فكيف ولم يوجد شيء من ذلك، فلما رأى الجبائي عوار هذا الكلام وتشنيع أهل الحق عليهم زعم أن تفسير مشيئة الجبر
The answer to it is that we say: What do you mean by the will of restriction and compulsion? They then differed in its interpretation. Abū al-Hudhayl and his followers claimed that its interpretation is that He creates faith in them by compulsion without their choice, so faith exists in them and disbelief is repelled. It was said to them: It is part of your doctrine that the believer is the doer of faith and the disbeliever is the doer of disbelief, and for this reason you refused that God be the creator of the acts of creatures, because if He were the creator, He would be the believer, the disbeliever, the obedient, the disobedient, the prayer, the faster. On this basis, if He created faith in them, He would be the believer, not the servants; so their faith would not be conceivable, and the will would not be effective. Thus His saying 'If He willed, He would have guided you all' and His saying 'And if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance' are invalidated, since He has the power to make Himself a believer, not the power to make the disbeliever a believer. And thus the inability to make the disbeliever a believer would not have been removed from Him; rather, He has the power to make Himself a believer. So if He willed, He would believe Himself and give His soul its guidance, no one else. And it is an amazing wonder that if He created in the servant faith as an acquisition (kasb) by his choice and his power was attached to it, the servant would not be a believer; rather, God would be a believer through it, because He is the one who brought faith into existence. And if He created in him faith and guidance without choice from the servant, without acquisition, and without attachment of his power, the servant would be a believer. And if God had made the Mu'tazila partners in His lordship and delegated to them the establishment of the proofs of His religion and made that dependent on their choice, and then obligated all nations to submit to them, to be pleased with their deeds, and to accept their rulings, they would have been more deserving of being ashamed of such speech and of setting up such a proof. So how (is it) when nothing of that has occurred? When al-Jubbā'ī saw the flaw of this speech and the rebuke of the people of truth against them, he claimed that the interpretation of the will of compulsion is...
Source pages p. 968

Commentary
This passage is the response (jawāb) to the Mu'tazila objection. The author begins by asking what they mean by 'will of compulsion' (mashīʿat al-jabr/qasr), noting that they differ in interpretation. Then he addresses the view of Abū al-Hudhayl, who said it means God creates faith in them by compulsion without choice. The author then uses the Mu'tazila's own principle against them: the Mu'tazila hold that the believer is the agent (fāʿil) of faith and the disbeliever is the agent of disbelief, and they deny that God creates acts of creatures because if He did, He would be the doer of acts like faith, disbelief, prayer, etc. Therefore, if God created faith in a person, that person would not be the believer; God would be the believer. Thus, God cannot make a disbeliever a believer; He can only make Himself a believer. So the verses that say 'if He willed, He would have guided you all' would be false if interpreted as compulsion, because God would only be guiding Himself, not others. Then the author highlights a paradox: if God created in a servant faith as an acquisition (kasb) by the servant's choice, according to Mu'tazila (who deny kasb), the servant would not be a believer because God created it. But if God created faith without any involvement of the servant, then the servant would be a believer (which is absurd). This exposes inconsistency. Next, the author uses a sarcastic rhetorical point: if God had delegated religious authority to the Mu'tazila and made people follow them, they would be ashamed of such weak arguments. Finally, he mentions that al-Jubbā'ī saw the flaw and tried a different interpretation of 'mashīʾat al-jabr' (but the text cuts off). The refutation systematically uses the Mu'tazila's own doctrines to show the impossibility of their interpretation.

Key Terms
المشيئة
الجبر
أبو الهذيل
مشيئة القصر
الفاعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila interpretation of divine compulsion (creating faith without choice) is consistent with their principles.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that it contradicts their own principle that the believer is the agent of faith.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, if God creates faith in a person by compulsion, who would be the believer?
A) The person would be a believer.
B) God would be the believer.
C) Both God and the person would be believers.
D) No one would be a believer.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila cannot claim God compels faith without violating their own tenet that humans are the agents of their actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that God could compel belief, do you secretly wish He would force your heart to obey? Examine your own desire for easy certainty versus the responsibility of free choice. Will you today consciously own your faith as your own act of worship, or blame God for your lapses?
?
The Mu'tazila avoided attributing creation of evil to God. In your own life, do you ever shy away from acknowledging God's ultimate control over your failures? How does this lesson challenge you to accept both His will and your accountability without shifting blame? What will you change about how you repent today?
?
If you were to defend the truth that humans are responsible for their actions while affirming God's all-encompassing will, could you articulate it as clearly as al-Nasafi? Spend a moment in prayer asking God to strengthen your understanding of His decree and your duty, and resolve to study this topic further.

The Paradox of Acquisition and Delegation
Al-Nasafi exposes a paradox in the Mu'tazila position and adds a rhetorical critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the paradox al-Nasafi presents about creation of faith with and without acquisition, and his sarcastic use of delegation to expose the weakness of the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila doctrine leads to absurd consequences—if God creates faith with kasb, the servant is not a believer; without kasb, the servant is a believer.

Al-Nasafi now presents a baffling paradox: if God created faith as an acquisition (kasb) within the servant, the Mu'tazila would say the servant is not the believer; but if He created it without any involvement, the servant would be a believer. This contradiction shows the incoherence of their position. He then adds a sarcastic remark about delegating authority to the Mu'tazila, and mentions that even al-Jubbā'ī saw the flaw.

Guided Path
1
Read the paradox carefully.
Al-Nasafi presents two scenarios about God creating faith in a servant and the resulting status of the servant regarding faith.
2
Identify the two scenarios and the absurd outcome.
First scenario: God creates faith as an acquisition (kasb) with the servant's choice and power attached → the servant is not a believer, God is. Second scenario: God creates faith without any involvement from the servant → the servant is a believer. This is contradictory.
3
Understand the sarcastic point about delegation.
Al-Nasafi says if God had delegated religious authority to the Mu'tazila, they would be ashamed of such weak arguments. This highlights the weakness of their position.
4
Note the mention of al-Jubbā'ī's attempted reinterpretation.
The passage ends with al-Jubbā'ī recognizing the flaw and trying a different interpretation of 'will of compulsion' (text cuts off).

Key Terms
الكسب
الاختيار
القدرة
الجبائي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates faith with acquisition (kasb), the servant is a believer.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that according to Mu'tazila principles, if God creates faith, He is the doer, so the servant is not a believer; it is God who is the believer.

Checkpoint
In the first scenario of the paradox, if God creates faith as an acquisition (kasb) by the servant's choice and with power attached, who is the believer according to al-Nasafi?
A) The servant is the believer.
B) God is the believer.
C) Both are believers.
D) Neither is a believer.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila position on compulsion leads to absurd contradictions, as shown by the paradoxical outcomes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that your faith is ultimately created by God, do you ever feel that your own efforts in worship are meaningless? Or does this truth drive you to greater reliance on His mercy? Examine your heart: do you secretly believe that your faith is something you 'acquire' through your own deeds? How would your prayer change if you truly embraced that every moment of belief is a gift from Allah?
?
The Mu'tazila were proud of their rational arguments, but al-Nasafi says they should be ashamed of their weak proofs. In what areas of your life do you trust your own reasoning more than divine revelation? Are you willing to submit to a truth that may seem paradoxical to your mind? What concrete step can you take today to humble your intellect before the word of Allah?

Refuting Abu Hashim's Concept of Mashi'at al-Jabr
Refutes Abu Hashim's definition of mashi'at al-jabr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Māturīdī position holds that necessary knowledge of punishment does not compel belief, contrary to Abu Hashim's definition of jabr.

Core Idea
Necessary knowledge does not force faith; obstinate disbelievers prove it.

Abu Hashim proposed that God's will of compulsion (mashi'at al-jabr) means He creates necessary knowledge in people that if they disbelieve, they will be punished. This lesson examines why this definition fails, using examples of obstinate disbelievers who knew their fate yet persisted in unbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on Abu Hashim's claim and the author's response.
Pay attention to the examples provided.
2
Identify Abu Hashim's definition
Identify what Abu Hashim claims is the meaning of mashi'at al-jabr: that God creates necessary knowledge of punishment for disbelief.
3
Analyze the counterexamples
Note the examples of obstinate disbelievers and Iblis. They knew their punishment but did not believe, showing that knowledge does not compel belief.
This refutes the idea that necessary knowledge forces faith.
4
Connect to the learning objective
Understand that the Māturīdī position distinguishes between knowledge and volition; thus, jabr cannot be reduced to necessary knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ابنه أبو هاشم فساد كلام أبيه زعم أن معنى مشيئة الجبران أن يخلق الله تعالى لهم العلم الضروري أنهم لو لم يؤمنوا لعذبوا عذابًا شديدا. وهذا أيضا فاسد لأن أهل العناد كانوا يعلمون أنهم يخلدون في النار بتكذيبه عليه السلام وما كانوا يؤمنون، وإبليس يعلم بذلك ولا يؤمن، فكذا من قامت له الدلائل الموجبة للعلم أو الذي خلق له العلم الضروري يعلم بذلك ولا يؤمن. ثم المذهب عنده أن الله تعالى يقدر على الظلم والسفه والكذب، ولو فعل شيئًا من ذلك لبطلت ألوهيته، ولا ضرر أعظم من زوال الربوبية وصيرورته عبدًا مربوبًا معاقبًا وهو يعلم أنه لو ظلم أو كذب أو سفه لتزول ربوبيته فكان على قضية كلامه مجبوراً على العدل والصدق والحكمة.
His son Abu Hashim [declared] the corruption of his father's statement, claiming that the meaning of the will of compulsion (mashi'at al-jabr) is that Allah the Exalted creates for them necessary knowledge that if they did not believe, they would be severely punished. This too is corrupt, because the people of obstinacy knew that they would abide eternally in the Fire for denying him (peace be upon him), yet they would not believe; and Iblis knows that and does not believe. Likewise, one for whom evidential proofs necessitating knowledge are established, or one for whom necessary knowledge is created, knows that and does not believe. Then, according to him, the doctrine is that Allah the Exalted has power over injustice, foolishness, and falsehood; and if He did any of that, His divinity would be nullified. There is no greater harm than the removal of lordship and His becoming a subjugated, punished servant, while He knows that if He did injustice, falsehood, or foolishness, His lordship would cease. So, according to the implication of his statement, He would be compelled (majburan) to justice, truthfulness, and wisdom.
Source pages p. 970

Commentary
This passage refutes the Mu'tazilī position attributed to Abu Hashim regarding the meaning of 'mashi'at al-jabr' (the will of compulsion). Abu Hashim claimed that God's willing compulsion means He creates necessary knowledge in people that if they do not believe, they will be severely punished. The author rejects this by pointing out that the obstinate disbelievers and Iblis already knew they would be punished yet did not believe; thus, necessary knowledge does not compel faith. Then the author criticizes Abu Hashim's related view that God has power over injustice, foolishness, and falsehood. He argues that if God could do such things, His divinity would be nullified, and since God knows this, He would be compelled to act justly, truthfully, and wisely. This would impose a constraint on God, which is absurd. The argument highlights that the Mu'tazilī position leads to logically untenable consequences.

Key Terms
مشيئة الجبر (mashi'at al-jabr)
العلم الضروري (al-'ilm al-daruri)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abu Hashim claimed that 'jabr' means God creates necessary knowledge that forces belief.
Correction: The Māturīdī position holds that necessary knowledge does not compel belief; obstinate disbelievers knew their punishment yet did not believe.

Checkpoint
What invalidates Abu Hashim's concept of mashi'at al-jabr?
A) It contradicts the Quranic verses on compulsion.
B) It is based on a weak hadith.
C) The example of obstinate disbelievers and Iblis shows that necessary knowledge does not force belief.
D) It denies human free will entirely.

Key Takeaway
Necessary knowledge of punishment does not compel belief; therefore, Abu Hashim's definition of jabr is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself knowing a truth about Allah or your religion but still hesitating to act on it? What is the area of your life where your knowledge has not yet translated into obedience? How will you confront that obstinacy today?
?
Iblis knew his punishment and still refused to submit. Is there any sin or attitude you cling to despite knowing its consequences? What would it cost you to let it go right now?
?
This passage shows that necessary knowledge does not force belief. What does this say about the condition of your heart? Are you banking on your knowledge alone to save you, or are you actively choosing faith and submission every moment?

Refuting the Implication of God Being Compelled to Justice
Refutes the idea that God is compelled to justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that God has power over injustice leads to the absurd conclusion that God would be compelled to act justly.

Core Idea
If God could do injustice, His divinity would cease; thus He cannot be compelled.

Abu Hashim's position also held that God has power over injustice, falsehood, and foolishness, but if He did so, His divinity would be nullified. This lesson explores why this reasoning forces God into compulsion, which is unacceptable in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the second part of the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the logical implications.
Notice the sequence: power to do injustice → divinity nullified → compulsion.
2
Understand Abu Hashim's claim
Abu Hashim asserts that God has power over injustice, falsehood, and foolishness, but if He did any, His divinity would cease.
This is a key point of contention.
3
Identify the logical consequence
The author argues that since God knows He would lose divinity by doing injustice, He must avoid it, making Him compelled to justice.
This leads to the absurdity of a compelled God.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Understand that this argument exposes a contradiction: asserting God's power over evil while making His divinity dependent on not doing it, resulting in external constraint.

The Dilemma of Power After Certain Knowledge
Dilemma about power of disbelief after necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma regarding whether power of disbelief remains after certain knowledge of faith, and how this undermines the concept of compulsion (jabr).

Core Idea
Either power remains, making compulsion incomplete, or it does not, making command and punishment unjust.

The author begins by posing a critical question to the proponents of jabr: after God creates necessary knowledge of faith or punishment, does the power to disbelieve remain? This question exposes a fundamental flaw in their reasoning. By analyzing the two possible answers, we see how the dilemma forces the opponent into an untenable position.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the two possible answers and the objections that follow each.
The passage uses a conditional structure: 'if he says no... if he says yes'.
2
Analyze the 'no' scenario
If they say power of disbelief is removed, the author objects: how can one be commanded to abandon what he cannot do, and how can he be punished for it?
This shows that jabr leads to absurdities in divine command and justice.
3
Analyze the 'yes' scenario
If they say power remains, then disbelief is still possible, so the alleged compulsion fails—the person could still choose disbelief.
Thus, jabr is self-contradictory.
4
Synthesize the argument
Reflect on how this dilemma invalidates the Mu'tazilī claim that human actions are fully compelled.
The author leaves the opponent with no coherent option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال له ولأبيه: هل بقيت معه قدرة الكفر بعد العلم الضروري بصحة الإيمان أو العلم أنه يعاقب؟ فإن قال: لا، قيل: كيف يؤمر بترك كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ وكيف يؤمر بالإيمان بدون القدرة إذ لو كانت قدرة الإيمان موجودة لكانت هي بعينها قدرة الكفر؟ وكيف يعاقب على كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ فإن قال : نعم. قيل : إذا كنت قدرة الكفر موجودة كان من الجائز أن يكفر بها ولا يؤمن. ثم الذي يبطل جميع تأويلاتهم أن الله تعالى قال : وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا وَلَكِن حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِنِّي لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ أخبر أنه تعالى لم يأت كل نفس هداها لما أن حق القول منه لأملأن جهنم ولو أتى كل نفس هداها لم يتصور أن يملأ جهنم بهم لأن المهتدي لا يملأ به جهنم، وإعطاء الهدى بطريق الجبر على الطرق التي زعموا لا يخرجهم من استحقاقهم جهنم، وأن يملأ منهم جهنم، فدل أن هذا باطل. يحققه أن لو شاء إيمانهم بطريق الجبر على ما زعموا وحصل إيمانهم لما كان ذلك الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا هو الإيمان الذي شاء الله منهم؛ لأنه على زعمهم شاء منهم الإيمان الاختياري الذي يصيرون به مستحقين للجنة والثواب خارجين عن أن يكونوا أهلا للعقاب، وما يحصل من الإيمان بمشيئة الجبر لا يكون هذا الإيمان فإن العبد لا يصير به أهلاً للجنة والثواب ولا يخرج عن استحقاق العقاب على طريق التخليد، فإذا لم يبق قادرًا على تحصيل ما أراد في ملكه وغلبت مشيئته مشيئة إبليس وإرادة كل كافر، ولأنه لا معنى لتعلق الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا بالمشيئة والإخبار أنه لو شاء لفعل لأنه قد فعل ذلك وحصل من كل كافر إذ كل كافر وكل مخلوق يشهد بخلقه أن له صانعا حكيمًا عليمًا موصوفا بصفات الكمال متبرئًا عن سمات النقص لا يؤيد بالمعجزة الكاذب، ولا يقيم دلالة الصدق على دعوى المفتري، فكان على هذا كل مخلوق مؤمنًا بخلقته، وقد شاء الله تعالى ذلك وفعل لا معنى لقوله : (وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ ) وقوله : ( وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَا نَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفِيس هُدَنهَا ) وقد فعل ذلك فدل أن المراد من الآية ليس هو الإيمان الحاصل جبرا بل إيمانهم الاختياري، وقد صح في المروي عن النبي عليه السلام أنه كان يقول : "ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن" وكذا هذه اللفظة متداولة على ألسنة
Then it is said to him and to his father: Did the power of disbelief (qudrat al-kufr) remain with him after the necessary knowledge (al-'ilm al-daruri) of the truth of faith, or after the knowledge that he will be punished? If he says: No, it is said: How can he be commanded to abandon a disbelief over which he has no power? And how can he be commanded to believe without power, since if the power of faith existed, it would itself be the power of disbelief? And how can he be punished for a disbelief over which he has no power? If he says: Yes, it is said: If the power of disbelief exists, then it is possible that he disbelieves by it and does not believe. Then that which invalidates all their interpretations is that Allah the Exalted said: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance, but the word from Me will be fulfilled: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together.' He informed that He the Exalted did not give every soul its guidance because the word from Him is 'I will surely fill Hell.' And if He gave every soul its guidance, it would be inconceivable to fill Hell with them because the guided one does not fill Hell. And giving guidance by way of compulsion (jabr) according to the ways they claimed does not remove them from deserving Hell, nor from filling Hell with them. So this shows that [their view] is false. He confirms it: that if He had willed their faith by way of compulsion as they claimed, and their faith occurred, then that faith occurring by compulsion would not be the faith that Allah willed from them. Because according to their claim, He willed from them voluntary faith (al-iman al-ikhtiyari) by which they become deserving of Paradise and reward, exiting from being worthy of punishment. And what occurs of faith by the will of compulsion is not this faith; for the servant does not become deserving of Paradise and reward by it, nor does he exit from deserving punishment in the way of eternal [punishment]. Thus He would not remain capable of achieving what He desired in His kingdom, and His will would be overcome by the will of Iblis and the will of every disbeliever. And because there is no meaning to attaching the faith that occurs by compulsion to the will and the report that if He willed He would do it, since He has already done that and it occurred from every disbeliever. For every disbeliever and every creature witnesses by its creation that it has a wise, knowing Creator described with attributes of perfection, free from marks of deficiency, who does not support a liar with a miracle, nor establish evidence of truth for a fabricator's claim. Thus, on this basis, every creature would be a believer by its creation, and Allah the Exalted has willed that and done it. Then there would be no meaning to His saying: 'And if your Lord had willed, all who are on earth would have believed,' and His saying: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance.' And He has done that. So this indicates that the intended meaning of the verse is not faith occurring by compulsion, but rather their voluntary faith. And it is established in what is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to say: 'Whatever Allah wills occurs, and whatever He does not will does not occur.' And likewise this phrase is common on tongues...
Source pages p. 970

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of the Mu'tazilī view on 'jabr' (compulsion) by presenting an objection-and-answer and then a scriptural argument. The author poses a question to Abu Hashim and his father: after necessary knowledge of faith or punishment is created, does the power (qudra) to disbelieve remain? Two possible answers are considered. If they say 'no', then the author objects: how can one be commanded to abandon disbelief or to believe if he lacks the power? Furthermore, punishment for an act over which one has no power would be unjust. If they say 'yes', the power to disbelieve remains, then disbelief is still possible, so the alleged compulsion fails. The author then provides the ultimate scriptural refutation: Quran 32:13 (and 10:99) states that if God had willed, He would have guided every soul, but He did not do so because He decreed to fill Hell. If He had compelled guidance, they would not deserve Hell. The logic shows that God wills voluntary faith, not compelled faith. He further clarifies that compelled faith would not be the faith God intended, which is voluntary and deserving of reward. If God compelled faith, He would not be able to fill Hell as He decreed, and His will would be overcome by Satan's will—an impossibility. Moreover, since every creature already has innate knowledge of God (fitra), if that were sufficient faith, all would be believers, making the verses meaningless. Thus, the verses must refer to voluntary faith. Finally, the hadith 'Whatever Allah wills occurs…' is cited to affirm God's absolute will, but it does not imply compulsion; it is a general statement of divine sovereignty.

Key Terms
قدرة (qudra)
العلم الضروري (al-'ilm al-daruri)
الكفر (al-kufr)
الإيمان (al-iman)
الجبر (al-jabr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that after God creates necessary faith, the person has no power to disbelieve, yet still deserves punishment for disbelief.
Correction: The passage argues that if the power is removed, command and punishment become meaningless, proving that the person must retain power for accountability.

Checkpoint
What is the first objection raised if the opponent says the power of disbelief is removed?
A) The person cannot be blamed for disbelief.
B) How can the person be commanded to abandon a disbelief over which he has no power?
C) The power of faith must be different.
D) The verses contradict each other.

Key Takeaway
The dilemma exposes that jabr cannot be defended without falling into absurdities regarding divine command and justice.

Refuting Jabr with Quran and Hadith
Scriptural proof and explanation distinguishing voluntary and compelled faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 32:13 and the hadith 'ma sha' Allahu kana' disprove the theory of compulsion (jabr) by showing that God wills voluntary, not compelled, faith.

Core Idea
God's will for faith is voluntary faith, not compelled faith that nullifies reward and punishment.

After dismantling the logical basis of jabr, the author now turns to scriptural evidence. The verse 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance' (32:13) is used to show that God did not compel belief, otherwise His decree to fill Hell would be impossible. The author further explains that compelled faith would not be the faith God intends—a faith that deserves reward—and concludes with the prophetic hadith affirming God's absolute will, which the proponents misinterpret.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic proof passage
Read the Arabic from 'ثم الذي يبطل جميع تأويلاتهم' to the end, focusing on how the verse is used as a refutation.
The verse is cited and then logically unpacked.
2
Analyze the logic of the verse
Notice that God states if He willed, He would guide all, but He did not because He intends to fill Hell. If He compelled guidance, no one would be in Hell.
This shows that jabr contradicts God's own decree.
3
Distinguish voluntary vs compelled faith
The author argues that compelled faith would not be the faith that merits reward or removes punishment; thus, the verses must refer to voluntary faith.
This is the core theological point.
4
Examine the hadith
The hadith 'Whatever Allah wills occurs…' is cited, but the author implies it does not justify jabr; it affirms God's power, not the quality of human action.
The common misunderstanding is to read jabr into this hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال له ولأبيه: هل بقيت معه قدرة الكفر بعد العلم الضروري بصحة الإيمان أو العلم أنه يعاقب؟ فإن قال: لا، قيل: كيف يؤمر بترك كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ وكيف يؤمر بالإيمان بدون القدرة إذ لو كانت قدرة الإيمان موجودة لكانت هي بعينها قدرة الكفر؟ وكيف يعاقب على كفر لا قدرة له عليه؟ فإن قال : نعم. قيل : إذا كنت قدرة الكفر موجودة كان من الجائز أن يكفر بها ولا يؤمن. ثم الذي يبطل جميع تأويلاتهم أن الله تعالى قال : وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا وَلَكِن حَقَّ الْقَوْلُ مِنِّي لَأَمْلَأَنَّ جَهَنَّمَ مِنَ الْجِنَّةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ أخبر أنه تعالى لم يأت كل نفس هداها لما أن حق القول منه لأملأن جهنم ولو أتى كل نفس هداها لم يتصور أن يملأ جهنم بهم لأن المهتدي لا يملأ به جهنم، وإعطاء الهدى بطريق الجبر على الطرق التي زعموا لا يخرجهم من استحقاقهم جهنم، وأن يملأ منهم جهنم، فدل أن هذا باطل. يحققه أن لو شاء إيمانهم بطريق الجبر على ما زعموا وحصل إيمانهم لما كان ذلك الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا هو الإيمان الذي شاء الله منهم؛ لأنه على زعمهم شاء منهم الإيمان الاختياري الذي يصيرون به مستحقين للجنة والثواب خارجين عن أن يكونوا أهلا للعقاب، وما يحصل من الإيمان بمشيئة الجبر لا يكون هذا الإيمان فإن العبد لا يصير به أهلاً للجنة والثواب ولا يخرج عن استحقاق العقاب على طريق التخليد، فإذا لم يبق قادرًا على تحصيل ما أراد في ملكه وغلبت مشيئته مشيئة إبليس وإرادة كل كافر، ولأنه لا معنى لتعلق الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا بالمشيئة والإخبار أنه لو شاء لفعل لأنه قد فعل ذلك وحصل من كل كافر إذ كل كافر وكل مخلوق يشهد بخلقه أن له صانعا حكيمًا عليمًا موصوفا بصفات الكمال متبرئًا عن سمات النقص لا يؤيد بالمعجزة الكاذب، ولا يقيم دلالة الصدق على دعوى المفتري، فكان على هذا كل مخلوق مؤمنًا بخلقته، وقد شاء الله تعالى ذلك وفعل لا معنى لقوله : (وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ ) وقوله : ( وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَا نَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفِيس هُدَنهَا ) وقد فعل ذلك فدل أن المراد من الآية ليس هو الإيمان الحاصل جبرا بل إيمانهم الاختياري، وقد صح في المروي عن النبي عليه السلام أنه كان يقول : "ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن" وكذا هذه اللفظة متداولة على ألسنة
Then it is said to him and to his father: Did the power of disbelief (qudrat al-kufr) remain with him after the necessary knowledge (al-'ilm al-daruri) of the truth of faith, or after the knowledge that he will be punished? If he says: No, it is said: How can he be commanded to abandon a disbelief over which he has no power? And how can he be commanded to believe without power, since if the power of faith existed, it would itself be the power of disbelief? And how can he be punished for a disbelief over which he has no power? If he says: Yes, it is said: If the power of disbelief exists, then it is possible that he disbelieves by it and does not believe. Then that which invalidates all their interpretations is that Allah the Exalted said: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance, but the word from Me will be fulfilled: I will surely fill Hell with jinn and people all together.' He informed that He the Exalted did not give every soul its guidance because the word from Him is 'I will surely fill Hell.' And if He gave every soul its guidance, it would be inconceivable to fill Hell with them because the guided one does not fill Hell. And giving guidance by way of compulsion (jabr) according to the ways they claimed does not remove them from deserving Hell, nor from filling Hell with them. So this shows that [their view] is false. He confirms it: that if He had willed their faith by way of compulsion as they claimed, and their faith occurred, then that faith occurring by compulsion would not be the faith that Allah willed from them. Because according to their claim, He willed from them voluntary faith (al-iman al-ikhtiyari) by which they become deserving of Paradise and reward, exiting from being worthy of punishment. And what occurs of faith by the will of compulsion is not this faith; for the servant does not become deserving of Paradise and reward by it, nor does he exit from deserving punishment in the way of eternal [punishment]. Thus He would not remain capable of achieving what He desired in His kingdom, and His will would be overcome by the will of Iblis and the will of every disbeliever. And because there is no meaning to attaching the faith that occurs by compulsion to the will and the report that if He willed He would do it, since He has already done that and it occurred from every disbeliever. For every disbeliever and every creature witnesses by its creation that it has a wise, knowing Creator described with attributes of perfection, free from marks of deficiency, who does not support a liar with a miracle, nor establish evidence of truth for a fabricator's claim. Thus, on this basis, every creature would be a believer by its creation, and Allah the Exalted has willed that and done it. Then there would be no meaning to His saying: 'And if your Lord had willed, all who are on earth would have believed,' and His saying: 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance.' And He has done that. So this indicates that the intended meaning of the verse is not faith occurring by compulsion, but rather their voluntary faith. And it is established in what is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to say: 'Whatever Allah wills occurs, and whatever He does not will does not occur.' And likewise this phrase is common on tongues...
Source pages p. 970

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of the Mu'tazilī view on 'jabr' (compulsion) by presenting an objection-and-answer and then a scriptural argument. The author poses a question to Abu Hashim and his father: after necessary knowledge of faith or punishment is created, does the power (qudra) to disbelieve remain? Two possible answers are considered. If they say 'no', then the author objects: how can one be commanded to abandon disbelief or to believe if he lacks the power? Furthermore, punishment for an act over which one has no power would be unjust. If they say 'yes', the power to disbelieve remains, then disbelief is still possible, so the alleged compulsion fails. The author then provides the ultimate scriptural refutation: Quran 32:13 (and 10:99) states that if God had willed, He would have guided every soul, but He did not do so because He decreed to fill Hell. If He had compelled guidance, they would not deserve Hell. The logic shows that God wills voluntary faith, not compelled faith. He further clarifies that compelled faith would not be the faith God intended, which is voluntary and deserving of reward. If God compelled faith, He would not be able to fill Hell as He decreed, and His will would be overcome by Satan's will—an impossibility. Moreover, since every creature already has innate knowledge of God (fitra), if that were sufficient faith, all would be believers, making the verses meaningless. Thus, the verses must refer to voluntary faith. Finally, the hadith 'Whatever Allah wills occurs…' is cited to affirm God's absolute will, but it does not imply compulsion; it is a general statement of divine sovereignty.

Key Terms
الهدى (al-huda)
الاستحقاق (al-istihqaq)
الإيمان الاختياري (al-iman al-ikhtiyari)
الإيمان الجبري (al-iman al-jabri)
مشيئة (mashi'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the hadith 'ma sha' Allahu kana' means God compels all human actions, including faith and disbelief.
Correction: The hadith only affirms God's ultimate will and power; it does not specify the nature of human action. The passage shows that God wills voluntary faith, and compelled faith would not achieve His purpose.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the Quranic verse 'And if We had willed, We would have given every soul its guidance' actually refute jabr?
A) Because it shows God can do whatever He wills.
B) Because if He compelled guidance, He could not fulfill His promise to fill Hell.
C) Because the verse is abrogated.
D) Because the verse applies only to prophets.

Key Takeaway
Quran 32:13 and the hadith 'ma sha' Allahu kana' support voluntary faith, not compelled faith, because compelled faith nullifies the divine purpose of reward and punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat your own faith as a voluntary act that you are responsible for, or do you sometimes blame 'qadar' for your spiritual laziness? What would change if you fully owned your choices before Allah today?
?
When you recite 'ma sha' Allahu kana,' do you use it to surrender to Allah's will in hardship, or to avoid taking responsibility for sins you could have avoided? Which of these does this lesson call you to?
?
If you truly believed that Allah wills your voluntary faith and not a forced one, would you still make excuses for the sins you commit? What one step can you take today to prove that your iman is a free choice?

5 min
Forced Faith Is Not the Desired Faith
Al-Nasafi argues that forced faith cannot be the desired faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why faith by compulsion cannot be the faith that God requires from people, because it does not make one deserving of Paradise.

Core Idea
Faith that is forced cannot be the faith that leads to Paradise.

Imam al-Nasafi begins refuting the Jabriyya claim that God's will for faith is coercive. He argues that if faith were forced, it would not fulfill the purpose of deserving reward. This lesson examines his first key argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author first states a conclusion (guided one does not fill Hell) and then verifies it with logical reasoning.
The author uses the phrase 'yuḥaqqiquhu' (he verifies it) to mark the core reasoning.
2
Identify the two types of faith
The passage contrasts 'faith by compulsion' (īmān jabrī) and 'voluntary faith' (īmān ikhtiyārī). Note the different consequences of each: one leads to Paradise, the other does not.
3
Understand the main claim
The core claim is that faith occurring by compulsion would not be the faith God willed from people. Ask yourself: why not? The answer is because it does not make the servant deserving of reward.
This is the key point to remember.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن المهتدي لا يملأ به جهنم، وإعطاء الهدى بطريق الجبر على الطرق التي زعموا لا يخرجهم من استحقاقهم جهنم، وأن يملأ منهم جهنم، فدل أن هذا باطل.
يحققه أن لو شاء إيمانهم بطريق الجبر على ما زعموا وحصل إيمانهم لما كان ذلك الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا هو الإيمان الذي شاء الله منهم؛ لأنه على زعمهم شاء منهم الإيمان الاختياري الذي يصيرون به مستحقين للجنة والثواب خارجين عن أن يكونوا أهلا للعقاب، وما يحصل من الإيمان بمشيئة الجبر لا يكون هذا الإيمان فإن العبد لا يصير به أهلاً للجنة والثواب ولا يخرج عن استحقاق العقاب على طريق التخليد، فإذا لم يبق قادرًا على تحصيل ما أراد في ملكه وغلبت مشيئته مشيئة إبليس وإرادة كل كافر، ولأنه لا معنى لتعلق الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا بالمشيئة والإخبار أنه لو شاء لفعل لأنه قد فعل ذلك وحصل من كل كافر إذ كل كافر وكل مخلوق يشهد بخلقه أن له صانعا حكيمًا عليمًا موصوفا بصفات الكمال متبرئًا عن سمات النقص لا يؤيد بالمعجزة الكاذب، ولا يقيم دلالة الصدق على دعوى المفتري، فكان على هذا كل مخلوق مؤمنًا بخلقته، وقد شاء الله تعالى ذلك وفعل لا معنى لقوله : (وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ ) وقوله : ( وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا ﴾ ، وقد فعل ذلك فدل أن المراد من الآية ليس هو الإيمان الحاصل جبرا بل إيمانهم الاختياري، وقد صح في المروي عن النبي عليه السلام أنه كان يقول : "ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن" وكذا هذه اللفظة متداولة على ألسنة الأمة ولا وجه لحملها على مشيئة الجبر ؛ لأنه لو استقام بأحد شطري الكلام لم يستقم بالشطر الآخر فإنه إن أمكن أن يقال : ما شاء الله جبراً كأن لم يمكن أن يقال وما لم يشأ جبرًا لم يكن، لأن الطاعات كلها عندكم لم يشأ جبرًا وكانت والمعاصي لم يشأ جبرًا، وقد كانت فدل أن المراد من المشيئة غير مشيئة الجبر.
Because the guided one does not fill Hell with them, and giving guidance by way of compulsion (jabr) in the ways they claimed does not remove them from their being deserving of Hell, and that they would fill Hell from them, so it indicates that this is false. He verifies it: If He willed their faith by way of compulsion as they claimed and their faith occurred, that faith occurring by compulsion would not be the faith that God willed from them; because according to their claim He willed from them the voluntary faith (al-īmān al-ikhtiyārī) by which they become deserving of Paradise and reward, exiting from being worthy of punishment. And what occurs of faith by the will of compulsion is not this faith, for the servant does not become by it deserving of Paradise and reward nor does he exit from deserving of punishment in the way of eternal (punishment). So when He is not able to accomplish what He willed in His kingdom, and His will is overcome by the will of Iblis and the will of every disbeliever. And because there is no meaning to the attachment of faith occurring by compulsion to the will and the information that if He willed He would do it, since He has done that and it has occurred from every disbeliever, for every disbeliever and every creature bears witness by his creation that he has a wise, knowing Creator described with attributes of perfection, free from characteristics of deficiency, who does not support the liar with a miracle, nor establish an evidence of truth upon the claim of the fabricator. So on this basis every creature would be a believer by his very creation, and God has willed that and done it. There would be no meaning to His saying: (And if your Lord had willed, all those on earth would have believed) and His saying: (And if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance), and He has done that. So it indicates that the intended meaning of the verse is not faith occurring by compulsion, but rather their voluntary faith. And it is authentically reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he used to say: 'What God wills is, and what He does not will is not.' And this phrase is current on the tongues of the community, and there is no way to interpret it as the will of compulsion; because if it were valid for one part of the statement, it would not be valid for the other part. For if it were possible to say: 'What God wills by compulsion is,' it would not be possible to say: 'What He does not will by compulsion is not,' because according to you all acts of obedience were not willed by compulsion, yet they existed, and acts of disobedience were not willed by compulsion, yet they existed. So it indicates that the intended meaning of will is other than the will of compulsion.
Source pages p. 971

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Jabriyya interpretation of divine will concerning faith. The author argues that if God had willed faith by coercion (jabr), that faith would not be the faith God actually wants from people, which is voluntary faith (ikhtiyārī) that makes one deserving of Paradise and reward. He points out that forced faith does not remove the servant from deserving eternal punishment. He then argues that if God were unable to accomplish what He willed in His kingdom, His will would be overcome by the will of Iblis and every disbeliever, which is impossible. He also notes that every creature naturally knows his Creator, so if faith were coerced, everyone would be a believer, making verses like 'If your Lord had willed, all would have believed' meaningless because God has done that (given natural knowledge) yet many disbelieve. Therefore the intended meaning is voluntary faith. He then cites the famous hadith 'What God wills is, and what He does not will is not' and argues that it cannot be understood as the will of compulsion, because if it were, the second part 'what He does not will is not' would be false: acts of obedience and disobedience both exist even though God did not will them by coercion. Hence the will in that phrase is the divine will in a different sense, not the will of compulsion.

Key Terms
إيمان جبري
إيمان اختياري
استحقاق الجنة
استحقاق العقاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that God's will for faith is coercive, so if He wills faith, He forces it and the person becomes deserving of Paradise.
Correction: Imam al-Nasafi shows that forced faith does not make one deserving of Paradise or remove one from deserving punishment, so it cannot be the faith God wills.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the faith that occurs by compulsion (jabr) NOT do?
A) It makes the servant deserving of Paradise.
B) It removes the servant from deserving eternal punishment.
C) Both A and B.
D) It fulfills God's will.

Key Takeaway
Faith that is forced does not make one deserving of Paradise, so it cannot be the faith God wills from humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered your own faith as something forced upon you by upbringing or environment? What does this lesson say about the value of such faith? How can you move towards a more voluntary, heartfelt faith?
?
This lesson teaches that forced faith does not save. Are there areas in your life where you rely on external compliance rather than inner conviction? What specific step can you take today to make your faith more voluntary and sincere?
?
The Jabriyya thought that whatever happens is God's will and thus salvation is predetermined. Do you ever feel fatalistic about your spiritual state? How does this passage challenge you to take responsibility for your faith?

Refuting the Jabriyya Interpretation of Divine Will
Al-Nasafi refutes Jabriyya with logical, scriptural, and hadith arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi refutes the Jabriyya interpretation of divine will using the impossibility of God's will being overcome and the implications of natural knowledge of God.

Core Idea
If God's will were coercive, it would be overcome by others, making divine will weak.

Imam al-Nasafi continues his refutation by showing the logical consequences of the Jabriyya view. He argues that if divine will were coercive, God would be unable to accomplish His will, and the verses about faith would become meaningless. This lesson explores these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify each argument
The passage contains three distinct arguments: (1) God's inability to achieve His will, (2) natural knowledge of God making everyone a believer, (3) the hadith about divine will. Identify each one.
The author uses 'fa-idhā' (so when) to introduce a new point.
2
Examine the first argument
The author argues that if faith were coerced, God would be unable to accomplish His will, and His will would be overcome by Iblis and disbelievers. This is impossible for God.
3
Examine the second argument
Every creature has innate knowledge of God (fitra). If faith were forced, everyone would believe, making verses like 'if your Lord had willed, all would have believed' meaningless, because God has given that knowledge yet many disbelieve.
This shows that the intended meaning is voluntary faith.
4
Examine the third argument
The hadith 'What God wills is, and what He does not will is not' cannot refer to coercive will because then the second part would be false: acts of obedience and disobedience exist even though God did not will them by coercion.
Thus the will in the hadith is a different kind of will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن المهتدي لا يملأ به جهنم، وإعطاء الهدى بطريق الجبر على الطرق التي زعموا لا يخرجهم من استحقاقهم جهنم، وأن يملأ منهم جهنم، فدل أن هذا باطل.
يحققه أن لو شاء إيمانهم بطريق الجبر على ما زعموا وحصل إيمانهم لما كان ذلك الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا هو الإيمان الذي شاء الله منهم؛ لأنه على زعمهم شاء منهم الإيمان الاختياري الذي يصيرون به مستحقين للجنة والثواب خارجين عن أن يكونوا أهلا للعقاب، وما يحصل من الإيمان بمشيئة الجبر لا يكون هذا الإيمان فإن العبد لا يصير به أهلاً للجنة والثواب ولا يخرج عن استحقاق العقاب على طريق التخليد، فإذا لم يبق قادرًا على تحصيل ما أراد في ملكه وغلبت مشيئته مشيئة إبليس وإرادة كل كافر، ولأنه لا معنى لتعلق الإيمان الحاصل جبرًا بالمشيئة والإخبار أنه لو شاء لفعل لأنه قد فعل ذلك وحصل من كل كافر إذ كل كافر وكل مخلوق يشهد بخلقه أن له صانعا حكيمًا عليمًا موصوفا بصفات الكمال متبرئًا عن سمات النقص لا يؤيد بالمعجزة الكاذب، ولا يقيم دلالة الصدق على دعوى المفتري، فكان على هذا كل مخلوق مؤمنًا بخلقته، وقد شاء الله تعالى ذلك وفعل لا معنى لقوله : (وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ ) وقوله : ( وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا ﴾ ، وقد فعل ذلك فدل أن المراد من الآية ليس هو الإيمان الحاصل جبرا بل إيمانهم الاختياري، وقد صح في المروي عن النبي عليه السلام أنه كان يقول : "ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن" وكذا هذه اللفظة متداولة على ألسنة الأمة ولا وجه لحملها على مشيئة الجبر ؛ لأنه لو استقام بأحد شطري الكلام لم يستقم بالشطر الآخر فإنه إن أمكن أن يقال : ما شاء الله جبراً كأن لم يمكن أن يقال وما لم يشأ جبرًا لم يكن، لأن الطاعات كلها عندكم لم يشأ جبرًا وكانت والمعاصي لم يشأ جبرًا، وقد كانت فدل أن المراد من المشيئة غير مشيئة الجبر.
Because the guided one does not fill Hell with them, and giving guidance by way of compulsion (jabr) in the ways they claimed does not remove them from their being deserving of Hell, and that they would fill Hell from them, so it indicates that this is false. He verifies it: If He willed their faith by way of compulsion as they claimed and their faith occurred, that faith occurring by compulsion would not be the faith that God willed from them; because according to their claim He willed from them the voluntary faith (al-īmān al-ikhtiyārī) by which they become deserving of Paradise and reward, exiting from being worthy of punishment. And what occurs of faith by the will of compulsion is not this faith, for the servant does not become by it deserving of Paradise and reward nor does he exit from deserving of punishment in the way of eternal (punishment). So when He is not able to accomplish what He willed in His kingdom, and His will is overcome by the will of Iblis and the will of every disbeliever. And because there is no meaning to the attachment of faith occurring by compulsion to the will and the information that if He willed He would do it, since He has done that and it has occurred from every disbeliever, for every disbeliever and every creature bears witness by his creation that he has a wise, knowing Creator described with attributes of perfection, free from characteristics of deficiency, who does not support the liar with a miracle, nor establish an evidence of truth upon the claim of the fabricator. So on this basis every creature would be a believer by his very creation, and God has willed that and done it. There would be no meaning to His saying: (And if your Lord had willed, all those on earth would have believed) and His saying: (And if We willed, We would give every soul its guidance), and He has done that. So it indicates that the intended meaning of the verse is not faith occurring by compulsion, but rather their voluntary faith. And it is authentically reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he used to say: 'What God wills is, and what He does not will is not.' And this phrase is current on the tongues of the community, and there is no way to interpret it as the will of compulsion; because if it were valid for one part of the statement, it would not be valid for the other part. For if it were possible to say: 'What God wills by compulsion is,' it would not be possible to say: 'What He does not will by compulsion is not,' because according to you all acts of obedience were not willed by compulsion, yet they existed, and acts of disobedience were not willed by compulsion, yet they existed. So it indicates that the intended meaning of will is other than the will of compulsion.
Source pages p. 971

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Jabriyya interpretation of divine will concerning faith. The author argues that if God had willed faith by coercion (jabr), that faith would not be the faith God actually wants from people, which is voluntary faith (ikhtiyārī) that makes one deserving of Paradise and reward. He points out that forced faith does not remove the servant from deserving eternal punishment. He then argues that if God were unable to accomplish what He willed in His kingdom, His will would be overcome by the will of Iblis and every disbeliever, which is impossible. He also notes that every creature naturally knows his Creator, so if faith were coerced, everyone would be a believer, making verses like 'If your Lord had willed, all would have believed' meaningless because God has done that (given natural knowledge) yet many disbelieve. Therefore the intended meaning is voluntary faith. He then cites the famous hadith 'What God wills is, and what He does not will is not' and argues that it cannot be understood as the will of compulsion, because if it were, the second part 'what He does not will is not' would be false: acts of obedience and disobedience both exist even though God did not will them by coercion. Hence the will in that phrase is the divine will in a different sense, not the will of compulsion.

Key Terms
مشيئة الجبر
الهدى
إيمان اختياري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret the hadith 'What God wills is...' as referring to coercive will that forces all actions.
Correction: Imam al-Nasafi shows that if it meant coercive will, acts of obedience and disobedience would not exist, which is false. Therefore the hadith refers to a different kind of divine will.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would be the consequence if every creature's natural knowledge of God were sufficient for faith by compulsion?
A) Everyone would be a believer, making certain verses meaningless.
B) Disbelievers would still exist, but they would be punished.
C) God's will would be fulfilled exactly as the Jabriyya claim.
D) The hadith would be confirmed.

Key Takeaway
Divine will cannot be coercive, otherwise God's will would be thwarted, everyone would believe, and the hadith would be contradictory.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall into sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking 'God willed it, so it's not my fault'? How does Al-Nasafi's argument that God's will is not coercive challenge that excuse? What would it cost you to take full ownership of your choices starting today?
?
You have witnessed the signs of the Creator in your own creation and in the world. Yet you still disobey. If God's will were coercive, you would be forced to obey — but you are not. So why do you persist in rebellion knowing that your faith must be voluntary? What is holding you back from surrendering fully?
?
The Prophet said, 'What God wills is, and what He does not will is not.' But if that 'will' were like a chain forcing you, then even your obedience would be meaningless. Are you living as if your acts of worship are merely obligations forced upon you, or as genuine offerings chosen by your heart? What would change today if you truly believed that every good deed you do is a free gift of love to your Creator?

Gathering on Guidance Requires One Kind of Guidance
Al-Nasafi states the condition for the verse's application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verse about gathering to guidance implies that all guidance must be of a single kind for gathering to be meaningful.

Core Idea
Gathering to guidance is only possible if guidance is uniform.

Imam al-Nasafi begins his argument by drawing attention to a key logical implication of the Quranic verse. If God had willed to gather all people to guidance, that would require that guidance be of one kind—otherwise the phrase 'gather them' would be inconsistent. This lesson unpacks that condition and the problem posed by the existence of two different types of guidance.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Al-Nasafi's claim
Read the verse (6:35) and his statement that gathering would only occur if guidance were one kind.
2
Identify the two types of guidance
Notice the distinction between coerced guidance (jabr) and voluntary guidance (ikhtiyār). Understand that each has different consequences.
3
Understand why mixed guidance fails
Realise that if guidance is of two types, the phrase 'gather them to guidance' cannot apply to everyone.
This sets up the problem.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أنه تعالى قال: ﴿ وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ لَجَمَعَهُمْ عَلَى الْهُدَى ﴾. وإنما يكون جمعهم على الهدى أن لو كان هدى الكل جنساً واحدًا فأما إذا كان هدى البعض جبرًا ولا تنال به الجنة، ولا يتخلص به عن النار وهدى البعض اختيارا، وتنال به الجنة ويتخلص به عن النار فلا يكون هذا جمعهم على الهدى وهو يكون بأحد وجهين إما أن يهدي الكفار باختيارهم حتى يكونوا مع الذين آمنوا باختيارهم مجموعين على الهدى، وإما أن يخلق الاهتداء جبرًا في الكفار ومنع الذين اهتدوا باختيارهم عن الهدى الاختياري وأثبت فيهم الهدى بطريق الجبر، وهذا منه صرف للمؤمنين عن الإيمان قهرا وجبرا، وهذا ليس بحكمة فلم يبق إلا أن يكون المراد هو جمع الكل على الهدى وهو ما بينا، فإذا لم يشأ ذلك دل أنه لم يشأ إيمان الكفرة، والله الموفق.
He verifies it: He, exalted, said: (And if God had willed, He would have gathered them to guidance). And He would gather them to guidance only if the guidance of all were one kind. But if the guidance of some is by compulsion (jabr) and they do not attain Paradise by it, nor are they saved from the Fire, and the guidance of others is by choice (ikhtiyār), and they attain Paradise by it and are saved from the Fire, then this would not be gathering them to guidance. And that would happen in one of two ways: either He would guide the disbelievers by their choice so that they would be together with those who believed by their choice gathered upon guidance, or He would create the guidance by compulsion in the disbelievers and prevent those who were guided by choice from optional guidance and establish in them guidance by way of compulsion. And this would be from Him a turning of the believers away from faith by force and compulsion, and this is not wise. So nothing remains except that the intended meaning is the gathering of all to guidance as we explained. So since He did not will that, it indicates that He did not will the faith of the disbelievers. And God is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 972

Commentary
This passage is an argument from the verse 'If God had willed, He would have gathered them to guidance' (Quran 6:35). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, explains that gathering all to guidance would only be meaningful if guidance were of one kind (jins wāḥid). But if guidance is of two types—coerced guidance (jabr) which does not lead to Paradise, and voluntary guidance (ikhtiyār) which does—then the phrase 'gathering them to guidance' would not apply. He then considers two possible ways that God could gather all to guidance: either by making disbelievers choose faith voluntarily (so all are voluntary believers), or by making disbelievers have coerced guidance and also turning the voluntary believers into coerced believers. The second option would involve unjustly forcing believers away from their voluntary faith, which is not wise (ḥikma). Therefore the only remaining interpretation is that the verse means gathering all to the same kind of voluntary guidance. Since God did not actually gather all to that guidance (as we see many disbelieve), it indicates that God did not will the faith of the disbelievers—meaning He wills it in a way that respects their free choice, not by coercion. This refutes the Jabriyya claim that God's will necessitates coercion.

Key Terms
الجمع على الهدى
هدى جبر
هدى اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That 'gathering on guidance' could be achieved by mixing coerced and voluntary guidance.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that mixing the two types prevents genuine gathering, as the outcomes are different.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what would be required for God to truly 'gather them to guidance'?
A) That all guidance be of a single kind.
B) That most people be guided.
C) That the disbelievers be forced to believe.
D) That both types of guidance exist.

Key Takeaway
For the verse to apply, guidance must be one kind; mixed coerced and voluntary guidance cannot be gathered.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine your own faith: Which type of guidance dominates your religious practice — coerced habit or voluntary choice? This lesson shows that only the latter saves. Identify one act of worship you do out of compulsion and commit to transforming it into a conscious choice today.
?
When you invite others to Islam, do you rely on pressure or persuasion? This passage reveals that forced guidance has no saving power. Will you change your approach to da'wah, trusting that only chosen guidance leads to Paradise?
?
Imagine standing before Allah and realizing that your rituals were mere habits, not heartfelt obedience. This lesson warns that coerced guidance cannot save you. Look at your daily prayers — are they routines or genuine submissions? Decide now to renew your intention in the next prayer.

Two Possible Ways of Gathering and the Refutation of Coercion
Al-Nasafi presents two ways of gathering and rejects coercion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two ways God could have gathered all to guidance and why the second way (coercion) is rejected as unwise, leading to the conclusion that God did not will the faith of disbelievers by compulsion.

Core Idea
Coercing believers is unwise; only voluntary guidance allows genuine gathering.

Having established that mixed guidance prevents gathering, Al-Nasafi now considers two hypothetical ways God could still achieve a gathering. He examines each and demonstrates that one of them—making all believers coerced—is contrary to divine wisdom. This lesson walks through that reasoning and its conclusion, which refutes the Jabriyya claim that God's will necessitates coercion.

Guided Path
1
Examine the two possible ways
Al-Nasafi presents two ways God could gather all: either guide disbelievers by choice, or make all believers coerced.
2
Evaluate the second way
Consider why turning believers away from voluntary faith by force is not wise. This is key to the argument.
3
Draw the conclusion
Conclude that since God did not do either, He did not will the faith of disbelievers in a way that would gather all to guidance.
This refutes the Jabriyya.

Source Text

The Dilemma of Coerced Faith for the Disbeliever
Al-Nasafi presents and refutes an objection about giving coerced faith as 'better' for the disbeliever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical dilemma used to refute the claim that coerced faith is better for the disbeliever.

Core Idea
If coerced faith were better, God would have given it to all—but He didn't.

Al-Nasafi presents a powerful objection against those who argue that compelling a disbeliever to believe is beneficial for him. By posing a simple either-or question, he exposes a contradiction that undermines their position. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the question posed and the two possible answers.
The passage ends with a conditional statement; note how the logic unfolds.
2
Identify the dilemma
The passage presents two options: either coerced faith is better for the disbeliever, or it is not. For each option, a consequence follows.
Write down the two branches of the argument.
3
Understand the refutation
The first option leads to a contradiction with observed reality (widespread disbelief). The second option makes the action impermissible. Both options refute the original claim.
This shows the strength of the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال : ماذا تزعمون أن إعطاء الإيمان للكافر بطريق الجبر هل هو أصلح له أم ليس بأصلح ؟ فإن قالوا: هو أصلح، كان ينبغي أن يعطى كل كافر إيمانا جبرًا فلا يبقى في الأرض كافر ، وحيث رأينا ما لا يحصى من الكفر دل أنه لم يفعل بهم ذلك فكان تاركا ما هو أصلح لهم ، وإن لم يكن ذلك أصلح لهم فلا يجوز له أن يفعل
Then it is said: What do you claim concerning granting faith to the disbeliever by way of compulsion (jabr)? Is it better (aṣlaḥ) for him or not better? If they say: It is better, then it would be necessary that He grant every disbeliever faith by compulsion, so that no disbeliever would remain on earth. But since we see countless disbelief, it indicates that He did not do that to them, so He would be leaving what is better for them. And if it is not better for them, then it is not permissible for Him to do it.
Source pages p. 972

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and a dilemma. The author asks the Jabriyya: Is giving faith to the disbeliever by way of compulsion (jabr) better (aṣlaḥ) for him or not? If they answer that it is better, then the logical consequence is that God would have done it for every disbeliever, as He is all-powerful and all-good. But we observe countless disbelievers, so God did not do it. Therefore, either God left what is better (which is impermissible for a wise and just God) or the premise that it is better is false. If they answer that it is not better, then it is not permissible for God to do it. This argument refutes the idea that coerced faith is beneficial. The text ends mid-sentence, likely continuing with an elaboration that if it is not better, God would not do it, which He has not done, so the argument stands.

Key Terms
أصلح
إيمان جبري
كافر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's not forcing faith on all disbelievers means He is unwilling or unable to guide them.
Correction: The passage shows that if coerced faith were truly beneficial, God would have given it to all. Its absence indicates it is not beneficial, not that God is lacking.

Checkpoint
What dilemma does the author pose to those who claim coerced faith is better for the disbeliever?
A) If it is better, God would give it to all, but He does not; if it is not better, He would not give it at all.
B) If it is better, then the disbeliever would accept it willingly.
C) If it is better, then God would be unjust for not giving it.
D) If it is not better, then God should still give it because He is merciful.

Key Takeaway
The objection shows that coerced faith cannot be genuinely better for the disbeliever, because if it were, God would have ensured it universally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If coerced faith is not truly better, then your own faith must be voluntary. Have you ever treated your faith as something you just 'have' without actively choosing it? What would change if you renewed your commitment to Allah consciously today?
?
This passage shows that God does not force belief because it would not be truly beneficial. Does this challenge your assumptions about why some people remain in disbelief? How does this understanding affect your view of God's justice and your own responsibility to convey faith?
?
The argument implies that coerced faith is valueless. In your own life, are there areas where you are merely going through religious motions without personal conviction? What step can you take this week to make your faith more voluntary and sincere?

The Logical Inconsistency of Jabr Interpretation
Nasafi refutes the Jabriyya via logical inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why interpreting divine will as compulsion leads to a logical contradiction when applied to acts of obedience and disobedience.

Core Idea
If divine will were compulsion, all acts would be forced, but some are chosen.

Nasafi begins his refutation by pointing out an internal inconsistency in the Jabriyya position. The phrase 'what Allah wills happens by compulsion' cannot be consistently maintained because both obedient and disobedient acts occur without being willed by compulsion according to the Jabriyya themselves. This simple logical test shows that the intended meaning of 'will' must be different.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how Nasafi uses a conditional structure.
2
Identify the logical structure
The passage presents a conditional: if the interpretation were valid in one part, it would not be valid in the other. Then it gives evidence from acts of obedience and disobedience. Identify these parts.
The key is the phrase 'لو استقام بأحد شطري الكلام لم يستقم بالشطر الآخر'.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Ask yourself: what does this contradiction prove about the intended meaning of divine will? Nasafi concludes that it cannot be compulsion.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأمة ولا وجه لحملها على مشيئة الجبر ؛ لأنه لو استقام بأحد شطري الكلام لم يستقم بالشطر الآخر فإنه إن أمكن أن يقال : ما شاء الله جبراً كأن لم يمكن أن يقال وما لم يشأ جبرًا لم يكن، لأن الطاعات كلها عندكم لم يشأ جبرًا وكانت والمعاصي لم يشأ جبرًا، وقد كانت فدل أن المراد من المشيئة غير مشيئة الجبر . يحققه أنه تعالى قال: ﴿ وَلَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ لَجَمَعَهُمْ عَلَى الْهُدَى ﴾. وإنما يكون جمعهم على الهدى أن لو كان هدى الكل جنسًا واحدًا فأما إذا كان هدى البعض جبرًا ولا تنال به الجنة، ولا يتخلص به عن النار وهدى البعض اختيارا، وتنال به الجنة ويتخلص به عن النار فلا يكون هذا جمعهم على الهدى وهو يكون بأحد وجهين إما أن يهدي الكفار باختيارهم حتى يكونوا مع الذين آمنوا باختيارهم مجموعين على الهدى، وإما أن يخلق الاهتداء جبرًا في الكفار ومنع الذين اهتدوا باختيارهم عن الهدى الاختياري وأثبت فيهم الهدى بطريق الجبر، وهذا منه صرف للمؤمنين عن الإيمان قهرا وجبرا، وهذا ليس بحكمة فلم يبق إلا أن يكون المراد هو جمع الكل على الهدى وهو ما بينا، فإذا لم يشأ ذلك دل أنه لم يشأ إيمان الكفرة، والله الموفق.
The Ummah has no justification to interpret it as the will of Jabr; because if it were valid in one part of the statement it would not be valid in the other part. For if it could be said: 'What Allah willed is by compulsion' it could not be said 'What He did not will by compulsion did not happen', because all acts of obedience according to you are not willed by compulsion yet they occur, and acts of disobedience are not willed by compulsion yet they occur. So it indicates that the intended meaning of will is not the will of Jabr. He confirms this by saying that Allah the Exalted said: 'And if Allah had willed, He would have gathered them all to guidance.' This gathering to guidance would only be if the guidance of all were one kind. But if the guidance of some is by compulsion without attaining Paradise or escaping Hell, and the guidance of some is by choice attaining Paradise and escaping Hell, then this would not be gathering them to guidance. It would be by one of two ways: either He guides the disbelievers by their choice so that they are with those who believed by their choice gathered upon guidance, or He creates guidance by compulsion in the disbelievers and prevents those who were guided by choice from guidance and establishes in them guidance by compulsion. This would be a turning of the believers away from faith by force and compulsion, and this is not wisdom. So nothing remains except that the intended meaning is the gathering of all to guidance, which we explained. Since He did not will that, it indicates that He did not will the faith of the disbelievers. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 972

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Jabriyya interpretation of divine will. The author begins by arguing that the interpretation of 'mashi'a' as compulsion (jabr) is inconsistent. If one takes the phrase 'what Allah wills happens by compulsion, and what He does not will does not happen' and applies it to acts of obedience and disobedience, it fails because both types of acts occur while they are not willed by compulsion according to the Jabriyya. Therefore, the intended meaning of will is different. The author then confirms this with Quranic verse 6:35. He explains that the verse about gathering all to guidance cannot mean compulsion because if guidance were only by compulsion for some and by choice for others, that would not be a gathering. The only two possible ways to gather all to guidance are either to guide the disbelievers by their choice (so they join the believers in choice) or to force guidance on the disbelievers and remove choice from the believers, which would be unjust and not wise. Thus, the verse indicates that Allah did not will (by compelling) the faith of the disbelievers, meaning He allowed them to choose disbelief.

Key Terms
مشيئة الجبر
الجبر
شطري الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'ما شاء الله كان' means that everything happens by Allah's compulsion.
Correction: Nasafi shows that if that were true, then acts of obedience and disobedience would both be forced, but they are not treated as such by the Jabriyya themselves.

Checkpoint
What does Nasafi use to show the inconsistency of the Jabr interpretation?
A) The fact that acts of obedience and disobedience occur
B) The fact that Allah is just
C) The Quranic verse about gathering to guidance
D) The consensus of the Ummah

Key Takeaway
Nasafi demonstrates that the Jabriyya interpretation of divine will is logically self-defeating because it cannot consistently account for the occurrence of both obedient and disobedient acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'ما شاء الله كان', do you ever use it to avoid taking responsibility for your own choices? Can you recall a specific moment when you blamed Allah's will for a sin you committed? How does Nasafi's argument expose the flaw in that thinking, and what will you do differently next time you feel that temptation?
?
If you truly believe that both obedience and disobedience occur by Allah's will but not by compulsion, how does that change the way you approach your daily actions? What one habit will you change today to affirm your personal accountability before Allah?
?
Nasafi says the Ummah has no basis to interpret will as compulsion. Has there ever been a moment when you comforted yourself with the thought 'it was written' to excuse laziness or sin? How can you internalize this lesson so that you never misuse divine decree as a shield against your own responsibility?
