The Meaning of Qadr and Its Two Aspects
Nasafi defines qadr and distinguishes its two aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two aspects of qadr (divine measure) as defined by Imam Nasafi and how they relate to divine decree and human actions.

Core Idea
Qadr has two faces: the intrinsic measure of things and their temporal-spatial circumstances.

Imam Nasafi meticulously defines the term qadr, distinguishing it from qada'. He explains that qadr is understood in two distinct senses: one relating to the inherent limit and quality of each created thing, the other to the specific circumstances of time, place, and consequent reward or punishment. This lesson unpacks these two aspects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the full translation. Let Nasafi's own definitions come through before you comment.
Pay attention to the two ‘وجوه’ (aspects) mentioned.
2
Identify the two aspects of qadr
The passage explicitly lists two aspects. Find the first (الحد الذي يخرج عليه الشيء) and the second (بيان ما يقع عليه كل شيء من زمان ومكان). Notice how each is defined and supported.
The first aspect is about the intrinsic nature, the second about external circumstances.
3
Understand the implication for human actions
Nasafi argues that the first aspect applies to all human actions (even if beyond human comprehension), while the second does not encompass their time/place. This supports the conclusion that all actions are by Allah's decree.
Reflect on how this resolves potential objections about human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كلها بقضاء الله تعالى أي بخلقه وتكوينه، وقد أقمنا الدلالة عليه بحمد الله تعالى. وأما القدر فهو على وجهين: أحدهما: الحد الذي يخرج عليه الشيء وهو جعل كل شيء على ما هو عليه من خير أو شر من حسن أو قبح من حكمة أو سفه وهو تأويل الحكمة أن يجعل كل شيء على ما هو عليه ويقدر كل شيء على ما هو الأولى به، ولهذا قلنا: إن خلق فعل الكفر ليس بسفه، وقال تعالى: إِنَّا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقْتَهُ بِقَدَرٍ. والثاني: بيان ما يقع عليه كل شيء من زمان ومكان وما له من الثواب والعقاب. فالأول قائم في أفعال الخلق من خروجه على ما لا تبلغه أوهامهم من الحسن والقبح ولا تقدره عقولهم، فثبت أنها خرجت على ذلك بالله تعالى. والثاني لا يحتمل بينهم أفعالهم من الزمان والمكان ولا يبلغه علمهم، فلا يحتمل أن يكون من ذلك الوجه لهم. وإذا عرف أن المراد من القضاء والقدر ما هو وقد أثبتنا بالدليل أن ذلك كله من الله تعالى صح قولنا: إن أفعالنا كلها بقضاء الله تعالى.
All of them are by the decree (qada') of Allah, meaning by His creation and bringing into existence, and we have established the proof for that by the praise of Allah. As for qadr, it has two aspects: One of them: the limit by which a thing emerges, and it is the making of everything as it is, of good or evil, of beauty or ugliness, of wisdom or foolishness, and it is the interpretation of wisdom: to make everything as it is and to determine everything according to what is most appropriate for it. For this reason we said: Indeed, creating the act of disbelief (kufr) is not foolishness. And He said, the Almighty: 'Indeed, We have created everything according to a measure (qadr).' The second: the clarification of that upon which everything occurs, of time and place, and what is for it of reward and punishment. The first is established in the actions of creatures, in their emerging in a way that their imaginations cannot reach in terms of goodness and ugliness, and their intellects cannot determine it. So it is proven that they emerged in that way by Allah, the Almighty. The second does not encompass their actions in terms of time and place, nor does their knowledge reach it, so it cannot be that it is from that aspect for them. And when it is known that the intended meaning of qada' and qadr is what it is, and we have proven by evidence that all of that is from Allah, the Almighty, our statement is correct: 'Our actions, all of them, are by the decree (qada') of Allah.'
Source pages p. 986

Commentary
This passage defines the term qadr (divine measure) and distinguishes its two aspects. The author begins by asserting that all actions are by qada' (decree) of Allah, meaning His creation and bringing into existence. Then he explains qadr has two meanings: first, the limit or precise measure by which everything is created, encompassing good and evil, beauty and ugliness, wisdom and foolishness. This is the interpretation of wisdom: to make each thing as it is and determine it according to what is most appropriate. The author notes that even creating disbelief is not foolish, citing Quran 54:49. Second, qadr refers to the determination of the time, place, reward, and punishment of each thing. The first aspect applies to all human actions, even though humans cannot fully comprehend the goodness or ugliness of them; thus it is proven that these actions come from Allah. The second aspect does not encompass human actions in terms of time and place, nor can humans know it fully, so it cannot be attributed to them. The conclusion is that all our actions are by the decree of Allah, as previously proven by evidence.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada')
قدر (qadr)
حد (limit)
تأويل الحكمة (interpretation of wisdom)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qadr only refers to predestination of events, not the qualities of things.
Correction: Nasafi defines qadr as having two aspects: one is the intrinsic limit/measure of everything (its qualities, goodness/evil), and the other is the determination of time, place, and recompense.

Key Takeaway
Qadr encompasses both the intrinsic limit of each created thing and the determination of its time, place, and recompense.

Distinguishing Qada' from Maqdi
Nasafi distinguishes qada' from maqdi in rebutting the Mu'tazilites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the crucial distinction between Allah's decree (qada') and the decreed thing (maqdi), and why disbelief being decreed does not contradict Allah's perfection.

Core Idea
Allah's decree is always true; the decreed thing may be false.

The Mu'tazilites argued that Allah cannot decree disbelief because disbelief is false, while Allah's decree is truth. Imam Nasafi begins his refutation by introducing a key distinction: the decree itself is distinct from what is decreed. This distinction resolves the apparent contradiction and lays the foundation for understanding divine decrees involving evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite claim
Start by reading how the Mu'tazilites frame their objection: because disbelief is false, it cannot be decreed by Allah whose decree is truth.
Notice their underlying assumption: the decree and the decreed must share the same moral quality.
2
Identify the Nasafi distinction
Find where Imam Nasafi distinguishes between qada' (decree) and maqdi (decreed thing). He states that disbelief is maqdi, not qada'.
This is the core of the refutation.
3
Understand the wisdom behind the decree
The author mentions that the decree of this decreed thing is correct because of wisdom, referring to the creation of actions. Reflect on why a decree involving falsehood can still be wise.
The wisdom lies in punishment, test, or ordering of creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة للمعتزلة، والرد عليها. وزعمت المعتزلة أن الله تعالى لا يقضي الكفر لأن الكفر متفاوت باطل، وقضاء الله تعالى حق وصواب وبه احتج الكعبي. وعندنا أن الكفر مقضي الله تعالى لا قضاؤه، وقضاؤه حق وصواب، ومقضيه باطل، وقضاء هذا المقضي صواب، لما فيه من الحكمة على ما بينا في مسألة خلق الأفعال، فمن رضي يجعل الله تعالى الكفر باطلاً قبيحًا شرًا فقد رضى بقضاء الله تعالى، ومن لم يرض بذلك فهو غير راض بقضاء الله، ومن رضي بذلك ولم يرض أن يكون الكفر صفة له ولم يحب أن يفعله في نفسه فقد رضي بقضاء الله تعالى ولم يرضى بما يوجب مقته وتعذيبه. واحتج الكعبي بقول النبي عليه السلام: من لم يرض بقضائي ولم يصبر على بلائي فليطلب ربا سواي. وقد بينا أنا رضينا بقضاء الله تعالى وأعلمنا كيفيته على أن حقيقة الخبر في الأمراض والمصائب ألا ترى أن الخلود في النار من قضائه عند المعتزلة إذ لا يثبتون الله تعالى تخليدًا سوى معنى الخلود، فليرض به الكعبي لنفسه، وإلا فليطلب ربا سواه. يحققه أن الكفر عندنا وإن كان بقضاء الله تعالى إلا أن من قضى عليه ذلك یرضی به ويتمسك به تمسكًا لا يرضى بالزوال عنه، وإنما الذي لا يرضى به المقضي عليه ويضجر منه في الأحايين هو الأمراض والمصائب، والمعتزلة لا يرضون بها إلا بعوض فليطلبوا ربا سوى من قضى بها عليهم، ثم العجب من الكعبي حيث سمع هذا الحديث فأخذ به ولم يسمع ما استفاض واشتهر وهو قوله
An issue concerning the Mu'tazilites, and the refutation of it. And the Mu'tazilites claimed that Allah, the Almighty, does not decree disbelief (kufr) because disbelief is [؟] false. And the decree (qada') of Allah, the Almighty, is truth and correctness, and by it al-Ka'bi argued. And with us, disbelief is decreed by Allah, the Almighty, not His decree (itself). And His decree is truth and correctness, and the decreed thing is false. And the decree of this decreed thing is correct, because of the wisdom in it, as we explained in the issue of the creation of actions. So whoever is pleased that Allah, the Almighty, makes disbelief false, ugly, evil, has indeed been pleased with the decree of Allah, the Almighty. And whoever is not pleased with that is not pleased with the decree of Allah. And whoever is pleased with that but is not pleased that disbelief be a quality for him and does not love to do it in himself, has been pleased with the decree of Allah, the Almighty, and has not been pleased with what necessitates His wrath and punishment. And al-Ka'bi argued with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Whoever is not pleased with My decree and does not have patience with My trial, let him seek a lord other than Me.' And we have clarified that we are pleased with the decree of Allah, the Almighty, and we know its manner, and that the true meaning of the report is concerning illnesses and calamities. Do you not see that eternity in the Fire is from His decree according to the Mu'tazilites, since they do not affirm for Allah, the Almighty, an eternal [؟] other than the meaning of eternity? So let al-Ka'bi be pleased with it for himself, otherwise let him seek a lord other than Him. He verifies it: that disbelief, with us, even though it is by the decree of Allah, the Almighty, yet the one who is decreed upon it is pleased with it and clings to it, clinging that he is not pleased with its removal. But that which the decreed upon is not pleased with and is annoyed by on occasion is illnesses and calamities. And the Mu'tatilites are not pleased with them except with compensation. So let them seek a lord other than the One who decreed them upon them. Then the wonder is from al-Ka'bi, because he heard this hadith and took it and did not hear what is widespread and well-known, which is his saying...
Source pages p. 986

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that Allah does not decree disbelief (kufr). The author begins by stating the Mu'tazilite claim and then responds. He makes a crucial distinction: disbelief is 'maqdi' (decreed by Allah), not 'qada'' (the decree itself). The decree (qada') is always truth and correct, while the decreed thing (maqdi) i.e., disbelief, is false. The wisdom of the decree lies in punishment and ordering of creation. Then the author discusses the concept of being pleased (rida) with the decree. He explains three cases: 1) One who is pleased that Allah makes disbelief false has pleased with the decree. 2) One who is not pleased with that is not pleased with the decree. 3) One who is pleased with that but does not want disbelief as his own attribute has pleased with the decree but not with what brings wrath. The author cites a hadith used by al-Ka'bi: 'Whoever is not pleased with My decree... let him seek a lord other than Me.' The author argues that the hadith primarily concerns illnesses and calamities, not disbelief. He then turns the argument against the Mu'tazilites: they affirm eternal punishment in Hell as from Allah, so they should be pleased with that decree for themselves, otherwise they too are rejecting the hadith logic. Finally, the author refines the point: the one decreed with disbelief is pleased with it and does not want it removed, whereas the one decreed with illness or calamity is annoyed by it. The Mu'tazilites only accept the hadith for calamities if compensated, which is inconsistent. He ends by criticizing al-Ka'bi for accepting this hadith while ignoring other widely transmitted hadith.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada')
مقضي (maqdi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah decrees disbelief, then His decree must be false or evil.
Correction: Allah's decree (qada') remains true and correct; it is the decreed thing (maqdi) that is false. The decree is wise, serving purposes like punishment.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between qada' and maqdi in the case of disbelief?
A) Qada' is false, maqdi is true.
B) Qada' is true, maqdi is false.
C) Both are true.
D) Both are false.

Key Takeaway
Allah's decrees are always true and wise, even when what is decreed is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone committing disbelief, do you secretly question Allah's wisdom in decreeing it? How does this lesson challenge you to accept that His decree remains true and correct, even when the thing decreed is false?
?
Are there events in your life that you have considered as 'mistakes' in Allah's plan? How can the distinction between qada' and maqdi help you trust that His decree over that event is always correct, no matter how flawed the event itself seemed?
?
How does knowing that Allah's decree is always true and wise affect your prayer for guidance for others? Will you now pray differently for those in disbelief, recognizing that Allah's decree of their state is part of a greater wisdom?

Three Levels of Pleasing with the Decree
Nasafi categorizes responses to the decree of disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct stances people take regarding being pleased with Allah's decree of disbelief, and how one can be pleased with the decree without approving of disbelief itself.

Core Idea
Being pleased with Allah's decree is not the same as being pleased with the act.

After establishing the qada'/maqdi distinction, Imam Nasafi addresses a practical consequence: how should believers relate to Allah's decree of disbelief? He defines three categories that clarify what it means to be pleased with the decree. This nuanced teaching prevents misunderstanding and extremism.

Guided Path
1
List the three cases
Read the passage and identify the three categories of people described. Notice how each relates to the decree and to disbelief itself.
2
Differentiate between the first two
The first is pleased with the decree, the second is not. Understand why the second is displeased: he rejects that Allah makes disbelief false.
This is the Mu'tazilite position in practice.
3
Examine the third case
The third person is pleased with the decree but not pleased that disbelief be his own attribute. See how this balances submission to the decree with personal moral responsibility.
This is the correct Sunni stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة للمعتزلة، والرد عليها. وزعمت المعتزلة أن الله تعالى لا يقضي الكفر لأن الكفر متفاوت باطل، وقضاء الله تعالى حق وصواب وبه احتج الكعبي. وعندنا أن الكفر مقضي الله تعالى لا قضاؤه، وقضاؤه حق وصواب، ومقضيه باطل، وقضاء هذا المقضي صواب، لما فيه من الحكمة على ما بينا في مسألة خلق الأفعال، فمن رضي يجعل الله تعالى الكفر باطلاً قبيحًا شرًا فقد رضى بقضاء الله تعالى، ومن لم يرض بذلك فهو غير راض بقضاء الله، ومن رضي بذلك ولم يرض أن يكون الكفر صفة له ولم يحب أن يفعله في نفسه فقد رضي بقضاء الله تعالى ولم يرضى بما يوجب مقته وتعذيبه. واحتج الكعبي بقول النبي عليه السلام: من لم يرض بقضائي ولم يصبر على بلائي فليطلب ربا سواي. وقد بينا أنا رضينا بقضاء الله تعالى وأعلمنا كيفيته على أن حقيقة الخبر في الأمراض والمصائب ألا ترى أن الخلود في النار من قضائه عند المعتزلة إذ لا يثبتون الله تعالى تخليدًا سوى معنى الخلود، فليرض به الكعبي لنفسه، وإلا فليطلب ربا سواه. يحققه أن الكفر عندنا وإن كان بقضاء الله تعالى إلا أن من قضى عليه ذلك یرضی به ويتمسك به تمسكًا لا يرضى بالزوال عنه، وإنما الذي لا يرضى به المقضي عليه ويضجر منه في الأحايين هو الأمراض والمصائب، والمعتزلة لا يرضون بها إلا بعوض فليطلبوا ربا سوى من قضى بها عليهم، ثم العجب من الكعبي حيث سمع هذا الحديث فأخذ به ولم يسمع ما استفاض واشتهر وهو قوله
An issue concerning the Mu'tazilites, and the refutation of it. And the Mu'tazilites claimed that Allah, the Almighty, does not decree disbelief (kufr) because disbelief is [؟] false. And the decree (qada') of Allah, the Almighty, is truth and correctness, and by it al-Ka'bi argued. And with us, disbelief is decreed by Allah, the Almighty, not His decree (itself). And His decree is truth and correctness, and the decreed thing is false. And the decree of this decreed thing is correct, because of the wisdom in it, as we explained in the issue of the creation of actions. So whoever is pleased that Allah, the Almighty, makes disbelief false, ugly, evil, has indeed been pleased with the decree of Allah, the Almighty. And whoever is not pleased with that is not pleased with the decree of Allah. And whoever is pleased with that but is not pleased that disbelief be a quality for him and does not love to do it in himself, has been pleased with the decree of Allah, the Almighty, and has not been pleased with what necessitates His wrath and punishment. And al-Ka'bi argued with the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Whoever is not pleased with My decree and does not have patience with My trial, let him seek a lord other than Me.' And we have clarified that we are pleased with the decree of Allah, the Almighty, and we know its manner, and that the true meaning of the report is concerning illnesses and calamities. Do you not see that eternity in the Fire is from His decree according to the Mu'tazilites, since they do not affirm for Allah, the Almighty, an eternal [؟] other than the meaning of eternity? So let al-Ka'bi be pleased with it for himself, otherwise let him seek a lord other than Him. He verifies it: that disbelief, with us, even though it is by the decree of Allah, the Almighty, yet the one who is decreed upon it is pleased with it and clings to it, clinging that he is not pleased with its removal. But that which the decreed upon is not pleased with and is annoyed by on occasion is illnesses and calamities. And the Mu'tatilites are not pleased with them except with compensation. So let them seek a lord other than the One who decreed them upon them. Then the wonder is from al-Ka'bi, because he heard this hadith and took it and did not hear what is widespread and well-known, which is his saying...

According to the passage, what distinguishes the third category from the first?
A) The third person is not pleased with the decree at all.
B) The third person is pleased with the decree but not with disbelief as his own attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone committing a sin, do you secretly feel a sense of superiority, or do you honestly struggle to hate the sin while accepting that Allah decreed it? Which of the three levels describes your heart's response?
?
Is there any sin that you secretly find attractive or excuse in yourself because 'Allah decreed it'? How does this passage challenge that excuse?
?
Are you truly pleased with Allah's judgment that disbelief is evil, even when it means your own actions might be judged? Or does part of you wish He had not called it evil so you could indulge without guilt?

Refuting al-Ka'bi's Hadith Argument
Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi's hadith citation and inverts it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi refutes al-Ka'bi's use of the hadith 'Whoever is not pleased with My decree...' and turns the argument back against the Mu'tazilites.

Core Idea
The hadith refers to calamities, not to disbelief; the Mu'tazilites themselves reject it when applied to their own beliefs.

Al-Ka'bi, a Mu'tazilite, attempts to support his position with a prophetic hadith that commands being pleased with the decree. Imam Nasafi now engages this argument, showing that the hadith actually concerns illnesses and trials, not theological decrees like disbelief. He then turns the tables: the Mu'tazilites, who affirm eternal punishment for disbelievers, must be pleased with that decree themselves or be inconsistent.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ka'bi's argument
Identify the hadith he cites and note how he expects it to prove that Allah does not decree disbelief.
He assumes that one cannot be pleased with a decree of disbelief.
2
Understand Nasafi's response
Imam Nasafi argues that the hadith is primarily about illnesses and calamities, not about disbelief itself. He points out that the Mu'tazilites believe Allah decrees eternal punishment, so by their own logic they should be pleased with that.
This is a tu quoque (you too) argument.
3
Reflect on the final point
Nasafi notes that the one decreed disbelief is pleased with it and clings to it, while the one afflicted with illness is annoyed. The Mu'tazilites only accept the hadith with compensation, showing inconsistency.
This completes the refutation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Are there any sins in your life that you have become comfortable with—sins you no longer wish to remove? If so, are you not like the disbeliever who is pleased with his disbelief? What would it take for you to genuinely seek to abandon that sin and be displeased with it?
?
If you were to apply the hadith to your own life right now, is there any area where you are not pleased with Allah's decree? What would change if you truly believed that every trial is from Him and that you must be pleased with it? Commit to one concrete step this week to cultivate patience and acceptance of a specific decree.

Hadiths on Qadar and Refutation of al-Ka'bi's Selectivity
Al-Nasafi cites hadiths on qadar and criticizes al-Ka'bi's selective acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses two key hadiths to refute al-Ka'bi's selective acceptance of teachings on qadar, and why belief in both good and evil of qadar is essential for iman.

Core Idea
Belief in qadar includes both good and evil from Allah; rejecting any part is disbelief.

Al-Nasafi continues his refutation of al-Ka'bi by pointing out the latter's inconsistency: he accepts a hadith that suits his view but ignores other widely-known hadiths. The passage cites two such hadiths: one stating that qadar's good and evil are from Allah, and another that lists four pillars of iman—including faith in qadar—and equates concealing any one of them with disbelief. This highlights the danger of selective theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the tone of amazement ('then amazing is al-Ka'bi') and the two hadiths cited.
The phrase 'قدر خيره وشره من الله' is a direct refutation of those who deny that evil is from Allah.
2
Understand the First Hadith
Identify the first hadith: 'The decree, its good and its evil, is from Allah.' This affirms that both good and evil are within Allah's decree.
Al-Ka'bi apparently accepted a hadith about patience with decree but ignored this one.
3
Understand the Second Hadith
The hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas lists four matters that constitute iman: shahada, belief in resurrection, and faith in qadar. One who rejects any of these has disbelieved.
This shows that belief in qadar is not optional but a requirement of iman.
4
Reflect on the Critique
Al-Nasafi concludes that al-Ka'bi is a man who takes what agrees with his desire and leaves what contradicts. This is a strong criticism of cherry-picking sources.
This lesson teaches the importance of accepting all authentic teachings, not just those that suit one's views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العجب من الكعبي حيث سمع هذا الحديث فأخذ به ولم يسمع ما استفاض واشتهر وهو قوله عليه السلام: القدر خيره وشره من الله وحديث سعد بن أبي وقاص به عن النبي عليه السلام أنه قال: أربع من كن فيه فهو مؤمن ومن جاء بثلاث وكتم واحدة فقد كفر، شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله، وأنه مبعوث من بعد الموت، وإيمان بالقدر خيره وشره فمن جاء بثلاث وكتم واحدة فقد كفر لكنه رجل يأخذ ما وافق هواه ويترك ما خالف ذلك.
Then amazing is al-Ka'bi, that he heard this hadith and took it, but did not hear what is widespread and well-known, namely his saying, peace be upon him: 'The decree (qadar), its good and its evil, is from Allah,' and the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas from him, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Four (qualities), whoever possesses them is a believer, and whoever comes with three and conceals one has disbelieved: the testimony that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah, and that he is raised after death, and faith in the decree, its good and its evil. So whoever comes with three and conceals one has disbelieved.' But he is a man who takes what agrees with his desire and leaves what contradicts that.
Source pages p. 988

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of al-Ka'bi. The author expresses amazement that al-Ka'bi accepts the hadith about patience with decree but ignores other widely-known hadiths, such as the Prophet's saying: 'The decree (qadar), its good and its evil, is from Allah.' Additionally, the author cites the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, which lists four essential beliefs that constitute iman: the testimony of tawhid and prophethood, belief in resurrection, and faith in qadar (both good and evil). The hadith states that one who accepts three but conceals one has disbelieved. The author concludes that al-Ka'bi selectively takes what suits his own desires and rejects what contradicts them, implying inconsistency and theological bias.

Key Terms
قدر
خيره وشره
سعد بن أبي وقاص
إيمان
هوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that belief in qadar only requires affirming God's knowledge, not that evil is from God.
Correction: The hadith explicitly states 'its good and its evil is from Allah', affirming both aspects as part of qadar.

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, what does the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas say about belief in qadar?
A) Belief in qadar is optional for believers.
B) One who believes in three of the four listed matters but rejects qadar has disbelieved.
C) Qadar only includes good, not evil.
D) Belief in qadar is only required for scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ka'bi's selective acceptance of hadiths reveals inconsistency; true iman requires belief in qadar entirely, including both good and evil from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself uneasy with the belief that both good and evil are from Allah? In what way might you have, like al-Ka'bi, avoided or dismissed parts of this teaching because they challenged your understanding? What will you do today to sincerely accept the full scope of qadar?
?
Consider the hadith that whoever accepts three of the four essentials but conceals one has disbelieved. Is there any core belief of Islam that you have downplayed or explained away to fit your worldview? What would it mean for your iman if you were to reject it entirely? Take a moment to reaffirm your faith in all its pillars, especially qadar.
?
Al-Ka'bi is described as a man who takes what agrees with his desire and leaves what contradicts. Where in your life are you tempted to follow your desires over revealed truth? In matters of qadar or other teachings, are you truly submitting to Allah's word, or are you picking and choosing? Commit to one concrete change in how you approach difficult teachings.

The Hadith on Qadar as a Pillar of Faith
A Prophetic hadith listing four requirements for true faith, including belief in qadar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in qadar—its good and evil—is presented in this hadith as an essential component of faith, and that denying it while affirming other pillars is a form of disbelief.

Core Idea
Faith in qadar is as essential as Tawheed and the Resurrection.

This lesson focuses on a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that lists four indispensible qualities of a believer. The hadith is quoted here to establish that belief in divine decree (qadar) is not optional; it is a pillar of faith. Pay attention to how the hadith describes the person who accepts three but conceals one—this sets the stage for the argument that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Read the Arabic and English translation of the hadith carefully. Note the four qualities: testimony of tawheed, testimony of prophethood, belief in resurrection, and belief in qadar.
The hadith is attributed to Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas from the Prophet.
2
Identify the condition for faith
The hadith says that whoever comes with three of these and conceals one has disbelieved. Reflect on what this means for the status of belief in qadar.
3
Notice the critique of selective belief
The hadith adds that such a person 'takes what agrees with his desire and leaves what contradicts that.' This hints at the problem of cherry-picking doctrines.
This leads into the author's refutation of excuses in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه السلام: 'القدر خيره وشره من الله وحديث سعد بن أبي وقاص به عن النبي عليه السلام أنه قال: أربع من كن فيه فهو مؤمن ومن جاء بثلاث وكتم واحدة فقد كفر، شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله، وأنه مبعوث من بعد الموت، وإيمان بالقدر خيره وشره فمن جاء بثلاث وكتم واحدة فقد كفر لكنه رجل يأخذ ما وافق هواه ويترك ما خالف ذلك، ثم اعملوا أن لا عذر لأحد في التخليق والإرادة والقضاء والقدر لأن هذه المعاني لم تجعلهم مضطرين إلى ما فعلوا بل فعلوا ما فعلوا مختارين فصار خلق الفعل وإرادته والقضاء به وتقديره كخلق الأوقات والأمكنة التي تقع فيها الأفعال ولا تقع بدونها، ولم يصر تخليق شيء من ذلك عذرا لأنه لا يوجب اضطرارهم وكذا هذا، ولأنه لم يخطر شيء من ذلك ببالهم وقت الفعل أنهم يفعلون لأجله فكان الاعتذار به والاحتجاج باطلاً، ولو كان لهم به الاحتجاج لكان بالعلم والتقوية ونحوهما احتجاج، ولأنه لا عذر لهم بأنه علمه بما يكون منهم، وبأنهم فعلوا ما فعلوا معتمدين على كرمه وجوده خلقهم مع والغناء عن تعذيبهم، وعلى أنه عفو غفور، وعلى أنه ليس له في طاعتهم نفع ولا عليه في معصيتهم ضرر فكذا هذا، على أنا أقمنا الدلالة على أن لهم فعلاً مختارون فيعاقبهم على ذلك، والله الموفق.
Peace be upon him: 'Qadar, its good and its evil, is from God.' And the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Four (qualities), whoever has them in him is a believer, and whoever comes with three and conceals one has disbelieved: testimony that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah, and that he is resurrected after death, and faith in qadar, its good and its evil. So whoever comes with three and conceals one has disbelieved, but he is a man who takes what agrees with his desire and leaves what contradicts that.' Then know that there is no excuse for anyone in (matters of) creation, will, decree, and destiny, because these meanings did not make them compelled to what they did, but rather they did what they did as choosers. Thus the creation of the act, and willing it, and decreeing it, and determining it became like the creation of the times and places in which acts occur and without which they do not occur. And the creation of any of that did not become an excuse because it does not necessitate their compulsion—likewise this. And because none of that came to their minds at the time of the act, that they do it for its sake, so making an excuse by it and arguing (with it) is false. And if they could argue by it, they would argue by knowledge, strengthening, and the like. And because there is no excuse for them that He knew what would be from them, and that they did what they did relying on His generosity and bounty—He created them with self-sufficiency from punishing them, and that He is Pardoning, Forgiving, and that there is no benefit to Him in their obedience nor harm to Him in their disobedience—likewise this. Moreover, we have established the proof that they have an act by which they are choosers, so He punishes them for that. And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 988

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof and refutation. It begins with a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that belief in qadar (divine decree) is one of four things without which one is not a believer. The author then argues that despite God's creation of actions, humans are not compelled—they act voluntarily (mukhtārin). The author compares God's creation of the act, will, decree, and determination to His creation of times and places: just as times and places do not compel the act, so God's creative role does not compel the agent. He refutes the excuse that God's foreknowledge or mercy could justify sin, because people do not act with that in mind. He concludes by reaffirming that humans have free choice (fi‘l mukhtār) and are justly punished.

Key Terms
القدر (al-qadar)
شهادة (shahāda)
إيمان (īmān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think belief in qadar is optional or secondary to other articles of faith.
Correction: The hadith clearly lists belief in qadar alongside tawheed and resurrection as one of four indispensable qualities; without it, one is not a believer.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith, how many qualities must a person have to be considered a believer?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Two
D) One

Key Takeaway
Belief in qadar—its good and evil—is a non-negotiable pillar of faith, on par with tawheed and resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every good and evil that happens to you is from Allah? How does this belief affect your reaction to trials and blessings? Are you willing to accept the decree even when it is painful?
?
The hadith warns that concealing one of these pillars is kufr. Is there any part of the Islamic creed that you are ashamed of or hesitant to affirm in front of others? Why?
?
If you were tested with a situation where your faith in qadar is shaken, would your response reflect true iman or selective belief? What can you do today to strengthen your conviction in qadar?

Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
God's Decree Does Not Excuse Sin
A rational argument refuting the excuse that divine decree compels sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that God's creation of actions, will, and decree does not compel humans to sin; therefore, it cannot serve as a valid excuse for wrongdoing.

Core Idea
God's decree is like time and place—they enable acts but don't compel them.

After establishing the importance of belief in qadar, the author now tackles the common objection: if God creates everything, including our actions, how can we be blamed? This lesson unpacks his response: God's creative role is analogous to providing the time and place in which an act occurs—these do not force the act. Humans remain free choosers, so responsibility stands.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'ثم اعملوا أن لا عذر لأحد' to the end. Follow the author's line of reasoning.
The author uses analogy: God's creation of the act is like His creation of times and places.
2
Identify the key analogy
Find the sentence where the author compares 'creation of the act, willing it, decreeing it, and determining it' to 'creation of times and places'. Reflect on why this analogy refutes compulsion.
Times and places don't make you act; they merely provide context.
3
Recognize the refutation of common excuses
The author mentions that people might argue using God's foreknowledge, mercy, or self-sufficiency. Notice how each is dismissed because it doesn't cause compulsion.
4
Conclude with free choice
The author ends by restating that humans have ‘acts by which they are choosers’ and are justly punished. This is the core theological point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه السلام: 'القدر خيره وشره من الله وحديث سعد بن أبي وقاص به عن النبي عليه السلام أنه قال: أربع من كن فيه فهو مؤمن ومن جاء بثلاث وكتم واحدة فقد كفر، شهادة أن لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله، وأنه مبعوث من بعد الموت، وإيمان بالقدر خيره وشره فمن جاء بثلاث وكتم واحدة فقد كفر لكنه رجل يأخذ ما وافق هواه ويترك ما خالف ذلك، ثم اعملوا أن لا عذر لأحد في التخليق والإرادة والقضاء والقدر لأن هذه المعاني لم تجعلهم مضطرين إلى ما فعلوا بل فعلوا ما فعلوا مختارين فصار خلق الفعل وإرادته والقضاء به وتقديره كخلق الأوقات والأمكنة التي تقع فيها الأفعال ولا تقع بدونها، ولم يصر تخليق شيء من ذلك عذرا لأنه لا يوجب اضطرارهم وكذا هذا، ولأنه لم يخطر شيء من ذلك ببالهم وقت الفعل أنهم يفعلون لأجله فكان الاعتذار به والاحتجاج باطلاً، ولو كان لهم به الاحتجاج لكان بالعلم والتقوية ونحوهما احتجاج، ولأنه لا عذر لهم بأنه علمه بما يكون منهم، وبأنهم فعلوا ما فعلوا معتمدين على كرمه وجوده خلقهم مع والغناء عن تعذيبهم، وعلى أنه عفو غفور، وعلى أنه ليس له في طاعتهم نفع ولا عليه في معصيتهم ضرر فكذا هذا، على أنا أقمنا الدلالة على أن لهم فعلاً مختارون فيعاقبهم على ذلك، والله الموفق.
Peace be upon him: 'Qadar, its good and its evil, is from God.' And the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Four (qualities), whoever has them in him is a believer, and whoever comes with three and conceals one has disbelieved: testimony that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah, and that he is resurrected after death, and faith in qadar, its good and its evil. So whoever comes with three and conceals one has disbelieved, but he is a man who takes what agrees with his desire and leaves what contradicts that.' Then know that there is no excuse for anyone in (matters of) creation, will, decree, and destiny, because these meanings did not make them compelled to what they did, but rather they did what they did as choosers. Thus the creation of the act, and willing it, and decreeing it, and determining it became like the creation of the times and places in which acts occur and without which they do not occur. And the creation of any of that did not become an excuse because it does not necessitate their compulsion—likewise this. And because none of that came to their minds at the time of the act, that they do it for its sake, so making an excuse by it and arguing (with it) is false. And if they could argue by it, they would argue by knowledge, strengthening, and the like. And because there is no excuse for them that He knew what would be from them, and that they did what they did relying on His generosity and bounty—He created them with self-sufficiency from punishing them, and that He is Pardoning, Forgiving, and that there is no benefit to Him in their obedience nor harm to Him in their disobedience—likewise this. Commentary
This passage is a combined proof and refutation. It begins with a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating that belief in qadar (divine decree) is one of four things without which one is not a believer. The author then argues that despite God's creation of actions, humans are not compelled—they act voluntarily (mukhtārin). Key Terms
التخليق (al-takhlīq)

القضاء (al-qaḍā')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that if God creates an action, then the human is forced to do it and bears no responsibility.
Correction: The author argues that creation does not compel; the human still chooses voluntarily, as shown by the analogy with time and place.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to explain why God's creation of an act does not compel the agent?
A) Creating a bird and its flight
B) Creating times and places
C) Creating a tool and its use
D) Creating a seed and its growth

Key Takeaway
God's creative role does not compel humans; they remain free agents responsible for their choices.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking 'it was my fate' or 'Allah decreed it'? What is one specific sin you have excused this way, and how will you sincerely repent tonight without using that excuse?
?
The lesson says that the thought of divine decree never occurs to you at the moment of sinning. Think of a recent sin—were you consciously relying on decree when you committed it? If not, why do you bring it up afterward? What would it take for you to stop using that excuse entirely?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's decree does not force you to sin, how would your daily struggle against disobedience change? Name one area where you have been passive, blaming your environment, and commit tomorrow to actively choose obedience as a free agent.

The Maturidi View: God Creates Guidance and Misguidance
One-sentence Maturidi statement on guidance and misguidance as created acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that God creates both guidance and misguidance as acts in His servants, based on the premise that God creates all human actions.

Core Idea
Guidance and misguidance are created acts of God.

The Maturidi school affirms that God's power encompasses all human actions, including the acts of being guided or misguided. This passage states that since God creates all actions, He directly creates the act of guidance and the act of misguidance in the servant, making Him the source of both. This sets the stage for the Mu'tazila objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Maturidi claim
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation carefully. Notice the logical flow: 'since it is established that God creates actions, He is the one who creates the act of being guided and the act of being misguided.'
The key term is 'فعل الاهتداء وفعل الضلال' (the act of being guided and the act of being misguided).
2
Understand the premise
The claim rests on the premise that God creates all human actions. If God creates all actions, then the actions of being guided and misguided are also created by Him.
This is a foundational Maturidi principle in the debate over free will and predestination.
3
Identify the conclusion
The conclusion is that guidance (hudā) and misguidance (iḍlāl) originate from God. This is a direct consequence of the premise.
This view contrasts sharply with the Mu'tazila, who deny that God creates human actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما ثبت أن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد فكان هو الذي خلق فيهم فعل الاهتداء وفعل الضلال، فوجد منه الهدى والإضلال. وعند المعتزلة لما لم يجز أن يخلق أفعالهم لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال، ويقولون ما أضيف إلى الله تعالى من الهداية فالمراد منه بيان طريق الدين لا تخليق فعل الاهتداء، وما أضيف إليه من الإزاغة والإضلال والخذلان والطبع بقوله: (وَطَبَعَ اللهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ) والمد بقوله: (وَيَمُدُّهُمْ فِي طُغْيَانِهِمْ يَعْمَهُونَ) فلأن السبب الذي كان به منهم الأفعال كان من الله تعالى كالقدر والآلات، وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى مسببها، وكذا في الهداية والعصمة قد تضاف على هذا الطريق، وقد يقولون بأنها تضاف إليه على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى شروطها التي توجد هي عندها إذ لولا المحنة والتكليف لما وجدت منهم هذه
Then, since it is established that God Most High created the actions of servants, so He is the one who created in them the act of being guided and the act of being misguided, so guidance and misguidance came from Him. According to the Mu‘tazila, since it is not permissible that He create their actions, there did not occur from Him creation of the act of being guided nor creation of the act of being misguided. And they say: what is attributed to God Most High of guidance, the intended meaning is the clarification of the path of religion, not the creation of the act of being guided. And what is attributed to Him of misguidance, leading astray, abandonment, and sealing, by His saying: 'And Allah has sealed their hearts' and the prolongation by His saying: 'And He prolongs them in their transgression, wandering blindly' (is) because the cause by which actions occurred from them was from God Most High, like capacity and instruments, and actions are sometimes attributed to their cause. Similarly, in guidance and protection (from sin) they are attributed in this way. And they sometimes say that they are attributed to Him according to the attribution of things to their conditions, which exist when they exist, since had it not been for the trial and obligation, these actions would not have occurred from them.
Source pages p. 989

Commentary
This passage contrasts the Maturidi and Mu‘tazili positions on guidance (huda) and misguidance (idlal). The author first states the Maturidi position: since God creates all actions, He creates the acts of being guided and being misguided in humans; thus guidance and misguidance originate from Him. Then he presents the Mu‘tazili objection: because God cannot create human actions (on their view), He does not create the act of guidance or misguidance. Instead, they reinterpret scriptural attributions: 'guidance' from God means mere clarification (bayān) of the right path, not creation of the act. Similarly, 'misguidance', 'sealing', and 'prolongation' are due to God's creation of causes (like capacity and instruments) which make actions possible; actions are then attributed to their causes. They also say these attributes are like conditions: without the trial (miḥna) and obligation (taklīf), these actions would not exist. The author is presenting their view without immediate refutation, setting up for a later response.

Key Terms
الهدى (al-hudā)
الإضلال (al-iḍlāl)
فعل الاهتداء (fi‘l al-ihtidā')
فعل الضلال (fi‘l al-ḍalāl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Maturidi view implies that God forces people to be guided or misguided without any human role.
Correction: The Maturidi hold that God creates the act, but the human acquires it (kasb). This passage only asserts divine creation, not that humans have no part.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for saying that guidance and misguidance come from God?
A) Because God commands guidance and forbids misguidance.
B) Because God creates all human actions, including the acts of being guided and misguided.
C) Because guidance and misguidance are independent of human actions.
D) Because the Qur'an says so without further explanation.

Key Takeaway
In the Maturidi view, guidance and misguidance are created acts of God, flowing from His creation of all human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a moment of clarity or guidance in your faith, do you truly believe that God created that act of being guided in you at that very moment? How would your gratitude change if you lived with that awareness every second?
?
If misguidance too is a created act from God, does that not terrify you? What is your responsibility in seeking guidance when you know it is ultimately a gift He creates? Will you beg Him for it with utter dependence?
?
The passage says 'guidance and misguidance came from Him.' Does your heart accept that both are from the same Lord, or do you secretly resent God for the misguidance you see in the world? How will you reconcile this with His perfect wisdom and justice?

Divine Decree

The Mu‘tazila Reinterpretation of Divine Guidance and Misguidance
Mu‘tazila arguments reinterpreting divine guidance, misguidance, and related attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu‘tazila reinterpret Qur'anic attributions of guidance and misguidance to God, denying that He creates these acts and offering alternative explanations.

Core Idea
For the Mu‘tazila, 'guidance' from God means showing the right path, not creating the act.

The Mu‘tazila cannot accept that God creates human actions, including guidance and misguidance. This passage presents their reinterpretation: they explain away the plain meaning of verses by arguing that 'guidance' is merely clarification, and that attributions of 'misguidance', 'sealing', and 'prolongation' refer to God's creation of causes or conditions, not direct creation of acts. This lesson unpacks their arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu‘tazila objection
Read the Arabic passage from 'وعند المعتزلة' onward. Notice how they first deny that God creates the acts of guidance or misguidance.
2
Analyze their view on guidance
They reinterpret divine guidance (hidāya) as 'clarification of the path of religion' (بيان طريق الدين), not creation of the act of being guided.
This is a key linguistic and theological maneuver.
3
Understand their explanation for misguidance and related terms
For terms like 'misguidance', 'sealing', and 'prolongation', they attribute them to God as the cause of the conditions (like capacity and instruments) that make actions possible, not as the direct creator of the acts.
They give two ways of attributing such actions to God: as causes of conditions, or as conditions themselves.
4
Recognize the broader implication
This reinterpretation preserves the Mu‘tazili principle that God does not create evil or human acts, while still maintaining that God is ultimately involved through secondary causality.
This sets up a later Maturidi refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لما ثبت أن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد فكان هو الذي خلق فيهم فعل الاهتداء وفعل الضلال، فوجد منه الهدى والإضلال. وعند المعتزلة لما لم يجز أن يخلق أفعالهم لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال، ويقولون ما أضيف إلى الله تعالى من الهداية فالمراد منه بيان طريق الدين لا تخليق فعل الاهتداء، وما أضيف إليه من الإزاغة والإضلال والخذلان والطبع بقوله: (وَطَبَعَ اللهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ) والمد بقوله: (وَيَمُدُّهُمْ فِي طُغْيَانِهِمْ يَعْمَهُونَ) فلأن السبب الذي كان به منهم الأفعال كان من الله تعالى كالقدر والآلات، وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى مسببها، وكذا في الهداية والعصمة قد تضاف على هذا الطريق، وقد يقولون بأنها تضاف إليه على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى شروطها التي توجد هي عندها إذ لولا المحنة والتكليف لما وجدت منهم هذه
Then, since it is established that God Most High created the actions of servants, so He is the one who created in them the act of being guided and the act of being misguided, so guidance and misguidance came from Him. According to the Mu‘tazila, since it is not permissible that He create their actions, there did not occur from Him creation of the act of being guided nor creation of the act of being misguided. And they say: what is attributed to God Most High of guidance, the intended meaning is the clarification of the path of religion, not the creation of the act of being guided. And what is attributed to Him of misguidance, leading astray, abandonment, and sealing, by His saying: 'And Allah has sealed their hearts' and the prolongation by His saying: 'And He prolongs them in their transgression, wandering blindly' (is) because the cause by which actions occurred from them was from God Most High, like capacity and instruments, and actions are sometimes attributed to their cause. Similarly, in guidance and protection (from sin) they are attributed in this way. And they sometimes say that they are attributed to Him according to the attribution of things to their conditions, which exist when they exist, since had it not been for the trial and obligation, these actions would not have occurred from them.
Source pages p. 989

Commentary
This passage contrasts the Maturidi and Mu‘tazili positions on guidance (huda) and misguidance (idlal). The author first states the Maturidi position: since God creates all actions, He creates the acts of being guided and being misguided in humans; thus guidance and misguidance originate from Him. Then he presents the Mu‘tazili objection: because God cannot create human actions (on their view), He does not create the act of guidance or misguidance. Instead, they reinterpret scriptural attributions: 'guidance' from God means mere clarification (bayān) of the right path, not creation of the act. Similarly, 'misguidance', 'sealing', and 'prolongation' are due to God's creation of causes (like capacity and instruments) which make actions possible; actions are then attributed to their causes. They also say these attributes are like conditions: without the trial (miḥna) and obligation (taklīf), these actions would not exist. The author is presenting their view without immediate refutation, setting up for a later response.

Key Terms
الهداية (al-hidāya)
الإضلال (al-iḍlāl)
الخذلان (al-khidhlān)
الطبع (al-ṭab‘)
المد (al-madd)
المحنة (al-miḥna)
التكليف (al-taklīf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu‘tazila completely deny any involvement of God in guidance and misguidance.
Correction: The passage shows they do attribute these to God, but as causes of conditions or as clarifications, not as direct creation.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu‘tazila as presented in the passage, what does 'guidance' (hidāya) from God mean?
A) The creation of the act of being guided in the servant.
B) The clarification of the path of religion.
C) The predestination of all actions.
D) The granting of faith directly.

Key Takeaway
The Mu‘tazila reinterpret Qur'anic verses on guidance and misguidance to maintain that God does not create human acts, instead explaining them as clarification or as causal conditions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read in the Qur'an that Allah 'seals hearts' and 'leads astray,' do you instinctively try to explain it away like the Mu'tazila, or does it bring you to your knees, acknowledging that your guidance is entirely in His hands? How would your life change if you truly believed you have no power to guide yourself even one step without His creating that act in you?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed guidance is only 'clarification.' Is that how you treat Allah's guidance in your life—as mere information to be accepted or rejected at will? Or do you desperately beg Him every day to create the act of guidance in your heart, knowing that without His direct intervention you will surely stray? Which belief drives you to pray more fervently?
?
If you hold that God only provides conditions for guidance but does not create the act of being guided, then what happens to your gratitude? Do you take credit for your own faith and obedience, subtly believing that you chose well because of your own wisdom? Or do you weep with the realization that every moment of belief is a gift created by Him alone? Examine your heart: are you more proud of your īmān or more thankful?

The Maturidi View on Divine Guidance and Misguidance
Nasafi states the Maturidi position on huda and idlal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that Allah creates the acts of guidance and misguidance in His servants, making both directly from Him.

Core Idea
Allah creates both guidance and misguidance because He creates all actions.

Imam Nasafi opens the discussion by stating the foundational Maturidi principle: since Allah creates all human actions, He also creates the acts of being guided and going astray. This sets the stage for the contrast with the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence once. Notice the logical flow: 'since it is established... so He is the one... so from Him came...'
This is a concise argument from a major premise.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that Allah creates both the act of being guided and the act of going astray. Underline the verbs 'خلق' and 'وجد'.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this differs from the common belief that guidance is from Allah but misguidance is from the servant. The Maturidis affirm both are from Allah.
This is a direct challenge to the Mu'tazila position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الهدى والإضلال
لما ثبت أن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد فكان هو الذي خلق فيهم فعل الاهتداء وفعل الضلال، فوجد منه الهدى والإضلال.
وعند المعتزلة لما لم يجز أن يخلق أفعالهم لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال، ويقولون ما أضيف إلى الله تعالى من الهداية فالمراد منه بيان طريق الدين لا تخليق فعل الاهتداء، وما أضيف إليه من الإزاغة والإضلال والخذلان والطبع بقوله : ( وَطَبَعَ اللهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ ) والمد بقوله: ﴿ وَيَمُدُّهُمْ فِي طُغْيَننهم يَعْمَهُونَ ) فلأن السبب الذي كان به منهم الأفعال كان من الله تعالى كالقدر والآلات، وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى مسببها ، وكذا في الهداية والعصمة قد تضاف على هذا الطريق، وقد يقولون بأنها تضاف إليه على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى شروطها التي توجد هي عندها إذ لولا المحنة والتكليف لما وجدت منهم هذه المعاني وإنما وجدت عند التكليف فتضاف إليه، وإن لم يكن منه فيها فعل كما يضاف إلى القرآن: فَزَادَهُمْ إِيمَنَا ) فَزَادَتْهُمْ رِجْسًا ( وإلى الدعاء أنه: (وَزَادَهُمْ ) تفورا : (( وإلى الأصنام : إِنَّهُنَّ أَضْلَلْنَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ النَّاسِ ) ( وقد يقولون: إنها تضاف إليه لأنها حملت عقيب أحوال أوجدها الله تعالى تصير تلك الأحوال حاملة لهم عليها من نحو الإنعام والإمهال مع علمهم بقدرته، والتقرر عندهم أن من عصى من له القدرة عليه لا يمهله بل يعالجه بالتعذيب والتنكيل، ثم الله تعالى لم يعاقبهم بل أمهلهم، ولم يكتف بالإمهال حتى أدر عليهم سوابغ نعمه وتركهم يتقلبون في آثار أفضاله ويترددون في أثناء منته وإنعامه، فظنوا أن ذلك لرضا الله تعالى بصنيعهم واستحسانه ما هم عليه من النحل والمذاهب حتى ادعوا الأمر فقالوا والله أمرنا بها، فصار ذلك مبعثةً لهم على التمسك بما هم عليه فأضيف إليه كما يضاف إلى الدنيا الغرور لاغترار الناس بها لما هي عليه من حالة الزهرة والبهجة، وربما يقولون ما يضاف إليه من الهداية فالمراد منه هداية المحسنين طريق الجنة في الآخرة، وهذا التأويل محكي عن الجبائي، ويقولون في معنى الإضلال المضاف إلى الله تعالى : إنه ليس بتخليق فعل الضلال بل هو تسميته إياه ضالاً يقال: أضله أي
سماه أي سماه ضالاً.
قال الكميت :
فطائفة قد أكفروني بحبكم وطائفة قالوا مسيء ومذنب
Discussion on guidance and misguidance.
Since it is established that Allah Almighty created the actions of servants, so He is the one who created in them the act of being guided and the act of going astray, so from Him came guidance and misguidance.
According to the Mu'tazila, since it is not permissible that He create their actions, from Him does not come the creation of the act of being guided nor the creation of the act of going astray. They say: What is attributed to Allah Almighty of guidance means the clarification of the path of religion, not the creation of the act of being guided. And what is attributed to Him of leading astray, misguidance, abandonment, and sealing, by His saying: 'And Allah has set a seal upon their hearts' (Quran 9:93) and prolonging by His saying: 'And He prolongs them in their transgression, wandering blindly' (Quran 2:15), then because the cause by which actions came from them was from Allah Almighty, such as capability and instruments. And actions may be attributed to their cause. Similarly, in guidance and protection, they may be attributed in this way. And they may say that they are attributed to Him according to the attribution of things to their conditions, which come to be at them, for if not for the trial and obligation, these meanings would not have come from them; rather they came at the time of obligation, so they are attributed to Him, even though there is no act from Him in them, just as it is attributed to the Quran: 'And it increased them in faith' (Quran 3:173) and 'It increased them in abomination' (Quran 9:125) and to the call that 'It increased them in aversion' (Quran 25:60) and to idols: 'Indeed, they have led astray many among the people' (Quran 14:36). And they may say that they are attributed to Him because they occurred following states that Allah Almighty brought into existence, and those states become bearers for them, such as favor and respite, along with their knowledge of His power. And it is established with them that whoever disobeys the one who has power over him does not give him respite but rather punishes and torments him. Then Allah Almighty did not punish them but gave them respite, and He did not suffice with respite until He bestowed upon them abundant favors and left them turning over in the traces of His bounty and moving about amidst His favor and kindness. So they thought that this was because of Allah's pleasure with their deed and His approval of what they were upon of sects and schools, until they claimed the matter and said: 'By Allah, He commanded us to do it.' So that became an incentive for them to cling to what they were upon, so it was attributed to Him just as the world is attributed to delusion because people are deluded by it due to its state of bloom and splendor. And perhaps they say that what is attributed to Him of guidance means guiding the righteous to the path of Paradise in the Hereafter, and this interpretation is related from al-Jubba'i. And they say concerning the meaning of misguidance attributed to Allah Almighty: It is not the creation of the act of going astray, but rather He calls him 'astray'; it is said: 'He led him astray' means He called him astray, i.e., He named him astray.
Al-Kumayt said: 'A faction has declared me disbeliever because of my love for you, and a faction said: sinner and guilty.'
Source pages p. 989

Commentary
This passage presents a comparative theological discussion on divine guidance (huda) and misguidance (idlal). The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by stating the Maturidi position: since Allah creates all actions of His servants, He creates both the act of being guided and the act of going astray, so guidance and misguidance are directly from Him. Then he expounds the Mu'tazila view, which denies that Allah creates human actions. For the Mu'tazila, the divine attributes of 'guidance' and 'misguidance' cannot refer to creation. They reinterpret these attributes in several ways: first, 'guidance' means showing the path of religion, not creating guidance. Second, terms like 'leading astray', 'abandonment', and 'sealing' are explained by causal attribution: the conditions or causes (such as capability) that allow actions to occur are from Allah, so actions are attributed to Him indirectly, just as effects are attributed to their causes. They also give examples from the Quran where things like the Quran itself, prayer, or idols are said to increase faith or lead astray, but the actual act is not from those objects. Another Mu'tazila explanation is that these attributes are applied because they occur after states Allah creates (like favor and respite) that make the person persist in disbelief, so the misguidance is attributed to Allah as a secondary effect, similar to how the world is called 'deceptive' because it deludes people. They also mention an interpretation from al-Jubba'i that 'guidance' in the Hereafter refers to leading believers to Paradise. Finally, they claim that 'leading astray' can mean simply naming someone as astray, not creating misguidance. The passage ends with a poetic quotation from al-Kumayt illustrating how different groups label others. This passage is a classic example of Maturidi-Mu'tazila polemics on human actions and divine attributes.

Key Terms
الهدى
الإضلال
خلق أفعال العباد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that guidance is only from Allah and misguidance is not from Him.
Correction: The Maturidis affirm that both are created by Allah, as stated in this passage.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does Nasafi say about the relationship between Allah and guidance/misguidance?
A) Allah only creates guidance, not misguidance.
B) Allah creates both the act of being guided and the act of going astray.
C) Allah only clarifies the path, not creates the acts.
D) Allah does not create any human actions.

Key Takeaway
For the Maturidis, guidance and misguidance are both created by Allah because He creates all actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah creates both guidance and misguidance, do you see your own faith as a gift from Him or as your own achievement? How does that change how you approach your next act of worship?
?
Are there areas of your life where you think you have 'gone astray'? Can you now see that even your going astray was created by Allah? How does that affect your repentance?
?
If guidance comes only from Allah, do you truly ask for it every time you pray? Commit today to saying 'Ihdina as-sirat al-mustaqeem' with the full awareness that only He can guide.

Mu'tazila Reinterpretations: Guidance as Clarification and Causal Attribution
Nasafi details Mu'tazila reinterpretations of guidance and misguidance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila reinterpret divine guidance as clarification of the path and misguidance as causal or conditional attribution to Allah.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila deny Allah creates actions; they reinterpret attributes as showing the way or as causal attribution.

Imam Nasafi now presents the Mu'tazila position. Since they reject that Allah creates human actions, they offer alternative interpretations for scriptural attributions of guidance and misguidance. This passage explains their view that 'guidance' means clarifying the religion, and that terms like 'leading astray' and 'sealing' are attributed to Allah either as the cause (e.g., capability and instruments) or as the condition (e.g., trial and obligation).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage identifying the two reinterpretations
First, note the Mu'tazila claim that guidance is 'بيان طريق الدين' not creation. Then find the causal explanation for misguidance terms like 'إزاغة' and 'طبع'.
2
Examine the causal model
The passage says that the cause (السبب) of actions, like capability and instruments, is from Allah, so actions are attributed to Him as the cause. This is similar to attributing effects to their causes.
They use examples like the Quran increasing faith.
3
Examine the conditional model
They also say misguidance is attributed to Allah because it occurs at the time of obligation and trial (المحنة والتكليف), which are conditions from Allah. So attribution is like that of a condition to its outcome.
Note the examples from Quran: the Quran increases belief or defilement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وعند المعتزلة لما لم يجز أن يخلق أفعالهم لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال، ويقولون ما أضيف إلى الله تعالى من الهداية فالمراد منه بيان طريق الدين لا تخليق فعل الاهتداء، وما أضيف إليه من الإزاغة والإضلال والخذلان والطبع بقوله : ( وَطَبَعَ اللهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ ) والمد بقوله: ﴿ وَيَمُدُّهُمْ فِي طُغْيَننهم يَعْمَهُونَ ) فلأن السبب الذي كان به منهم الأفعال كان من الله تعالى كالقدر والآلات، وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى مسببها ، وكذا في الهداية والعصمة قد تضاف على هذا الطريق، وقد يقولون بأنها تضاف إليه على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى شروطها التي توجد هي عندها إذ لولا المحنة والتكليف لما وجدت منهم هذه المعاني وإنما وجدت عند التكليف فتضاف إليه، وإن لم يكن منه فيها فعل كما يضاف إلى القرآن: فَزَادَهُمْ إِيمَنَا ) فَزَادَتْهُمْ رِجْسًا ( وإلى الدعاء أنه: (وَزَادَهُمْ ) تفورا : (( وإلى الأصنام : إِنَّهُنَّ أَضْلَلْنَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ النَّاسِ ) ( وقد يقولون: إنها تضاف إليه لأنها حملت عقيب أحوال أوجدها الله تعالى تصير تلك الأحوال حاملة لهم عليها من نحو الإنعام والإمهال مع علمهم بقدرته، والتقرر عندهم أن من عصى من له القدرة عليه لا يمهله بل يعالجه بالتعذيب والتنكيل، ثم الله تعالى لم يعاقبهم بل أمهلهم، ولم يكتف بالإمهال حتى أدر عليهم سوابغ نعمه وتركهم يتقلبون في آثار أفضاله ويترددون في أثناء منته وإنعامه، فظنوا أن ذلك لرضا الله تعالى بصنيعهم واستحسانه ما هم عليه من النحل والمذاهب حتى ادعوا الأمر فقالوا والله أمرنا بها، فصار ذلك مبعثةً لهم على التمسك بما هم عليه فأضيف إليه كما يضاف إلى الدنيا الغرور لاغترار الناس بها لما هي عليه من حالة الزهرة والبهجة، وربما يقولون ما يضاف إليه من الهداية فالمراد منه هداية المحسنين طريق الجنة في الآخرة، وهذا التأويل محكي عن الجبائي، ويقولون في معنى الإضلال المضاف إلى الله تعالى : إنه ليس بتخليق فعل الضلال بل هو تسميته إياه ضالاً يقال: أضله أي

?

?
If you were to adopt the Mu'tazila view that your sins are only attributed to Allah as conditions (like being tested), would you feel less personal accountability? The passage shows they still uphold obligation (taklīf) as the framework—does that challenge your own tendency to blame circumstances for your wrong choices?
?

Are you willing to ask Allah to make the Quran a means of guidance for you, not misguidance, and to hold yourself accountable for your response?

Mu'tazila Reinterpretations: State-Based Attribution and Naming
Nasafi relates Mu'tazila views on guidance/misguidance via states and naming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two further Mu'tazila explanations for attributing guidance and misguidance to Allah: first, that they occur after states created by Allah (like favor and respite) which delude the person, and second, that 'leading astray' can simply mean naming someone as astray.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila attribute misguidance to Allah as a consequence of His favors and respite, or as merely naming.

Imam Nasafi continues to expound the Mu'tazila positions. They offer yet another interpretation: misguidance is attributed to Allah because it follows certain states He creates, such as favor and respite, which unintentionally encourage persistence in disbelief. Additionally, they propose a simpler interpretation: 'leading astray' (idlāl) may mean nothing more than 'declaring someone astray' (tasmiyya).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about state-based attribution
Focus on the explanation that because Allah grants favors and respite, the disbelievers mistakenly think He approves of their actions, so this leads them to cling to their ways. Thus, misguidance is attributed to Allah indirectly.
2
Understand the analogy with the world's deception
The passage compares this to how the world is called 'deceptive' (ghurūr) because it deludes people, even though the world has no intent. Similarly, Allah's actions become a cause for misguidance.
3
Examine the naming interpretation
Finally, they say that 'idlāl' can mean simply calling someone astray, quoting the poet al-Kumayt to illustrate how different groups label each other.
This is a linguistic interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الهدى والإضلال
لما ثبت أن الله تعالى خلق أفعال العباد فكان هو الذي خلق فيهم فعل الاهتداء وفعل الضلال، فوجد منه الهدى والإضلال.
وعند المعتزلة لما لم يجز أن يخلق أفعالهم لم يوجد منه خلق فعل الاهتداء ولا خلق فعل الضلال، ويقولون ما أضيف إلى الله تعالى من الهداية فالمراد منه بيان طريق الدين لا تخليق فعل الاهتداء، وما أضيف إليه من الإزاغة والإضلال والخذلان والطبع بقوله : ( وَطَبَعَ اللهُ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ ) والمد بقوله: ﴿ وَيَمُدُّهُمْ فِي طُغْيَننهم يَعْمَهُونَ ) فلأن السبب الذي كان به منهم الأفعال كان من الله تعالى كالقدر والآلات، وقد تضاف الأفعال إلى مسببها ، وكذا في الهداية والعصمة قد تضاف على هذا الطريق، وقد يقولون بأنها تضاف إليه على حسب إضافة الأشياء إلى شروطها التي توجد هي عندها إذ لولا المحنة والتكليف لما وجدت منهم هذه المعاني وإنما وجدت عند التكليف فتضاف إليه، وإن لم يكن منه فيها فعل كما يضاف إلى القرآن: فَزَادَهُمْ إِيمَنَا ) فَزَادَتْهُمْ رِجْسًا ( وإلى الدعاء أنه: (وَزَادَهُمْ ) تفورا : (( وإلى الأصنام : إِنَّهُنَّ أَضْلَلْنَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ النَّاسِ ) ( وقد يقولون: إنها تضاف إليه لأنها حملت عقيب أحوال أوجدها الله تعالى تصير تلك الأحوال حاملة لهم عليها من نحو الإنعام والإمهال مع علمهم بقدرته، والتقرر عندهم أن من عصى من له القدرة عليه لا يمهله بل يعالجه بالتعذيب والتنكيل، ثم الله تعالى لم يعاقبهم بل أمهلهم، ولم يكتف بالإمهال حتى أدر عليهم سوابغ نعمه وتركهم يتقلبون في آثار أفضاله ويترددون في أثناء منته وإنعامه، فظنوا أن ذلك لرضا الله تعالى بصنيعهم واستحسانه ما هم عليه من النحل والمذاهب حتى ادعوا الأمر فقالوا والله أمرنا بها، فصار ذلك مبعثةً لهم على التمسك بما هم عليه فأضيف إليه كما يضاف إلى الدنيا الغرور لاغترار الناس بها لما هي عليه من حالة الزهرة والبهجة، وربما يقولون ما يضاف إليه من الهداية فالمراد منه هداية المحسنين طريق الجنة في الآخرة، وهذا التأويل محكي عن الجبائي، ويقولون في معنى الإضلال المضاف إلى الله تعالى : إنه ليس بتخليق فعل الضلال بل هو تسميته إياه ضالاً يقال: أضله أي
سماه أي سماه ضالاً.
قال الكميت :
فطائفة قد أكفروني بحبكم وطائفة قالوا مسيء ومذنب
Discussion on guidance and misguidance.
Since it is established that Allah Almighty created the actions of servants, so He is the one who created in them the act of being guided and the act of going astray, so from Him came guidance and misguidance.
According to the Mu'tazila, since it is not permissible that He create their actions, from Him does not come the creation of the act of being guided nor the creation of the act of going astray. They say: What is attributed to Allah Almighty of guidance means the clarification of the path of religion, not the creation of the act of being guided. And what is attributed to Him of leading astray, misguidance, abandonment, and sealing, by His saying: 'And Allah has set a seal upon their hearts' (Quran 9:93) and prolonging by His saying: 'And He prolongs them in their transgression, wandering blindly' (Quran 2:15), then because the cause by which actions came from them was from Allah Almighty, such as capability and instruments. And actions may be attributed to their cause. Similarly, in guidance and protection, they may be attributed in this way. And they may say that they are attributed to Him according to the attribution of things to their conditions, which come to be at them, for if not for the trial and obligation, these meanings would not have come from them; rather they came at the time of obligation, so they are attributed to Him, even though there is no act from Him in them, just as it is attributed to the Quran: 'And it increased them in faith' (Quran 3:173) and 'It increased them in abomination' (Quran 9:125) and to the call that 'It increased them in aversion' (Quran 25:60) and to idols: 'Indeed, they have led astray many among the people' (Quran 14:36). And they may say that they are attributed to Him because they occurred following states that Allah Almighty brought into existence, and those states become bearers for them, such as favor and respite, along with their knowledge of His power. And it is established with them that whoever disobeys the one who has power over him does not give him respite but rather punishes and torments him. Then Allah Almighty did not punish them but gave them respite, and He did not suffice with respite until He bestowed upon them abundant favors and left them turning over in the traces of His bounty and moving about amidst His favor and kindness. So they thought that this was because of Allah's pleasure with their deed and His approval of what they were upon of sects and schools, until they claimed the matter and said: 'By Allah, He commanded us to do it.' So that became an incentive for them to cling to what they were upon, so it was attributed to Him just as the world is attributed to delusion because people are deluded by it due to its state of bloom and splendor. And perhaps they say that what is attributed to Him of guidance means guiding the righteous to the path of Paradise in the Hereafter, and this interpretation is related from al-Jubba'i. And they say concerning the meaning of misguidance attributed to Allah Almighty: It is not the creation of the act of going astray, but rather He calls him 'astray'; it is said: 'He led him astray' means He called him astray, i.e., He named him astray.
Al-Kumayt said: 'A faction has declared me disbeliever because of my love for you, and a faction said: sinner and guilty.'
Source pages p. 989

Commentary
This passage presents a comparative theological discussion on divine guidance (huda) and misguidance (idlal). The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by stating the Maturidi position: since Allah creates all actions of His servants, He creates both the act of being guided and the act of going astray, so guidance and misguidance are directly from Him. Then he expounds the Mu'tazila view, which denies that Allah creates human actions. For the Mu'tazila, the divine attributes of 'guidance' and 'misguidance' cannot refer to creation. They reinterpret these attributes in several ways: first, 'guidance' means showing the path of religion, not creating guidance. Second, terms like 'leading astray', 'abandonment', and 'sealing' are explained by causal attribution: the conditions or causes (such as capability) that allow actions to occur are from Allah, so actions are attributed to Him indirectly, just as effects are attributed to their causes. They also give examples from the Quran where things like the Quran itself, prayer, or idols are said to increase faith or lead astray, but the actual act is not from those objects. Another Mu'tazila explanation is that these attributes are applied because they occur after states Allah creates (like favor and respite) that make the person persist in disbelief, so the misguidance is attributed to Allah as a secondary effect, similar to how the world is called 'deceptive' because it deludes people. They also mention an interpretation from al-Jubba'i that 'guidance' in the Hereafter refers to leading believers to Paradise. Finally, they claim that 'leading astray' can mean simply naming someone as astray, not creating misguidance. The passage ends with a poetic quotation from al-Kumayt illustrating how different groups label others. This passage is a classic example of Maturidi-Mu'tazila polemics on human actions and divine attributes.

Key Terms
الإنعام
الإمهال
الغرور
التسمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila deny any connection between Allah's actions and human misguidance.
Correction: They affirm a connection via states (favor/respite) that lead to misguidance, though not as direct creation.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, why do they attribute misguidance to Allah when they say it means 'calling someone astray'?
A) Because Allah creates the act of straying.
B) Because Allah merely names the person as astray, not create the act.
C) Because Allah gives the person a choice to stray.
D) Because Allah causes others to call him astray.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila offer state-based and linguistic interpretations to avoid attributing creation of misguidance to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When I receive blessings from Allah, do I ever assume He is pleased with my current state, even when I am disobeying Him? How can I guard against using His generosity as an excuse for my sins?
?
If I were the disbeliever who took Allah's respite as approval, what would my reaction be when I realize the truth on the Day of Judgment? What idle hopes have I allowed to delude me?
?
Al-Kumayt's poem shows how people label others as 'disbeliever' or 'sinner' based on their own criteria. Have I ever been quick to label someone as astray while ignoring my own faults? How can I apply the lesson that labeling belongs to Allah alone?
