Refutation of Guidance and Misguidance as Mere Naming
Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite interpretation of divine guidance and misguidance as mere naming or finding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite interpretation of 'guidance' and 'misguidance' as mere naming or finding is invalid according to Qur'anic verses that link these to Allah's will.

Core Idea
Guidance and misguidance are acts of Allah's will, not merely labels.

In this passage, Nasafi delivers the final blow to the Mu'tazilite attempt to strip divine guidance and misguidance of their true creative reality. By citing two Qur'anic verses that explicitly attach these acts to Allah's will (mashiah), he shows that mere naming or finding—which are not subject to will in the relevant sense—cannot be the intended meaning. This refutation reaffirms that guidance and misguidance are real acts of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the source passage carefully, noting the two Quranic verses and the logical conclusion.
The verses are key evidence.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
The passage refutes the claim that 'guidance' means just naming or finding someone misguided. Understand why this claim is problematic.
The claim reduces divine action to mere labeling.
3
Follow the logical refutation
Nasafi argues that these verses link guidance/misguidance to Allah's will, but naming/finding is not something that can be willed in a creative sense. Thus, the interpretation fails.
The key point: will is attached only to real actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال تعالى: فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ولا يهدي جميع الخلق إلى الجنة بل لو فعل ذلك لكان عندهم سفيها وقال تعالى: يُضِلُّ مَن يَشَاءُ وَيَهْدِي مَن يَشَاءُ وهذا لا يتصور في هداية طريق الجنة، وبهذا يبطل قولهم: إنه أراد به التسمية أو وجوده ضالاً، لأن ذلك مما لا يصح تعليقه بالمشيئة بل من وجد منه فعل الضلال.
And He Most High said: 'For if He willed, He would have guided you all together'—and He does not guide all creatures to Paradise; rather, if He did that, He would be foolish in their view. And He Most High said: 'He misguides whom He wills and guides whom He wills'—and this cannot be conceived concerning guidance to the path of Paradise. And by this is invalidated their saying: that He intended by it the naming or finding him misguided, because that is something whose attachment to will is not valid; rather, whoever is found to have performed the act of misguidance.
Source pages p. 992

Commentary
This passage delivers the final refutation of the Mu'tazilite claim that the divine acts of 'guidance' and 'misguidance' in the disputed verses merely mean 'calling someone guided/misguided' or 'finding someone such'. The author uses two additional Qur'anic verses: 'falaw shaa'a lahadakum ajma'in' (if He willed, He would have guided you all) and 'yudillu man yashaa'u wa yahdi man yashaa'u'. These verses explicitly attach guidance and misguidance to Allah's will (mashiah). If these terms meant only naming or finding, they could not be properly linked to Allah's will—since naming or finding is not something one 'wills' in the sense of creating. The act of misguidance, rather, is something that exists from the person. Therefore, the Mu'tazilite interpretation is invalid.

الوجود ضالاً
المشيئة

Correction: The passage shows that misguidance is directly tied to Allah's will, making it a real act, not just a label.

C) Because the Prophet said so

Key Takeaway
Guidance and misguidance are real acts of Allah's will, not merely names or findings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Mu'tazilites distorted the meaning of divine attributes to fit their reason. Are there any attributes of Allah that you struggle to accept or that you unconsciously reinterpret to make them more 'comfortable'? Will you commit to accepting them as they came in revelation, even if you do not fully comprehend them?

Refutation of Mu'tazila on Divine Will in Guidance
Nasafi refutes Mu'tazila interpretation of divine will in guidance verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila interpretation of divine will as a coercive will (mashī’at al-jabr) is invalid and how Imam Nasafi refutes it by showing that guidance and misguidance are attributed to God due to causes and conditions, not by direct coercion.

Core Idea
Divine guidance and misguidance are not by coercive will but by the creation of means and conditions.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi takes on the Mu'tazila claim that God's will in guidance and misguidance must be interpreted as a coercive will (mashī’at al-jabr). He argues that this interpretation leads to absurdities and is based on a misunderstanding of the verses. He demonstrates that the correct attribution of guidance and misguidance to Allah does not imply coercion but rather the provision of causes and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila position
Read the passage and identify the Mu'tazila claim that the will in guidance verses refers to coercion (jabr).
2
Follow Nasafi's refutation
Note how Nasafi compares their claim to saying Allah is called black from whomever He wills – an absurdity.
This shows the logical inconsistency in their interpretation.
3
Grasp the alternative explanation
Nasafi explains that guidance and misguidance are general for all people and are attributed to Allah due to the existence of causes or conditions, not by direct will.
This aligns with the Ash'ari/Maturidi position.
4
Conclude the argument
See how Nasafi affirms the verses support the correct position and invalidate the Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسمى ضالاً ضالاً، ويوجد من لم يوجد منه ذلك لا يسمى بذلك ولا يوجد كذلك. والقول به كالقول بأن الله تعالى يسمى أسود من شاء ويجد طويلاً من شاء وهذا فاسد، فكذا ما نحن فيه. ومما يحقق بطلان ذلك أنهم عرفوا بطلانهم حتى صرفوا الهداية المذكورة في هذه الآيات إلى ما صرفنا نحن، وفسروا المشيئة بمشيئة الجبر، وإنما يحتاج إلى صرف المشيئة إلى مشيئة الجبر عند كون الهداية ما بينا دون بيان الدين بدلائله والتسمية والوجود وإراء طريق الجنة في الآخرة، ثم قد بينا إبطال مشيئة الجبر وبهذه الآيات بطل إضافته ذلك إلى الله تعالى لوجود السبب منه أو الشرط أو الحالة الحاملة على ذلك، لأن هذه المعاني عامة في حق الناس كافة، فلم تكن هداية من اهتدى عندهم بمشيئته ولا ضلال من ضل فلم يكن لتعليق ذلك بالمشيئة معنى، فصح أن الأمر كما بينا، وأن الآيات كلها ناطقة بصحة ما ذهبنا إليه وبطلان ما ذهبت إليه المعتزلة، والله الموفق. ولكون هذه المسألة عين مسألة خلق أفعال العباد لم نشتغل بتطويلها، وإيراد ما أورده سلف الأمة من الدلائل السمعية والعقلية. ولو تلقت المعتزلة ما نطق به كتاب الله تعالى من إضافة الهداية والإضلال إليه بالقبول، وتعلموا من أهل الحق دفع ما تتمسك به الثنوية من الشبهة، وهو أن الحكيم لا يفعل القبيح لكان خيراً لهم من أن تلقنوا من الثنوية هذه الشبهة، وتشبثوا بالعرب يقولون: ضلل فلان فلاناً إذا سماه ضالاً، ولم نجدهم يقولون أضل فلان فلانا بهذا المعنى، فلما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ ﴾ لم يجز أن يكون معنى ذلك الاسم والحكم إذ لم يجز في العرب أن يقال أضل فلان فلانا إذ سماه ضالاً. نعوذ بها، وجعلوها قانونا لكتاب الله فصرفوا ما لا يوافقها إلى وجوه مستكرهة وأولوه تأويلات غير منقادة، فحرفوا الكلم عن مواضعها، وأزالوا النصوص عن مواردها وراموا تسوية حكم الربوبية على ما خالوه عقلاً، وظنوه علمًا بالله من الخذلان وهو المستعان وعليه التكلان - والله الموفق.
He is called misguided, misguided, and one from whom that is not found is not called that, nor is he found likewise. And saying it is like saying that Allah is called black from whomever He wills and is found tall from whomever He wills, and this is corrupt, so likewise what we are in. And among what verifies the corruption of that is that they recognized their own corruption until they diverted the guidance mentioned in these verses to what we have diverted, and they interpreted the will (mashī’a) as the will of coercion (jabr). And they only need to divert the will to the will of coercion when the guidance is as we explained, without the explanation of the religion by its proofs, and naming, and existence, and showing the path to Paradise in the Hereafter. Then we have already shown the invalidity of the will of coercion, and with these verses the attribution of that to Allah is invalidated due to the existence of the cause from Him, or the condition, or the state that necessitates it, because these meanings are general for all people. So guidance of the guided according to them was not by His will, nor misguidance of the misguided, so there was no meaning to attaching that to the will. So it is confirmed that the matter is as we explained, and that all the verses speak of the correctness of what we have held and the invalidity of what the Mu'tazila held. And Allah is the Granter of success. And since this issue is the same as the issue of the creation of the acts of servants, we did not engage in prolonging it, and citing what the predecessors of the nation brought of scriptural and rational proofs. And if the Mu'tazila had accepted what the Book of Allah speaks of regarding attributing guidance and misguidance to Him, and had learned from the people of truth to repel the doubt to which the Dualists cling, namely that the Wise does not do evil, it would have been better for them than to learn from the Dualists this doubt, and they clung to the Arabs saying: 'So-and-so made someone misguided (ḍallala) if he named him misguided,' and we do not find them saying 'so-and-so led someone astray (aḍalla)' with this meaning. So when Allah said: {And Allah leads the wrongdoers astray (yuḍillu)} it is not permissible for the meaning of that to be naming and judgment, since it is not permissible in Arabic to say 'so-and-so led someone astray (aḍalla)' when he named him misguided. We seek refuge from this. And they made it a canon for the Book of Allah, and diverted what did not conform to it to disliked meanings and interpreted it with forced interpretations, so they distorted words from their places, and removed texts from their contexts, and sought to equalize the rule of lordship according to what they fancied intellectually, and they thought it knowledge of Allah due to abandonment, and He is the sought for help and upon Him is reliance – and Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 993

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila interpretation of Qur'anic verses about guidance (hidāya) and misguidance (iḍlāl). The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by pointing out a linguistic inconsistency: someone is called 'misguided' only if misguidance is found in them; otherwise they are not called that. He then argues that the Mu'tazila, by interpreting God's will as a coercive will (mashī’at al-jabr), have twisted the clear meaning of the verses. The author explains that the Mu'tazila were forced to do so because they could not reconcile divine attribution of guidance and misguidance with their principle that God does not do evil. He then reiterates that the correct view is that God's guidance and misguidance are not by a coercive will but by His creation of the means or conditions, and that the verses themselves confirm the Ash'ari/Maturidi position. The author further notes that this issue is identical to the question of the creation of human actions, which he does not elaborate on here. He then criticizes the Mu'tazila for adopting a doubt from the Dualists (al-Thanawiyya) that the wise does not do evil, and for distorting the clear texts. He uses the linguistic argument that the Arabs use 'ḍallala' for naming someone misguided, not 'aḍalla', so the Qur'anic use of 'yuḍillu' in {وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ} does not mean creation of misguidance but rather judgment and naming. The passage ends with a condemnation of the Mu'tazila for their forced interpretations and a seeking of refuge in God.

Key Terms
هداية
إضلال
مشيئة الجبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, what does the Mu'tazila interpretation of the will (mashī’a) in guidance verses lead to?
A) A correct understanding
B) Absurdities like saying Allah is called black from whomever He wills
C) The affirmation of free will
D) The negation of divine attributes

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila interpretation of divine will as coercion is invalid because guidance and misguidance are attributed to Allah through causes and conditions, not direct will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experienced a moment of guidance, did you think it was purely your own doing or Allah's arrangement of circumstances? How does Nasafi’s explanation of causes and conditions reshape your gratitude and sense of responsibility?
?
Have you ever used the excuse that ‘Allah willed my sin’ to avoid accountability? If so, how does this passage challenge that excuse by distinguishing between direct coercion and causal attribution?
?
If guidance and misguidance are linked to Allah’s creation of means, what specific means (e.g., studying, companionship, dua) are you neglecting? What is one cause you will actively pursue today to strengthen your guidance?

The Linguistic Clarification: Misguidance as Judgment
Nasafi uses linguistic analysis to refute Mu'tazila on misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic argument distinguishing between 'ḍallala' and 'aḍalla' and how it refutes the Mu'tazila interpretation of the Qur'anic verse 'And Allah leads the wrongdoers astray'.

Core Idea
The Arabic language itself shows that divine misguidance is a judgment and naming, not an act of creating error.

Imam Nasafi now turns to a linguistic analysis to further refute the Mu'tazila. He points out that the Arabs use the word 'ḍallala' for naming someone misguided, but not 'aḍalla'. Therefore, when Allah says 'yuḍillu', it must be understood as a judgment, not as creation of misguidance. He then criticizes the Mu'tazila for adopting principles from the Dualists and distorting the clear texts.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic point
Read the passage and note the distinction between 'ḍallala' and 'aḍalla' as used by the Arabs.
The Arabs say 'ḍallala' for naming someone misguided, but do not use 'aḍalla' in that sense.
2
Apply to the Qur'an
See how this distinction applies to the verse {وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ} – it cannot mean creation of misguidance.
The verse uses the form 'yuḍillu', which is not used for naming, so it must be interpreted differently.
3
Recognize the Mu'tazila mistake
Nasafi criticizes them for adopting the Dualist doubt that the Wise does not do evil, and for forcing interpretations.
This shows their methodology is flawed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسمى ضالاً ضالاً، ويوجد من لم يوجد منه ذلك لا يسمى بذلك ولا يوجد كذلك. والقول به كالقول بأن الله تعالى يسمى أسود من شاء ويجد طويلاً من شاء وهذا فاسد، فكذا ما نحن فيه. ومما يحقق بطلان ذلك أنهم عرفوا بطلانهم حتى صرفوا الهداية المذكورة في هذه الآيات إلى ما صرفنا نحن، وفسروا المشيئة بمشيئة الجبر، وإنما يحتاج إلى صرف المشيئة إلى مشيئة الجبر عند كون الهداية ما بينا دون بيان الدين بدلائله والتسمية والوجود وإراء طريق الجنة في الآخرة، ثم قد بينا إبطال مشيئة الجبر وبهذه الآيات بطل إضافته ذلك إلى الله تعالى لوجود السبب منه أو الشرط أو الحالة الحاملة على ذلك، لأن هذه المعاني عامة في حق الناس كافة، فلم تكن هداية من اهتدى عندهم بمشيئته ولا ضلال من ضل فلم يكن لتعليق ذلك بالمشيئة معنى، فصح أن الأمر كما بينا، وأن الآيات كلها ناطقة بصحة ما ذهبنا إليه وبطلان ما ذهبت إليه المعتزلة، والله الموفق. ولكون هذه المسألة عين مسألة خلق أفعال العباد لم نشتغل بتطويلها، وإيراد ما أورده سلف الأمة من الدلائل السمعية والعقلية. ولو تلقت المعتزلة ما نطق به كتاب الله تعالى من إضافة الهداية والإضلال إليه بالقبول، وتعلموا من أهل الحق دفع ما تتمسك به الثنوية من الشبهة، وهو أن الحكيم لا يفعل القبيح لكان خيراً لهم من أن تلقنوا من الثنوية هذه الشبهة، وتشبثوا بالعرب يقولون: ضلل فلان فلاناً إذا سماه ضالاً، ولم نجدهم يقولون أضل فلان فلانا بهذا المعنى، فلما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ ﴾ لم يجز أن يكون معنى ذلك الاسم والحكم إذ لم يجز في العرب أن يقال أضل فلان فلانا إذ سماه ضالاً. نعوذ بها، وجعلوها قانونا لكتاب الله فصرفوا ما لا يوافقها إلى وجوه مستكرهة وأولوه تأويلات غير منقادة، فحرفوا الكلم عن مواضعها، وأزالوا النصوص عن مواردها وراموا تسوية حكم الربوبية على ما خالوه عقلاً، وظنوه علمًا بالله من الخذلان وهو المستعان وعليه التكلان - والله الموفق.
He is called misguided, misguided, and one from whom that is not found is not called that, nor is he found likewise. And saying it is like saying that Allah is called black from whomever He wills and is found tall from whomever He wills, and this is corrupt, so likewise what we are in. And among what verifies the corruption of that is that they recognized their own corruption until they diverted the guidance mentioned in these verses to what we have diverted, and they interpreted the will (mashī’a) as the will of coercion (jabr). And they only need to divert the will to the will of coercion when the guidance is as we explained, without the explanation of the religion by its proofs, and naming, and existence, and showing the path to Paradise in the Hereafter. Then we have already shown the invalidity of the will of coercion, and with these verses the attribution of that to Allah is invalidated due to the existence of the cause from Him, or the condition, or the state that necessitates it, because these meanings are general for all people. So guidance of the guided according to them was not by His will, nor misguidance of the misguided, so there was no meaning to attaching that to the will. So it is confirmed that the matter is as we explained, and that all the verses speak of the correctness of what we have held and the invalidity of what the Mu'tazila held. And Allah is the Granter of success. And since this issue is the same as the issue of the creation of the acts of servants, we did not engage in prolonging it, and citing what the predecessors of the nation brought of scriptural and rational proofs. And if the Mu'tazila had accepted what the Book of Allah speaks of regarding attributing guidance and misguidance to Him, and had learned from the people of truth to repel the doubt to which the Dualists cling, namely that the Wise does not do evil, it would have been better for them than to learn from the Dualists this doubt, and they clung to the Arabs saying: 'So-and-so made someone misguided (ḍallala) if he named him misguided,' and we do not find them saying 'so-and-so led someone astray (aḍalla)' with this meaning. So when Allah said: {And Allah leads the wrongdoers astray (yuḍillu)} it is not permissible for the meaning of that to be naming and judgment, since it is not permissible in Arabic to say 'so-and-so led someone astray (aḍalla)' when he named him misguided. We seek refuge from this. And they made it a canon for the Book of Allah, and diverted what did not conform to it to disliked meanings and interpreted it with forced interpretations, so they distorted words from their places, and removed texts from their contexts, and sought to equalize the rule of lordship according to what they fancied intellectually, and they thought it knowledge of Allah due to abandonment, and He is the sought for help and upon Him is reliance – and Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 993

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila interpretation of Qur'anic verses about guidance (hidāya) and misguidance (iḍlāl). The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by pointing out a linguistic inconsistency: someone is called 'misguided' only if misguidance is found in them; otherwise they are not called that. He then argues that the Mu'tazila, by interpreting God's will as a coercive will (mashī’at al-jabr), have twisted the clear meaning of the verses. The author explains that the Mu'tazila were forced to do so because they could not reconcile divine attribution of guidance and misguidance with their principle that God does not do evil. He then reiterates that the correct view is that God's guidance and misguidance are not by a coercive will but by His creation of the means or conditions, and that the verses themselves confirm the Ash'ari/Maturidi position. The author further notes that this issue is identical to the question of the creation of human actions, which he does not elaborate on here. He then criticizes the Mu'tazila for adopting a doubt from the Dualists (al-Thanawiyya) that the wise does not do evil, and for distorting the clear texts. He uses the linguistic argument that the Arabs use 'ḍallala' for naming someone misguided, not 'aḍalla', so the Qur'anic use of 'yuḍillu' in {وَيُضِلُّ اللهُ الظَّالِمِينَ} does not mean creation of misguidance but rather judgment and naming. The passage ends with a condemnation of the Mu'tazila for their forced interpretations and a seeking of refuge in God.

أضل

B) God names them misguided

The Arabic language shows that divine misguidance is a judgment, not creation of error, refuting the Mu'tazila interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Mu'tazila allowed their intellect to distort the clear meaning of the Quran. In what area of your life are you tempted to reinterpret Islamic teachings to fit your own sense of fairness? Will you submit to the apparent meaning of the text, even if it offends your reasoning?
?
This passage shows that misguidance is a judgment, not a creative act. Do you ever use divine decree as an excuse for your sins, thinking 'God made me do it'? How does realizing that misguidance is a judgment—not a causation—press you to take full responsibility for your actions today?

Ahl al-Haqq on Al-Aslah: No Obligation on Allah
Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Haqq position on lutf and al-aslah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Haqq affirm that Allah is not obligated to provide the most beneficial to His servants, and how they defend His justice and sovereignty.

Core Idea
Allah's mercy is a gift, not a debt; withholding benefit is not injustice.

Imam Nasafi begins by articulating the Sunni position on al-aslah, the doctrine of the most beneficial. The key distinction is between what Allah has the power to do and what He is obligated to do. This passage establishes that even if Allah withholds a certain 'gentleness' (luṭf) that would cause disbelievers to believe, He is not unjust or stingy; rather, His actions are always free from obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sunni argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage for the Ahl al-Haqq position once, then the translation. Notice the series of negations: Allah is not stingy, foolish, unjust, etc.
The argument uses a conditional structure: 'if He did X, He would be Y, but He is not Y because He didn't do X.'
2
Identify the key terms
Find and note the terms: الأصلح (al-aslah), لطف (luṭf), مصلحة (maslaha), واجب (wajib). Understand how each is used in the argument.
3
Analyze the logical structure
The passage makes several points: (1) Allah has lutf in His power, (2) He does not use it on disbelievers, (3) This does not imply negative attributes, (4) If He did use it, it would be grace, not obligation, (5) He may do what is not beneficial, (6) There is no limit to what He can do for good. List these points in order.
This is an enumerative argument; each point defends Allah's freedom from obligation.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Ask yourself: Why is it important that Allah is not obligated to give the most beneficial? How does this protect His sovereignty and mercy?
This distinguishes Sunni theology from Mu'tazila, who see obligation as necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤- الكلام في الأصلح:
قال أهل الحق أن في مقدور الله تعالى لطفا لو فعل ذلك بالكفار لأمنوا اختيارا، ولم يفعل بهم ذلك ولم يكن بأن لم يعطهم ذلك بخيلاً ولا سفيها ولا جائراً ولا ظالما ، ولو فعل ذلك لكان منعمًا متفضلاً لا مؤديًا ما عليه، وإنه إذا لم يعطهم ذلك فقد منعهم ما هو الأصلح لهم ، وكان إعطاؤه إياهم ذلك اللطف أصلح لهم من ترك الإعطاء، ويجوز أن يفعل بالعبد ما ليس بمصلحة له وإعطاء المصلحة ليس بواجب على الله تعالى ولا إعطاء الأصلح، وليس لما في مقدور الله تعالى مما به الصلاح للعبد غاية ليس ورائها ما هو أصلح مما فعل.
وزعم جمهور المعتزلة أن ليس في مقدور الله تعالى لطف لو فعل بالكفار لأمنوا، ولو كان ذلك في مقدوره ولم يفعل ولم يعطهم ذلك لكان سفيها بخيلاً جائراً ظالمًا مانعا حقا مستحقاً، وغاية ما يقدر الله تعالى عليه مما به صلاح الخلق واجب
4. Discourse on the most beneficial (al-aṣlaḥ): The People of Truth said that in Allah's power there is a gentleness (luṭf) that if He did it to the disbelievers they would believe willingly, yet He did not do it to them, and He was not, by not giving it to them, stingy nor foolish nor unjust nor oppressive. And if He did it, He would be beneficent and gracious, not one who fulfills an obligation. And when He does not give it to them, He has prevented them from what is most beneficial for them, and His giving them that gentleness would be more beneficial for them than refraining from giving. And it is permissible for Him to do to the servant what is not a benefit to him, and giving benefit is not obligatory upon Allah, nor giving the most beneficial. And there is no limit to what is in Allah's power of that which is good for the servant beyond which there is something more beneficial than what He did. And the majority of the Mu'tazila claimed that there is not in Allah's power a gentleness that if He did to the disbelievers they would believe. And if that were in His power and He did not do it and did not give it to them, He would be foolish, stingy, unjust, oppressive, preventing a right that is deserved. And the utmost that Allah is capable of with regard to what is good for creation is obligatory
Source pages p. 994

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of two opposing views on the doctrine of al-aṣlaḥ (the most beneficial). It begins by stating the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the Ash'ari/Maturidi school): Allah has in His power a certain 'gentleness' (luṭf) that, if He were to do it to the disbelievers, they would believe willingly. However, He does not do it, and that does not make Him stingy, foolish, unjust, or oppressive. If He did it, He would be a benefactor, not one fulfilling an obligation. Therefore, by not giving it, He has withheld what is most beneficial for them, but His giving it would have been more beneficial than not giving. However, it is permissible for Allah to do what is not beneficial for the servant, and giving benefit is not obligatory upon Him, nor is giving the most beneficial. Moreover, there is no limit to what Allah can do for the servant's good beyond which there is a more beneficial thing. The passage then presents the Mu'tazila view: they deny that Allah has such a gentleness in His power; they claim that if He had it and did not do it, He would be foolish, stingy, unjust, etc. They hold that Allah is obliged to do the utmost that He can for the good of creation. Note: The text ends abruptly with 'واجب', indicating the Mu'tazila argument continues on the next page.

Key Terms
الأصلح
لطف
مصلحة
واجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God is obligated to provide the most beneficial to all creation.
Correction: Ahl al-Haqq affirm that giving benefit is not obligatory upon Allah, nor is giving the most beneficial. He may do what is not in the servant's interest.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq, if Allah were to give the lutf to the disbelievers, what would be the nature of that act?
A) It would be fulfilling an obligation.
B) It would be an act of stinginess.
C) It would be an act of beneficence and grace.
D) It would be unjust.

Key Takeaway
Allah is never obligated to provide the most beneficial to His creatures; His actions are always free and just.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that Allah owes you a life of ease and comfort? When hardship comes, do you feel He has been unjust to you? Let this lesson shatter that illusion: He owes you nothing, and even withholding is perfect justice. Will you now submit to His decree without resentment?
?
If Allah does not give you what you consider 'most beneficial,' can you trust that He knows better? The passage says there is no limit to what He can do for your good—beyond any act, there is something more beneficial. Right now, in your current difficulty, will you affirm that His withholding is a mercy you cannot see?
?
The disbelievers were denied a lutf that would have made them believe. You, however, have been given faith. Do you treat this as a debt Allah owes you or as an undeserved grace? Examine your heart: have you taken your faith for granted, as if you earned it? Repent and thank Him for the lutf He has given you.

Mu'tazila on Al-Aslah: The Obligation Argument
Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila rejection of lutf and their claim of obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila argument that Allah is obliged to provide the most beneficial (al-aslah) to His creation, and why they deny the existence of lutf in Allah's power.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila argue God owes the best to creation; otherwise He is unjust.

Imam Nasafi now presents the opposing view of the Mu'tazila. They reject the Sunni position and argue that if Allah had the power to give a gentleness (luṭf) that would cause disbelievers to believe, and He did not use it, He would be foolish, stingy, unjust, and oppressive. Therefore, they must deny that such lutf exists in Allah's power. For them, Allah is obliged to do the utmost good for creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila claim
Read the Arabic passage for the Mu'tazila position and its translation. Notice the strong language: سفيها بخيلا جائرا ظالما (foolish, stingy, unjust, oppressive).
The argument is a conditional: if Allah had lutf and didn't give it, He would be those negative things.
2
Identify the core point of disagreement
The Mu'tazila assert that Allah must do the most beneficial; otherwise He would be unjust. Compare this with the Sunni view from the previous lesson.
This is a fundamental difference in the concept of divine justice.
3
Recognize the obligation (wujub) claim
The passage ends with the assertion that the utmost of what Allah can do for good is obligatory (واجب). This is the crux of the Mu'tazila position.
The text is cut off; the argument likely continues with consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وزعم جمهور المعتزلة أن ليس في مقدور الله تعالى لطف لو فعل بالكفار لأمنوا، ولو كان ذلك في مقدوره ولم يفعل ولم يعطهم ذلك لكان سفيها بخيلاً جائراً ظالمًا مانعا حقا مستحقاً، وغاية ما يقدر الله تعالى عليه مما به صلاح الخلق واجب
4. Discourse on the most beneficial (al-aṣlaḥ): The People of Truth said that in Allah's power there is a gentleness (luṭf) that if He did it to the disbelievers they would believe willingly, yet He did not do it to them, and He was not, by not giving it to them, stingy nor foolish nor unjust nor oppressive. And when He does not give it to them, He has prevented them from what is most beneficial for them, and His giving them that gentleness would be more beneficial for them than refraining from giving. And it is permissible for Him to do to the servant what is not a benefit to him, and giving benefit is not obligatory upon Allah, nor giving the most beneficial. And there is no limit to what is in Allah's power of that which is good for the servant beyond which there is something more beneficial than what He did. And the majority of the Mu'tazila claimed that there is not in Allah's power a gentleness that if He did to the disbelievers they would believe. And if that were in His power and He did not do it and did not give it to them, He would be foolish, stingy, unjust, oppressive, preventing a right that is deserved. And the utmost that Allah is capable of with regard to what is good for creation is obligatory
Source pages p. 994

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of two opposing views on the doctrine of al-aṣlaḥ (the most beneficial). It begins by stating the position of Ahl al-Haqq (the Ash'ari/Maturidi school): Allah has in His power a certain 'gentleness' (luṭf) that, if He were to do it to the disbelievers, they would believe willingly. Note: The text ends abruptly with 'واجب', indicating the Mu'tazila argument continues on the next page.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, what would be the consequence if Allah had a lutf in His power and did not give it?
A) He would be merciful.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argue that Allah is obliged to provide the most beneficial; otherwise He would be unjust, so they deny the existence of lutf in His power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a moment of disbelief or hardness in your heart, do you secretly think that Allah could force you to believe, but He doesn't, so you feel He is unjust? This lesson shows the Mu'tazila reached such a conclusion to protect God's justice. But what does this say about your own relationship with Him? Are you willing to accept that Allah's wisdom might not grant you the means that would compel your faith, not because He is unjust, but because He tests you? How will you respond to that test starting today?
?
The Mu'tazila argued that if Allah had the power to make all disbelievers believe and didn't, He would be preventing a due right. Do you ever feel that God owes you something—like guidance, ease, or understanding? Have you ever complained in your heart that He should have made it easier for you to obey? Today, repent from such thoughts and affirm that nothing is obligatory upon Allah except by His own mercy. Will you let go of your sense of entitlement and submit to His will?
?
This lesson confronts you with the fact that the Mu'tazila denied the existence of a specific grace (lutf) from Allah because they deemed it incompatible with His justice. In your life, have you ever rejected a blessing from Allah because you thought you deserved it, or because you felt it came with conditions? Examine your heart: Do you truly accept whatever Allah gives or withholds, trusting His perfect justice? Commit to thanking Him for every small grace, even if it doesn't fit your expectations.

The Sunni Position on al-Aslah: Allah is Not Obliged to Give the Most Beneficial
Al-Nasafi states the Sunni rejection of the obligation of al-Aslah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni (Ahl al-Haqq) position that Allah is not obligated to give the most beneficial (al-aslah) to His servants, and why withholding lutf does not imply injustice or deficiency.

Core Idea
Allah owes nothing to His creation; giving the most beneficial is grace, not duty.

The Mu'tazilites argued that Allah must do what is best for His creatures. Here, al-Nasafi presents the Sunni rebuttal: Allah has the power to grant a special grace that would lead disbelievers to faith, but He is not obliged to do so. To withhold it is not a flaw in His generosity or justice. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms: lutf, maslaha, al-aslah.
Passage is dense; don't worry about understanding every word immediately.
2
Identify the key claims
Find the statement that Allah has lutf that could cause faith, the denial that withholding implies deficiency, and the explicit negation of obligation.
Look for 'ليس بواجب' and 'لم يكن بخيلاً'.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Consider how these points directly counter the Mu'tazilite claim that al-aslah is obligatory on Allah.
This is the central point of the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤- الكلام في الأصلح: قال أهل الحق أن في مقدور الله تعالى لطفا لو فعل ذلك بالكفار لأمنوا اختيارا، ولم يفعل بهم ذلك ولم يكن بأن لم يعطهم ذلك بخيلاً ولا سفيها ولا جائراً ولا ظالما، ولو فعل ذلك لكان منعمًا متفضلاً لا مؤديًا ما عليه، وإنه إذا لم يعطهم ذلك فقد منعهم ما هو الأصلح لهم، وكان إعطاؤه إياهم ذلك اللطف أصلح لهم من ترك الإعطاء، ويجوز أن يفعل بالعبد ما ليس بمصلحة له وإعطاء المصلحة ليس بواجب على الله تعالى ولا إعطاء الأصلح، وليس لما في مقدور الله تعالى مما به الصلاح للعبد غاية ليس ورائها ما هو أصلح مما فعل.
4. Discussion on al-Aslah (the most beneficial): The people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq) said that in the power of Allah the Exalted there is a lutf (grace/favor) — if He did it to the disbelievers, they would believe by choice, but He did not do it to them; and His not giving that to them does not make Him stingy, nor foolish, nor unjust, nor oppressive. And if He did that, He would be benevolent and gracious, not one fulfilling an obligation upon Him. And if He does not give them that, then He has prevented them from what is most beneficial for them. And His giving them that lutf would be more beneficial for them than refraining from giving. And it is permissible that He does to the servant what is not beneficial for him. And giving benefit is not obligatory upon Allah the Exalted, nor giving the most beneficial. And there is no limit to what is within Allah's power that brings benefit to the servant, beyond which there is nothing more beneficial than what He does.
Source pages p. 994

Commentary
This passage defines the Sunni (Ahl al-Haqq) position on the issue of al-Aslah (the most beneficial). The author begins by stating the doctrine: Allah has the power to bestow a special grace (lutf) upon disbelievers that would cause them to believe voluntarily, but He does not do so. This does not imply any deficiency in Allah; He is not considered miserly, foolish, unjust, or oppressive for withholding it. If He did give it, He would be acting as a gracious benefactor, not as one fulfilling an obligation. Then the passage explains that although giving that lutf would be more beneficial for them, Allah is not obligated to give what is beneficial (maslaha) or what is most beneficial (al-aslah). Moreover, there is no finite limit to Allah's power such that beyond a certain point there is nothing more beneficial He could do; His power is infinite. This refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that Allah must do what is best for people.

Key Terms
الصلاح
الأصلح
اللطف
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is unjust if He withholds lutf from disbelievers, since He could cause them to believe.
Correction: Allah is not obliged to give lutf; withholding does not contradict His justice or generosity, as He is free from obligation to His creation.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq, what is the ruling on Allah giving the most beneficial (al-aslah) to His servants?
A) It is obligatory upon Allah.
B) It is permissible but not obligatory.
C) It is forbidden.
D) It is obligatory for believers only.

Key Takeaway
Allah is not obligated to give the most beneficial to His servants; His withholding of lutf is not injustice but an exercise of His will and wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is not obliged to give you what is most beneficial, are you still grateful for what He gives? How does this truth reshape your trust in His wisdom when you face hardship?
?
This passage says Allah could make disbelievers believe by giving lutf but chooses not to. How does this affect your view of divine mercy and justice? Do you still submit to His decree even when you don't understand why He withholds grace from some?
?
The lesson teaches that Allah's withholding is not injustice. When you feel He has withheld something you desperately wanted—a job, a spouse, health, guidance for a loved one—do you harbor resentment? What must you change in your heart to accept His decisions fully and without complaint?

Proof of Ahl al-Haqq from Quran and Existence
Nasafi enumerates the fourfold proof and expands on Quran and existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi uses Quranic verses and the fact of existence to prove that all actions, including disbelief and sins, are created by Allah.

Core Idea
God's power to guide all proves that actions are created by Him.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi outlines the proof of Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) regarding the creation of actions. He begins by listing four sources of proof, then focuses on two: the Quran and the evidence of existence. Through a careful reading of three verses and a logical argument from the reality of disbelief, he establishes that all actions are created by Allah—without falling into the error of compulsion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sources of proof
Read the opening line of the passage where Nasafi lists the four proofs: the Book of Allah, existence, consensus of religious communities, and rational proof. Notice that he only elaborates on the first two in this passage.
The other two proofs (consensus and reason) are mentioned but not detailed here.
2
Analyze the Quranic argument
Examine the three Quranic verses (32:13, 6:149, 10:99) that Nasafi cites. Understand the conditional logic: if God did not have the power to make everyone believe, these verses would be meaningless. Then read his refutation of the interpretation that these verses imply compulsion.
Pay attention to the phrase 'like the action of a lying pretender'—this is a strong rhetorical comparison.
3
Consider the argument from existence
Nasafi argues that since disbelief and sins undeniably exist, and we have previously proven (through auditory and rational proofs) that all actions are created by Allah, it follows that these evil actions are also created by Him. Reflect on how this argument builds on prior established principles.
The phrase 'they are harmed' (وهم يتضررون) indicates that servants suffer the consequences of their actions, but the creation of the action is from Allah.
4
Connect to the broader doctrine
Think about how this passage fits into the Maturidi position on qadar (divine decree). The proof avoids both the extremes of compulsion (jabr) and complete human independence (tafwīd), affirming that actions are created by Allah while humans acquire them.
This passage is a key part of the Maturidi response to the Qadariyya and Jabriyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل لأهل الحق في المسألة كتاب الله تعالى والوجود، وإجماع أهل الأديان والدليل العقلي. أما الكتاب فقول الله تعالى: وَلَوْ شِئْنَا لَآتَيْنَا كُلَّ نَفْسٍ هُدَاهَا وقوله تعالى: فَلَوْ شَاءَ لَهَدَاكُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ وقوله تعالى: وَلَوْ شَاءَ رَبُّكَ لَآمَنَ مَن فِي الْأَرْضِ كُلُّهُمْ جَمِيعًا، ولو لم يكن في مقدوره ما لو فعل بهم لآمنوا لم يكن لهذه الآيات فائدة سوى ادعاء قدرة ومشيئة ليستا له كفعل الكذوب المتصلف الذي يتحلى بما ليس فيه ما لا يحسن، وحملهم الآيات على مشيئة الجبر والقسر باطل على ما مر. وأما الوجود فإن الكفر والمعاصي قد وجدت، وإنا أثبتنا بالدلائل السمعية والعقلية التي لا مدفع لها ولا اعتراض عليها ولا ريب فيها لمن أنصف من نفسه ولم يكابر عقله أن أفعال العباد مخلوقة الله، وفيها الكفر والمعاصي، وهم يتضررون
And the proof for the people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq) in this matter is the Book of Allah, existence, the consensus of religious communities, and rational proof. As for the Book, it is the saying of Allah: 'And if We had willed, We could have given every soul its guidance,' and His saying: 'For if He willed, He could have guided you all,' and His saying: 'And if your Lord had willed, everyone on earth would have believed, all of them together.' If it were not within His power that if He did it they would believe, these verses would have no benefit except claiming a power and will that are not His, like the action of a lying pretender who adorns himself with what he does not possess. And their interpretation of the verses as referring to the will of compulsion and force is invalid, as has passed. As for existence: disbelief and sins have indeed existed, and we have proven through auditory and rational proofs that are undeniable, unobjectionable, and beyond doubt for one who is fair to himself and does not contradict his intellect, that the actions of servants are created by Allah, and among them are disbelief and sins, and they are harmed.
Source pages p. 998

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) regarding the creation of actions. It begins by listing four sources: the Quran (Kitab Allah), existence (al-wujud), consensus of religious communities (ijma' ahl al-adyan), and rational proof (al-dalil al-'aqli). The author then focuses on the Quranic proof, citing three verses (32:13, 6:149, 10:99) that state if God willed, He could have guided all. These verses imply that God has the power to make everyone believe, but He does not. If He did not have that power, the verses would be meaningless. The author refutes the claim that these verses refer to a will of compulsion, saying that is invalid as previously established. Next, the author argues from existence: disbelief and sins are observed in the world. The author asserts that it has been proven by auditory (sam'iyya) and rational ('aqliyya) proofs that all actions of servants are created by God, including disbelief and sins. The passage ends by noting that servants are harmed by these actions, implying that God's creation of them does not necessitate injustice, but rather is part of His wisdom.

Key Terms
أهل الحق (Ahl al-Haqq)
الوجود (al-wujud)
الإجماع (al-ijma')
الدليل العقلي (al-dalil al-'aqli)
الجبر (al-jabr)
القسر (al-qasr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verses about God willing guidance imply that God compels people to disbelief or faith.
Correction: Nasafi states that interpreting the verses as referring to a will of compulsion (jabr/qasr) is invalid. The verses affirm God's power, not compulsion.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would the Quranic verses about God willing guidance mean if God did not actually have the power to guide all?
A) They would still be valid as metaphorical
B) They would be a claim of power and will that God does not have
C) They would prove free will
D) They would be abrogated

Key Takeaway
The Quran and the existence of disbelief together demonstrate that God creates all actions, without implying compulsion, and that human acquisition of actions entails responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly feel that it was created by Allah, yet you are responsible for it? How does this reality affect the way you seek forgiveness?
?
If the Quranic verses about God's will to guide all are true, then He could have made you a perfect believer without effort. Why has He not done so, and what does that demand from you today?
?
The analogy of the lying pretender warns against claiming power one does not have. In your own life, where do you claim power or control that belongs only to Allah? How will you surrender it starting now?

God's Actions Are Wise, Not Necessarily Beneficial
Al-Nasafi refutes al-aslah with the disbeliever's preservation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi refutation of the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah and the proof from the disbeliever's continued existence.

Core Idea
God's wisdom transcends human benefit.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi tackles a central disagreement between Maturidis and Mu'tazilites: must God always act for the individual's best interest? He presents a concrete example—the disbeliever whom God keeps alive and gives intellect—to show that God's actions are governed by wisdom, not by the narrow principle of benefit. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two examples: the disbeliever and the apostate.
2
Identify the two examples
The passage gives two cases: God keeping a disbeliever alive and giving him intellect despite knowing he will disbelieve, and God preserving a Muslim who will later apostatize. Find each and see how they refute al-aslah.
3
Understand the refutation of al-aslah
Ask yourself: If God always did what is most beneficial for the individual, would He have done differently in these cases? The author argues yes, so God is not bound by al-aslah.
This is the core argument.
4
Grasp the concept of hikma (wisdom)
The author concludes that God's actions are wise (hikma), even if we don't perceive the benefit. Wisdom is broader than immediate benefit.
The Mu'tazilites' error is ignorance of the true nature of wisdom.
5
Reflect on the refutation of folly
The passage ends by rejecting the accusation that such actions are foolish—calling them so would be disbelief. Recognize why this is a strong theological stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ما هو أظهر من هذا وأدل أن الله تعالى فعل بالكافر ما لا صلاح له فيه بل له فيه مضرة ومفسدة، فإن الله تعالى أبقاه إلى وقت بلوغه وركب فيه العقل مع علمه أنه لا يؤمن بل يكفر ويعادي الله تعالى، ولا شك أن الله تعالى إذا علم أنه يكفر عند بلوغه واعتدال عقله لو أماته في حال صغره وعدم تمييزه أو لم يركب فيه العقل عند بلوغه حتى لو بلغ مجنونا غير مخاطب لكان ذلك أصلح له، وحيث لم يمته بل أبقاه وركب فيه العقل والتمييز حتى دخل في حد التكليف والامتحان مع علمه أنه يكفر دل أنه لم يفعل به ما له فيه صلاح، وكذا من عاش مدة على الإسلام ثم ارتد بعد ذلك - نعوذ بالله - ولو كان الله تعالى قبض روحه وتوفاه قبل ارتداده بساعة حتى ختم له بالإسلام ولم يستحق التعذيب في النار خالدًا مخلدًا كان أصلح له، وحيث لم يفعل بل أبقاه مع علمه أنه يرتد عن الإسلام وكان ذلك مضرة له لا صلاحًا فقد فعل ذلك وهو تعالى حكيم، دل أن ذلك كان حكمة، ووقعت المعتزلة فيما وقعت لجهلهم بحقيقة الحكمة، ثم بعد تقرير فعل الله تعالى ذلك دعوى من زعم أن ذلك سفه وليس بحكمة وصف منه الله تعالى بذلك وهو كفر، بل ظهر بفعله أنه حكمة وإن جهلت المعتزلة بجهة الحكمة إذ الجهل عليهم جائز وخروج فعل الله تعالى عن الحكمة ممتنع.
Then what is more apparent than this and more indicative is that God Almighty did to the disbeliever that which has no benefit for him, rather in it is harm and corruption. For God Almighty kept him alive until the time of his maturity and placed in him intellect with His knowledge that he will not believe but will disbelieve and oppose God Almighty. There is no doubt that if God Almighty knew that he would disbelieve upon his maturity and soundness of intellect, if He had caused him to die in his childhood and lack of discrimination, or had not placed in him intellect upon maturity so that he reached puberty insane and not obligated, that would have been more beneficial for him. Since He did not cause him to die but kept him alive and placed in him intellect and discrimination until he entered the boundary of obligation and trial with His knowledge that he will disbelieve, this indicates that He did not do for him what has benefit for him. Likewise, one who lived a period upon Islam then apostatized after that—we seek refuge in God—if God had taken his soul and caused him to die before his apostasy by an hour so that his end was sealed with Islam and he would not deserve eternal punishment in Hellfire, that would have been more beneficial for him. Since He did not do that but kept him alive with His knowledge that he will apostatize from Islam and that was harm for him, not benefit, yet He did that while He is Wise, this indicates that that was wisdom. The Mu'tazilites fell into what they fell into due to their ignorance of the reality of wisdom. Then after establishing God's action of this, the claim of one who claims that this is folly and not wisdom, and ascribing that to God Almighty—that is disbelief. Rather, it became apparent by His action that it is wisdom, even if the Mu'tazilites are ignorant of the aspect of wisdom, since ignorance is permissible regarding them, while the departure of God's action from wisdom is impossible.
Source pages p. 999

Commentary
This passage presents a theological proof against the Mu'tazilite doctrine of al-aslah (the most beneficial). The author, Imam al-Nasafi, argues that God's actions are not necessarily for the individual's benefit but are inherently wise (hikma). He begins by stating that what is more apparent is God's action towards the disbeliever: God keeps him alive and gives him intellect, knowing he will disbelieve. If God had let him die in childhood or without intellect, that would have been more beneficial for him. Since God does not do this, it shows God does not always act for the individual's benefit. Similarly, God preserves a Muslim who will later apostatize instead of taking his soul before apostasy, which would have been more beneficial. The author then notes that the Mu'tazilites fell into error due to ignorance of the true nature of wisdom. He refutes the claim that such actions are foolish, stating that to accuse God of folly is disbelief. Rather, God's actions are wise, and the Mu'tazilites' ignorance does not change that fact. The passage concludes that it is impossible for God's action to lack wisdom.

Key Terms
صلاح
أصلح
حكمة
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God must always do what is most beneficial for each individual (al-aslah).
Correction: God's actions are governed by wisdom, not necessarily by the individual's benefit. The preservation of disbelievers and apostates shows that God may act contrary to what would be individually beneficial.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does God's keeping the disbeliever alive indicate that He does not always act for the individual's benefit?
A) Because it would be more beneficial to kill the disbeliever in childhood.
B) Because God does not care about benefit.
C) Because the disbeliever's intellect is a punishment.
D) Because God's actions are arbitrary.

Key Takeaway
God's actions are always wise, even when they do not appear beneficial to the individual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When has God allowed something in your life that seemed harmful or purposeless? How does this lesson challenge you to trust His wisdom even when you cannot see the benefit?
?
The disbeliever in this lesson was given intellect and a chance, knowing he would reject. How does this affect the way you view those who reject faith? Are you willing to accept that God's wisdom in preserving them may be beyond your understanding?
?
If you truly believe that God's actions are always wise, what would change about your reaction to a trial or to the suffering of others? Be specific: what will you do differently the next time you face something that feels unfair?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Claim of al-Aslah through an Analogy
Author refutes Mu'tazilite claim of al-aslah using a father-son analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazilite argument that preserving a disbelieving child is beneficial is refuted by a rational analogy.

Core Idea
Certain harm cannot be outweighed by a mere possibility of benefit.

The Mu'tazilites argued that God's preservation of a child who will later disbelieve is beneficial because it exposes him to the possibility of high reward. This passage presents a powerful counter-analogy that exposes the irrationality of this claim. We will examine the analogy and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Read the first part of the passage that describes the Mu'tazilite assertion: keeping the child alive is al-aslah (most beneficial) because it allows for potential reward despite known future disbelief.
Notice that the Mu'tazilites consider exposure to reward as a benefit even when the outcome is certain harm.
2
Examine the father-son analogy
Read the analogy carefully. The father sends his son to trade despite knowing he will be killed or waste the money. Ask yourself: Is the father acting beneficially?
The analogy mirrors the Mu'tazilite logic: potential benefit vs. certain harm.
3
Understand the refutation
The author presents two possible answers to the rhetorical question. If the Mu'tazilite says the father is acting beneficially, he is foolish. If he says no, then the Mu'tazilite claim collapses. Recognize that the analogy forces a reductio ad absurdum.
This shows that the Mu'tazilite position is irrational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من جهل المعتزلة أنهم يزعمون أن إبقاء الطفل إلى أن يبلغ ويتركب العقل فيه عند البلوغ مع علمه أنه يكفر أصلح له، وكذا إبقاء من يعلم الله تعالى أنه يرتد لا محالة أصلح له من الإماتة قبل وقت الارتداد لما أنه تعالى ركب فيه العقل وأمره بالإيمان وهداه السبيل وبين حسن الإيمان وقبح الكفر، فكان إبقاؤه إياه مع هذه المعاني تعريضا له لأعلى المنزلتين وأسناهما، ولإحراز زيادة الثواب والتعريض لذلك مصلحة له، ومن المعقول الذي لا ريب فيه أن هذا الكلام لو تكلم به مبرسم أو هذى به مخبل لتعجب منه السامعون وضحك منه الحاضرون، ثم يقال له: لو أن رجلاً دفع مالاً إلى ولد له وأمره أن يذهب إلى بلده كذا ويتجر، وكان الأمر بحال لو وصل الابن إلى تلك البلدة وأتجر بها لوقعت له تجارات رابحة وحصلت له أموال نفيسة جمة، غير أن الأب يعلم يقينا أن ابنه لا يصل إلى تلك البلدة بل يقطع عليه الطريق ويغار على ما دفعه إليه من الأموال ويجز رقبته، أو يعلم يقينا أن ابنه لا يتجر بتلك الأموال بل يقامر بها ينفقها في ثمن الشراب وأجرة الزواني والقحاب ثم مع علمه بهذا يدفع إليه الأموال ويأمره بالذهاب ويحرضه على التجارة وينهاه عما يصده عنها ، أيكون هذا الرجل بهذا الصنيع والتعريض للتجارة الرابحة فاعلاً بهذا الولد ما هو الأصلح ومريدا لصلاحه وصلاح ماله مع علمه بما يؤول إليه عاقبة أمره؟ فإن قال: كان بذلك فاعلاً به الأصلح ومريدًا لصلاحه. نادى على نفسه بالحمق والمكابرة بل بعدم العقل ويسخر به كل من سمع ذلك منه، وإذا آل الأمر إلى ارتكاب مثل هذا المحال كان الإعراض عن مجادلته أصوب وتصوير عقيدته لعامة الناس ليعرفوا عناده أو غباوته أوجب، وإن قال : لم يكن بهذا التعريض فاعلاً به الأصلح ولا مريدًا
Then among the ignorance of the Mu'tazilites is that they claim that preserving the child until he reaches maturity and intellect is composed in him upon maturity, with His knowledge that he will disbelieve, is more beneficial for him. Likewise, preserving one whom God knows will apostate without fail is more beneficial for him than causing him to die before the time of apostasy, because He composed in him intellect and commanded him to believe and guided him to the way and explained the goodness of faith and the evil of disbelief. So His preserving him with these meanings is an exposure to the highest of the two stations and their loftiest, and for the attainment of increased reward, and exposure to that is a benefit for him. And it is from the rational, concerning which there is no doubt, that if this speech were uttered by a delirious person or babbled by a confused one, the listeners would wonder at it and mock him. Then it is said to him: If a man gave money to his son and ordered him to go to such-and-such a town and trade, and the matter was such that if the son reached that town and traded there, profitable trades would occur and he would obtain precious abundant wealth, but the father knows with certainty that his son will not reach that town but will be waylaid and robbed of the money given to him and his neck will be slit, or he knows with certainty that his son will not trade with that money but will gamble with it, spending it on the price of wine and the wages of prostitutes and harlots, then with his knowledge of this he gives him the money and orders him to go and urges him to trade and forbids him from what prevents him from it—would this man by this action and exposure to profitable trade be doing to this son what is most beneficial and intending his benefit and the benefit of his wealth, with his knowledge of what his end will be? If he says: He was by that doing for him what is most beneficial and intending his benefit—he proclaims against himself foolishness and obstinacy, rather lack of intellect, and everyone who hears that from him will mock him. When the matter leads to committing such an impossibility, then turning away from disputing him is more correct, and depicting his belief to the common people so that they may know his obstinacy or foolishness is more obligatory. And if he says: He was not by this exposure doing for him what is most beneficial nor intending
Source pages p. 999

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a specific Mu'tazilite argument. The author first states that it is ignorance on the part of the Mu'tazilites to claim that keeping the child alive until maturity (knowing he will disbelieve) is more beneficial. They argue that by giving him intellect, commanding faith, and explaining good and evil, God exposes him to the highest stations and increased reward, which is beneficial. The author then dismisses this as clearly irrational, saying that if a delirious or confused person uttered such speech, listeners would laugh. He then presents an analogy: a father gives his son money and orders him to travel to a certain town to trade, but the father knows with certainty that the son will be robbed and killed or will waste the money on sinful pleasures. Despite this, the father still sends him. The author asks: is this father doing what is most beneficial for his son? If one answers yes, he is foolish and obstinate, and will be mocked. If one answers no, then the Mu'tazilite claim collapses. The implication is that God, who knows the disbeliever's end, is not doing what is most beneficial by preserving him, thus refuting the Mu'tazilite position.

Key Terms
أصلح
تعريض
مصلحة
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That exposing someone to possible reward justifies causing certain harm.
Correction: The analogy shows that knowingly exposing someone to certain harm for a possible benefit is not beneficial, refuting the Mu'tazilite claim.

Checkpoint
The analogy of the father and son is used to refute which claim?
A) That God must always do what is most beneficial (al-aslah).
B) That keeping the child alive is beneficial because it exposes him to the possibility of high reward.
C) That God acts foolishly.
D) That the disbeliever is responsible for his own actions.

Key Takeaway
The analogy demonstrates that knowingly exposing someone to certain harm for a possible benefit is not beneficial, refuting the Mu'tazilite claim of al-aslah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on times you have knowingly continued in a sinful habit because you hoped for 'eventual' repentance or reward, does the father-son analogy in this lesson expose a self-deception? What would it mean to truly trust God's wisdom over your own rationalizations?
?
The Mu'tazilites argued that exposing a person to possible reward justifies certain harm. In your own spiritual life, can you identify a 'certain harm' (like a persistent sin) that you tolerate because you hope for some 'possible benefit' (like eventual good deeds)? How does this lesson command you to respond?
?
If you were a father and knew that sending your son on a journey would certainly lead to his destruction, you would not send him. Yet how often do you assume that God, who knows all ends, acts differently? What does this analogy teach about the character of God's actions towards His creation?

Divine Decree
beginner
6 min
God's Wisdom in Allowing Apostasy: Principle and Analogy
The author presents a principle and an analogy to refute a fatalistic objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that God's action of keeping alive those He knows will apostatize is actually more beneficial, and how he uses an analogy to force a contradiction in the opponent's view.

Core Idea
God's foreknowledge does not negate His wisdom; He gives every creature the maximum potential benefit.

This lesson examines the initial part of Imam al-Nasafi's refutation of a fatalistic objection. The author first establishes a principle: even for one known to apostatize, being kept alive is more beneficial because it exposes him to the possibility of faith and great reward. Then he presents a powerful analogy to show the absurdity of the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle statement
Read the first few lines where the author states that keeping alive the one known to apostatize is more beneficial (أصلح). Note the reasons given: intellect, guidance, exposure to high stations.
This principle is counterintuitive but central.
2
Analyze the analogy of the father and son
The author compares God's action to a father giving money to a son whom he knows will squander it. Understand how this analogy illustrates the absurdity of acting against knowledge of harm.
The analogy is meant to show that the opponent's view would mean God acts foolishly.
3
Follow the two possible responses
The author presents the opponent with two choices: either say the father did what is beneficial (absurd) or not (which invalidates the opponent's own argument). See how this forces a contradiction.
This is a classic dialectical move.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من يعلم الله تعالى أنه يرتد لا محالة أصلح له من الإماتة قبل وقت الارتداد لما أنه تعالى ركب فيه العقل وأمره بالإيمان وهداه السبيل وبين حسن الإيمان وقبح الكفر، فكان إبقاؤه إياه مع هذه المعاني تعريضا له لأعلى المنزلتين وأسناهما، ولإحراز زيادة الثواب والتعريض لذلك مصلحة له، ومن المعقول الذي لا ريب فيه أن هذا الكلام لو تكلم به مبرسم أو هذى به مخبل لتعجب منه السامعون وضحك منه الحاضرون، ثم يقال له: لو أن رجلاً دفع مالاً إلى ولد له وأمره أن يذهب إلى بلده كذا ويتجر، وكان الأمر بحال لو وصل الابن إلى تلك البلدة وأتجر بها لوقعت له تجارات رابحة وحصلت له أموال نفيسة جمة، غير أن الأب يعلم يقينا أن ابنه لا يصل إلى تلك البلدة بل يقطع عليه الطريق ويغار على ما دفع إليه من الأموال ويجز رقبته، أو يعلم يقينا أن ابنه لا يتجر بتلك الأموال بل يقامر بها ينفقها في ثمن الشراب وأجرة الزواني والقحاب ثم مع علمه بهذا يدفع إليه الأموال ويأمره بالذهاب ويحرضه على التجارة وينهاه عما يصده عنها، أيكون هذا الرجل بهذا الصنيع والتعريض للتجارة الرابحة فاعلاً بهذا الولد ما هو الأصلح ومريدا لصلاحه وصلاح ماله مع علمه بما يؤول إليه عاقبة أمره؟ فإن قال: كان بذلك فاعلاً به الأصلح ومريدًا لصلاحه. نادى على نفسه بالحمق والمكابرة بل بعدم العقل ويسخر به كل من سمع ذلك منه، وإذا آل الأمر إلى ارتكاب مثل هذا المحال كان الإعراض عن مجادلته أصوب وتصوير عقيدته لعامة الناس ليعرفوا عناده أو غباوته أوجب، وإن قال : لم يكن بهذا التعريض فاعلاً به الأصلح ولا مريدًا لصلاحه. فقد أبطل كلامه ولزمته الحجة. ثم الذي يقطع شغبه أنا نقول له: هل رأيت طفلاً مات؟ فلا بد من بلى. قيل وهل رأيت رجلاً بلغ وآمن وختم له به؟ فلا بد من بلى قيل: وهل رأيت أو سمعت إنسانًا ارتد عن الإسلام بعد ما بلغ عاقلاً؟ فلا بد من بلى. قيل: فلو أن الله تعالى أثاب البالغ الذي ختم له بالإيمان ورفع له الدرجات في الجنة وأوصل إليه على ما سبق منه من الطاعات ما لا عين رأت ولا أذن سمعت من أنواع النعم الأبدية فعاين ذلك الطفل المتوفى في حال صغره قصور ثوابه ومنزلته عن ذلك فناجي ربه :وقال يا رب لم توفيتني في حال صغري وانعدام عقلي، ولم تبقني مع تركب العقل في إلى وقت البلوغ بل لم تمهلني مع ذلك إلى وقت الشيب لأكتسب من الطاعات ما أنال عليها من الثواب ما يوازي ثواب هذا، فماذا يقول له الله تعالى؟ فإن قال : يقول له أن الأصلح لك كان أن أميتك وأتوفاك في حال الصغر وانعدام العقل لأني علمت بسابق علمي أنك لو بلغت عاقلاً لكفرت واستوجبت التخليد في النار فتوفيتك في حال الصغر لئلا تبقى في النار خالدًا مخلدًا، قيل له فلو سمع الكبير الذي مات على الكفر وارتد بعد ما زجى أكثر عمره على الإيمان فناجي فقال : يا رب لما كنت تعلم أني أكفر بعد البلوغ أو أرتد لما لم تمتني في حال صغري كما أمت هذا لئلا أبقى خالدًا مخلدًا في النار؟ فماذا يجيبه الله تعالى؟ فإن قال : يجيبه أن ذلك كان أصلح لك لأني عرضتك لأعلى المنزلتين، قيل : فيقول الصغير : إذا كان ذلك أصلح له فلم لم تفعل بي ذلك فلم يبق إلا الانقطاع والقصيرة عن الطويلة أن إماتة الصغير وإن كان أصلح له فلماذا أبقى الذي علم أنه يكفر ؟ وإن كان الإبقاء أصلح لما فيه من التعريض فلماذا أمات هذا الصغير ؟ وهذا مما لا انفصال لهم إلى أن يبيض الفار ويشيب الغراب، فاعترض
For the one whom God Almighty knows will inevitably apostatize, it is more beneficial to him than causing death before the time of apostasy, because God Almighty implanted in him intellect, commanded him to faith, guided him to the path, and made clear the goodness of faith and the evil of disbelief. Thus, keeping him alive with these meanings is an exposure to the highest and most sublime of the two stations, and to obtain additional reward, and exposure to that is a benefit for him. It is rationally undeniable that if this speech were uttered by a delirious person or babbled by a madman, listeners would marvel at him and those present would laugh at him. Then it is said to him: If a man gave money to his son and commanded him to go to such-and-such a town and trade, and the situation was such that if the son reached that town and traded he would gain profitable trade and acquire many precious possessions, but the father knows for sure that his son will not reach that town; rather, the road will be blocked for him, he will be robbed of the money given to him, and his throat will be cut; or he knows for sure that his son will not trade with that money, but will gamble with it, spending it on wine and the wages of adulterers and prostitutes; then, despite this knowledge, he gives him the money, commands him to go, urges him to trade, and forbids him from what would prevent him from it—is this man, by this action and exposure to profitable trade, doing what is most beneficial to this son and desiring his welfare and the welfare of his property, while knowing the ultimate outcome of his affair? If he says: By that he was doing what is most beneficial to him and desiring his welfare, he declares himself foolish and stubborn, indeed lacking intellect, and everyone who hears that from him will mock him. And when matters reach the point of committing such an absurdity, it is more appropriate to refrain from arguing with him and more necessary to depict his belief to the common people so that they may know his stubbornness or stupidity. And if he says: By this exposure he was not doing what is most beneficial to him nor desiring his welfare, then he has invalidated his statement and the argument is binding against him. Then what cuts off his disturbance is that we say to him: Have you seen a child who died? He must say yes. He is asked: Have you seen a man who reached adulthood, believed, and ended with (Iman)? He must say yes. He is asked: Have you seen or heard of a person who apostatized from Islam after reaching adulthood and being rational? He must say yes. He is asked: So if God Almighty rewarded the adult who ended with faith, raised his ranks in Paradise, and gave him, for the acts of obedience that preceded from him, what no eye has seen nor ear has heard of eternal blessings, and that child who died in his infancy saw the deficiency of his reward and station compared to that, and he privately called his Lord saying: O Lord, why did You cause me to die in my infancy and lack of intellect, and not keep me alive with the combination of intellect until the age of puberty, and not even grant me respite to old age so that I could earn from acts of obedience a reward comparable to the reward of this one? Then what would God Almighty say to him? If he says: He says to him that the most beneficial for you was to cause you to die and take you in infancy and lack of intellect, because I knew by My prior knowledge that if you reached adulthood with intellect you would disbelieve and merit eternal dwelling in the Fire, so I caused you to die in infancy so that you would not remain in the Fire eternally dwelling forever. It is said to him: If the adult who died in disbelief and apostatized after spending most of his life in faith heard this and privately called saying: O Lord, since You knew I would disbelieve after puberty or apostatize, why did You not cause me to die in my infancy as You caused this one to die, so that I would not remain in the Fire eternally dwelling forever? Then what would God Almighty answer him? If he says: He would answer him that that was more beneficial for you because I exposed you to the highest of the two stations. He says: Then the child says: If that is more beneficial for him, why did You not do that for me? So nothing remains but being cut off, and the short is (stuck) on the long: that causing the child to die, even if it is more beneficial for him, why did He keep alive the one whom He knew would disbelieve? And if keeping alive is more beneficial because of the exposure in it, why did He cause this child to die? And this is something from which they have no escape until the mouse turns white and the crow turns grey. Then he interrupted.
Source pages p. 1000

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection regarding God's wisdom in allowing people whom He knows will apostatize to reach adulthood. The author argues that God's actions are always for the creature's ultimate benefit, even when human reason cannot fully grasp it. He first states a principle: for one known to apostatize, keeping him alive is more beneficial than causing death before apostasy, because God has given him intellect, commanded faith, and guided him, thereby exposing him to the highest reward. This exposure itself is a benefit. The author then mocks the absurdity of the opposite view by comparing it to a delirious person's speech. Next, he presents an analogy: a father who gives money to his son for trade, knowing the son will lose it all—such a father is not acting for the son's benefit. This illustrates that if God acted similarly, it would be irrational. The opponent is forced into a contradiction: either he admits God does what is beneficial (which the analogy contradicts) or he denies it, invalidating his position. Then the author introduces a dialogue: a child who died young complains that he was not given the chance to earn greater rewards like an adult believer. God would answer that dying early was more beneficial because He knew the child would otherwise disbelieve and be punished eternally. But then an adult who disbelieved would counter-argue that God should have let him die young as well. The opponent cannot consistently answer both. Thus the author concludes that the opponent's position is insurmountably flawed.

ارتداد
إماتة
تعريض
مصلحة
أصلح
المنزلتين
الثواب
العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's foreknowledge of unbelief makes Him unjust in allowing the person to reach adulthood.
Correction: The author argues it is actually more beneficial because it grants the person the possibility of great reward, and God's action is not unjust but full of wisdom.

Checkpoint
According to the author's argument in this part, why is keeping alive the one known to apostatize more beneficial than causing death before apostasy?
A) Because the person might repent
B) Because it exposes him to the highest station and potential reward through God's guidance and intellect
C) Because God does not know the future
D) Because the person will definitely believe

Key Takeaway
God's actions are always for the creature's ultimate benefit, even if human intellect cannot fully grasp it; foreknowledge does not negate wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a sin you repeatedly commit, knowing it displeases Allah. Have you ever felt that Allah's guidance and commands for you are pointless because 'you'll never change'? How does this lesson's teaching that even the exposure to faith is a benefit (regardless of your track record) challenge that despair? Will you today accept that every moment you are alive is an opportunity for reward, not a waste?
?
If you were the son in the analogy, would you resent your father for giving you the money and command to trade, knowing you would fail? Or would you see the gift of opportunity as a mercy? Now apply this to Allah: are you grateful for the chances He gives you, even when you stumble? Or do you secretly accuse Him of being unfair? Lay bare your heart before Him now.
?
When you see someone who has left Islam or lives in sin, do you think Allah's wisdom in giving them life was wasted? This lesson says even their exposure to faith was a benefit for them, though they rejected it. How does this change the way you look at them? Will you stop judging and instead see the mercy in God's gift of existence, even for those who misuse it?
